“Why don’t you just take the day off?” Rio says, eyeing Jen, who looks like she’s one sneeze away from collapsing. “Tell Agatha you’re sick, and have her call me for anything she needs.” It’s not like Rio really misses hearing Agatha’s voice, but she’s genuinely worried about Jen.

Jen seems to consider it but then shakes her head. “No. She’d kill me if I took a day off. She specifically told me to keep things running here while she’s gone. So, I’m not sick. I’m fine. Absolutely fine.”

Turns out Jen hasn’t been fine at all when she calls Rio around 6 pm on a Saturday, saying she’s at the hospital after passing out while grabbing coffee at a café below her apartment.

“Jesus, for real? What hospital are you at? Do you have someone with you? Do you want me to come?” Rio says into the phone, already pushing herself up from the couch.

“Charmed, but no. I’m fine now. Nurses are taking care of me,” Jen says from the other line. “And trust me, I wouldn’t be calling if what I’m about to tell you wasn’t important. Look, this is kind of embarrassing, but I need you to do me a favor.”

“Okay, just tell me what’s up,” Rio says, not sure what to expect next.

“I know it’s a Saturday, but I need you to go to the office right now and grab something for me. It’s a black envelope in one of my drawers. Should be easy to find. I keep my drawers pretty organized, and it’s probably the only envelope with a label on it. So don’t touch anything else,” Jen says, then starts coughing, making Rio pull the phone away from her ear at how rough she sounds.

“Are you sure you’re okay? Is there anyone with you besides the nurses? I can send a friend over if you want someone to keep an eye on you.”

Jen coughs again. “No, I don’t need your friend, and I don’t need a babysitter. What I do need is for that envelope to get to Agatha in an hour, or I’m dead.”

“Wait, what? What do you mean get it to Agatha?”

“Rio, you’re delivering the envelope to Jersey. Were you even listening?” Jen snaps and Rio instantly freezes. “There’s a car waiting at the office,” Jen continues over the phone. “You have to drive it yourself because none of the company drivers are available on a damn weekend. Now I have to go. They’re poking me with something again, taking more blood or whatever. You’ve got one hour, Rio, so move!”

The call dies before she can even process everything. “Seriously?” she mutters, staring down at herself in boxers and a loose tank. She practically bolts to her room, yanks on the first pair of black jeans she can find, grabs a white button-up, and throws on her oversized Colorado hoodie, because of course it’s starting to get fucking cold outside.

She catches her reflection in the mirror and groans. 

If she’d known she’d be driving to freaking New Jersey to see Agatha today, she might’ve at least tried to look halfway decent. But it’s too late to dig through her closet now, so she throws on her shoes, grabs her bag, storms outside, and immediately flags down a cab.

It takes about fifteen minutes before she reaches the office, grabs the envelope from one of Jen’s drawers, skips the elevator, races down the stairs, jumps into one of the company cars in the basement, and pulls out into traffic. 

More than an hour, one gas stop, and a flat tire later, Rio’s nerves are fraying by the mile. Her eyes keep darting between the road and the blue arrow inching closer to the drop-off point Jen had texted her.

By the time she finally turns into the gated neighborhood on the lakefront fringe of Morris County, the sky has already faded into a deep blue. She rolls to a stop in front of a massive mansion of white stone and glass, with clean lines and perfectly groomed hedges. The driveway alone could host a block party. And there’s a fountain. Of course there’s a fountain.

Rio puts the car in park and just stares. “Jesus Christ,” she mumbles, eyes wide at the house.

Suddenly, she feels entirely out of place. Of all the days she could have shown up here, of course it had to be the actual wedding day. And she appears like she just crawled out of a subway grate, even if she technically showered this morning and is squeaky clean.

She immediately tugs off her hoodie, chuntering a curse under her breath, and tries to smooth out the creases on her button-up. It’s a lost cause, but she does it anyway. Then she grabs the envelope from the passenger seat, braces herself, and steps out of the car.

The house is flanked by rows of shiny, expensive-looking cars. From the front lawn, she can see a giant white tent out back, with music and chatter spilling over the hedges. 

She heads toward the noise, clutching the envelope she’s meant to deliver. The backyard is almost crowded with people talking too loudly, laughing too hard, and already tipsy on overpriced champagne. A waiter with a tray of tiny hors d’oeuvres nearly bumps into her as he maneuvers through the crowd.

“Oh, excuse me, dear,” an older woman with diamonds stacked on her wrist stops Rio, holding out her empty glass. “Would you mind getting me one of those cucumber cocktails? I’m parched, and I can’t seem to find any help around.” 

Rio blinks. “I, uh, I don’t—”

The woman’s polite smile falters at her mumbling, the corners of her eyes wrinkling as she gives Rio a meticulous look from head to toe. Rio follows the woman’s gaze to her own black jeans, untucked button-up, and scuffed sneakers. Then she looks around at the waitstaff gliding past them in spotless white shirts and matching black trousers.

But before she can even try to explain, someone behind them speaks up. 

“What seems to be the problem here?”

Rio turns around and immediately stiffens at the sight of Evanora Harkness standing in front of her, posture impeccable, dressed in an elegant pale blue dress that undoubtedly costs more than Rio’s monthly rent. The older woman doesn’t recognize her right away and gives her that distant, courteous look that wealthy people save for strangers below their tax bracket.

Then, just as she feels herself gradually sinking beneath Evanora’s trenchant stare, a familiar voice pulls her back to the surface just in time.

“Rio?” 

Agatha walks over to them quickly, looking like she’s just seen a ghost. Dressed in a cowl-necked, uranian blue satin dress, she looks every bit the composed socialite, except for how her eyes somehow dart anxiously between Rio and her mother.

“What are you doing here?”

Rio regards her for a second, realizing it’s the longest she’s gone without seeing Agatha. She’s almost breathless just looking at her. Dark brown hair swept into a loose bun, soft waves framing her face. But it’s her blue eyes that hold Rio still. Wide. Surprised. Maybe even a little alarmed. Agatha clearly wasn’t expecting to see her here. That much is obvious.

Rio opens her mouth. “Jen sent me. She said you needed this—” 

But before she can finish, Agatha grabs her firmly by the arm.

“Excuse us, Mother. Mrs. Crawley,” she says, wearing the tightest smile imaginable. “I need to speak with my assistant.” Then she turns on her heel and pulls Rio away from the gathering and out to the front lawn before either woman can get a word in.

“Why are you here? Where the hell is Jen?” Agatha scowls, letting go of Rio like she just realized she was holding something she hadn’t meant to. Rio merely blinks at her, clearly taken aback by the cold reception. Agatha didn’t even bother to ask how the trip was.

“Jen’s at the hospital. She’s been working sick since Monday and passed out earlier, but she says she’s fine now. Anyway, she said you needed this, so I drove it over.” She hands Agatha the envelope.

“You drove all the way here? By yourself?”

“There was no one available to take me.”

Agatha takes the envelope, frowning as she looks off to the side. 

“Jen shouldn’t have sent you,” she murmurs, almost to herself, but Rio still hears it.

“What’s that supposed to mean?”

Instead of answering, Agatha holds out her hand. “Give me your phone.”

Rio hesitates. “Why?”

“Just give it to me.”

She hands it over, and Agatha types something in before giving it back. “That’s the address of the hotel I’m staying at. Go there, give them my name, and they’ll take care of everything. You’ll get a room across from mine. Stay there tonight and head back tomorrow.”

“But it’s still early. I can make the drive—”

“No,” Agatha says firmly. “It’s late. I’m not letting you drive back alone.”

Rio tries her best not to blush in front of her boss, but fails the moment she feels her cheeks start to warm. The butterflies in her stomach aren’t helping either. 

“Wait,” she realizes, frowning a little. “You’re staying at a hotel? Not here?” She jerks her thumb at the massive house behind them. The place probably has ten bedrooms, at least, Rio thinks.

Agatha scoffs. “You really think I’d stay in that house for a whole week? I’d rather sleep on the street.”

Finally, she turns back to Rio, and for a second, she could swear Agatha’s blue eyes are saying she misses her too. Or maybe that’s just the whiplash from the sudden trip talking, and she’s just imagining it.

“Now go,” Agatha adds, brushing down her dress. “I still have to scream at the newlyweds to hurry up and consummate their marriage right in front of this whole Catholic freak show so we can all finally be put out of our misery.”

Rio snorts, shaking her head as Agatha starts walking away. But something tugs at her, something she hasn’t said yet. “Wait. Agatha.”

Agatha’s halfway across the lawn when she turns around, already looking annoyed again. “What?”

Rio takes a deep breath and stuffs her hands in her pockets so Agatha doesn’t see they’re slightly shaking. Then she says what’s been on her mind since the moment she laid eyes on her earlier.

“You look really pretty.”

Agatha sort of freezes, then lifts an eyebrow. “Pretty?” she repeats, like it’s an understatement.

Rio smiles shyly and gives a small shake of her head. 

“Beautiful,” she corrects herself. “You look really beautiful.”

Agatha’s lips part slightly. Her cheeks turn a soft pink. She opens her mouth like she’s about to say something, but doesn’t. Instead, she nods once, turns around, and walks back into the party.

Rio peers at the clock on the wall. It’s already past midnight when she finally switches off the TV, realizing she hadn’t really been watching it anyway. 

She’s in nothing but her button-up and boxers, planning to sleep in them since she didn’t bring any clothes. Maybe next time she should pack extra for unexpected trips like this. 

Her eyes then drift toward the door, wondering if Agatha’s already back and in the room across the hall.

Rio considers texting her boss to ask if she’s back, but that feels kind of unprofessional, doesn’t it? Then again, the line between professional and not has gotten pretty blurry lately. So really, what’s the harm? 

Still, she hesitates. What would Agatha even think? What would Rio even say? “Hey, are you back yet?” What is she, her needy girlfriend? Jesus. Rio groans and tosses her phone into the pillows.

Perhaps it’s just the high from seeing Agatha again after a few days apart. It will pass eventually. 

So, like the professional grownup she’s supposed to be, one who has no idea what to do with the growing feelings she has for her boss, Rio shoves the thoughts aside, crawls into bed, and forces herself to sleep.

She manages maybe an hour of sleep before she is jolted awake by intense, heavy pounding on her door. Still groggy and with her heart lurching, she scrambles out from under the sheets and opens it.

“Figured you’d be awake,” Agatha quips, standing in the doorway with two bottles of wine, one empty glass, and of all things, a blunt in her other hand. “Found my old stash in the attic. Probably tastes like shit, since I had this back in college. But this is all I have.”

Rio just blinks at her, caught somewhere between confused and concerned. 

“Are you gonna make me beg? Let your boss in, Rio.”

Wordlessly, Rio steps aside, and Agatha walks in as if she owns the place — which, to be fair, she sort of does, given that she’s the one footing the bill. She kicks off her heels with a sweep of her feet and collapses on the bed as if it were her own.

Rio closes the door behind her, still a little stunned. Agatha already appears to have had a touch too much. Her mascara’s smudged, and now that Rio’s eyes have adjusted, there’s a puffiness to her face she hadn’t noticed before. Had she been crying?

“Why are you still standing there?” Agatha calls out as she lights the blunt. “Am I supposed to enjoy all this by myself?” She takes a drag, immediately breaks into a violent cough, and makes a face. “God, that’s disgusting.” Still, she takes another hit, then shoots Rio a crooked grin and pats the bed. “Get your ass over here, Vidal. I don’t bite.”

Rio walks over and sits beside her. Agatha pours her a glass without asking and hands it over.

“Are you okay?”

Agatha exhales through her nose, smoke curling as she leans back. “Why do you always ask that?” Rio just gives her a look. “I’m fine,” she huffs. “This is me being fine. Celebrating it, actually. You should be grateful I decided to let you tag along.” She passes her the blunt.

Rio hesitates but takes a hit anyway, and immediately coughs like she’s being strangled. 

Agatha laughs. “Told you it was awful.”

“How much of that bottle have you had?” Rio asks, nodding to the nearly empty wine.

Agatha looks down at it, counts on her fingers, then lifts four, and adds a thumbs-up for good measure.

“Somewhere around there.” 

“Jesus, I think you’ve had enough,” Rio says, reaching for it, but Agatha quickly pulls it away.

“Hey, you’re not the boss of me,” she warns, wagging a finger. “I’m drinking. You’re here. So either join me, or I’ll take all this back to my room and enjoy this on my own.”

Rio watches Agatha for a second. She doesn’t know what happened at the party or in that big fancy house, but something clearly rattled her. So she sighs, takes another hit then immediately doubles over coughing so hard she nearly spills her wine.

“I can’t believe with all your money, this is the best you could dig up,” she wheezes.

Agatha snorts, sinking back against the headboard. “Please. It was last minute. It’s not like I could waltz into my father’s study and start digging through his desk for the good stuff.” 

By the time they’re almost through their second bottle, Rio somehow ends up upside down on the bed, feet near the headboard, lazily toying with Agatha’s toes like a bored cat. She briefly wonders, very stupidly, very suddenly, what Agatha would do if she leaned in and sucked on one.

Then immediately slaps herself — mentally, probably, though there’s a chance her actual cheek took a hit. Hard to tell at this point. Damn it. She hadn’t expected Agatha’s college weed to even hit this hard. 

Then again, maybe rich people’s weed ages like fine wine and just gets more potent with time.

Rio has completely lost track of what they've been talking about for the past hour. Maybe it was something about her first molly at Pride when she was seventeen. Or that time she’d gotten chased by a hellhound of a Doberman while covering a student council scandal for their college paper. 

Or when Agatha casually shares how she once punched a politician right in the face after he cornered her and tried to make a move by the bathroom entryway at a fundraiser, back when she was still trying to make a name for herself at Nocturne. Rio, halfway through her wine, had demanded to know the guy’s name, swearing she’ll find him and punch him all over again. But two glasses later, maybe five, maybe six, she ends up mixing up the names and vows vengeance on a completely different guy. 

Agatha had nearly choked on her drink laughing.

Then, noticing how quiet it’s gotten, Rio lifts her head to check on the other woman, only to find her already watching, like she’s been doing it for the past ten minutes. 

“You know, you should really stop looking at me like that if you’re not planning to tell me what you’re thinking,” she grumbles. “It’s driving me a little crazy.”

Agatha chuckles, her hair now loose in soft waves from the bun it had been in earlier. She crawls over and stretches out on her stomach beside Rio, resting her head on her arms. 

“ You drive me crazy,” she says, like it’s the simplest truth in the world. Rio, brain still fogged from the wine and weed, can’t even come up with a comeback before she adds, “Because you don’t know how to keep your mouth shut.”

Silence falls as Agatha’s eyes search Rio’s like they’re flipping through pages only she can read. 

“Has anyone ever told you how much of a conundrum you are?” she murmurs, her finger lazily tracing the slope of Rio’s nose. Her mind, clearly floating somewhere a few feet above the bed.

“No. And I’m pretty sure most people I know now don’t even use that word anymore,” Rio mumbles, her eyelids drooping from the high, but she keeps them open, stubbornly memorizing Agatha’s face.

For a moment, there’s nothing but the sound of the night outside the hotel window. Then Agatha’s hand stills and moves to cup Rio’s cheek, her thumb gently brushing her skin.

“Well, you are, Rio Vidal,” she says, like it just slipped out of her. “You’re a conundrum. My conundrum.”

The weed might be fogging up Rio’s brain too much for her to fully process what Agatha is saying — or how she’s slowly leaning in, closing the small space between them. Rio’s eyes almost flutter shut, but she forces them open, holding on with everything she’s got for whatever’s about to happen.

And then, like the fog slowly lifting, Agatha moves closer and simply presses her lips to hers, soft and light as a breath.

And just as quickly, it’s over.

Agatha gradually pulls away, rolls onto her back, and lets out a soft yawn, as if nothing earth-shattering just happened to Rio. “You wouldn’t mind if I closed my eyes for a bit?” she mumbles, already halfway there before Rio can answer.

Rio, still caught in her head over what just happened, freezes like she’s in some kind of trance. Her brain keeps looping the fact that her boss, Agatha Harkness, of all people, just kissed her. Well, technically, it still counts as a kiss, right? Even if it was barely more than Agatha pressing her lips to hers.

But instead of overthinking what had just transpired, all of Rio’s uncertainties dissipate the second she hears a few soft snores from the woman next to her. And she can’t help but smile.

She watches as Agatha rolls onto her side, the hem of her satin dress riding up just enough to reveal the long lines of her legs. Carefully, Rio tugs it back down, reaches for the blanket, and drapes it gently over her. She lingers in the moment a minute longer, brushing a strand of hair off Agatha’s face.

“The thing about conundrums,” she whispers, “is that you’re mine just as much as I’m yours.”

Rio wakes to sunlight slipping through the hotel drapes like a slow leak of everything warm and way too bright for her throbbing head. 

Her mouth is dry as hell, and her limbs are tangled in the sheets. She blinks up at the ceiling, needing a second to remember where she is and why the room smells faintly of smoke and a familiar lavender scent. On instinct, her hand reaches across the mattress, only to find the space beside her cold.

She slowly turns her head, eyes landing on the bedside table. There’s a tall glass of water, a couple of advil, and a folded note scribbled on hotel stationery. Her stomach flips a little before she even reads it.

Left early. Drive safe. 

— A.H. 

A good journalist, Rio’s dad used to say, is always three steps ahead of the story. He drilled that into her at a young age, told her it was the one thing she should always carry with her. But somehow, that valuable lesson’s gone out the window now that Agatha’s back to pretending she doesn’t exist.

Rio should’ve seen it coming. She should’ve known the moment she saw the note. That was Agatha’s way of putting her walls back up, one careful brick at a time. And Rio, of all people, should’ve known better. She should’ve picked up on the signs, seen the change rolling in again, like a storm she’s already been through once before.

She studied journalism. She’d written articles, chased leads, connected dots from a single thread of truth. And even if she’s not writing anything right now, not in any official capacity, this job she’s had for months doesn’t change the fact that, at her core, she’s still a journalist.

And journalists are supposed to see what others don’t.

But when it comes to Agatha — Rio is blind. Not because she isn’t looking, the hell, she is, but because something about that woman scrambles every instinct she’s ever trusted.

Rio has eyes. But with Agatha, it’s like she doesn’t even know how to use them.

Days go by since that night in Jersey, and on the surface, everything slides back into the usual routine. At least, that’s what Rio tells herself, and she tries to believe it’s fine. 

Except for all the little things that keep crashing into it, poking holes in Rio’s carefully patched composure, and making her feel like she’s five seconds away from combusting into flames.

Take Thursday’s run-through, for instance. Nothing out of the ordinary: just her, Jen, some stylists, and a dozen models waiting to be approved or adjusted. 

Except Agatha, for some reason, has suddenly decided that she wants to get handsy. Fixing collars, brushing hair from shoulders, laughing a little too long at some other woman’s joke. Rio nearly snaps her pen in half. Because one, Agatha Harkness never flirts on the job. It’s like a rule. And two, the only time she’s ever even come close is with Rio. 

Another test of Rio’s patience and composure comes when a couple of gorgeous, long-legged editors from Nocturne France and Madrid show up at Agatha’s office, looking like they just walked off a runway. As if that wasn’t enough, Rio even catches wind of a juicy little rumor that Agatha might, or might not, have a history with one of them. Or both. 

Rio tries to shove the thought aside, but it’s impossible when she hears Agatha laughing from her office at whatever those runway-ready editors just said. 

It also doesn’t help that she can hear Agatha slip into French every now and then. Normally, that’d be sexy as hell, have Rio swooning, and undoubtedly turned on. But unfortunately, she’s too upset and way too jealous to even appreciate any of it. And that just makes her even madder.

The last straw for Rio, because she’s only human, with burning feelings and a heart that can only take so much, comes when a familiar blonde strides confidently toward the office, asking for her boss. The very same woman who, months ago, was supposed to be out of the picture. Or at least, out of Agatha’s.

“I’m sorry, but Agatha’s in an important meeting right now,” Rio says, stepping in front of the blonde. “And I don’t think we can accommodate you without an appointment.”

The blonde woman smiles, all pleasure and self-assurance. 

“Oh, I don’t really need an appointment. She’s been expecting me.” 

“She has?”

Rio doesn’t mean for it to sound as surprised as it does, but it earns her a curious look.

“Yes, she knows I’m coming today,” the woman replies. “But if she’s still in an important meeting, like you said, I’ll just wait for her in her office.” She’s already moving toward it as she speaks.

Rio seems to be in a completely different dimension, professionalism-wise, because she immediately steps in to block the way again. “I really don’t think I can let you do that.”

Jen, buried in paperwork at her desk, looks up and eyes Rio like she’s wondering what the hell she’s doing. Rio’s asking herself the same thing, especially when the blonde starts to look a little annoyed.

“And why’s that?” she asks. 

“Like I said, no appointment. Agatha doesn’t like other people wandering into her office unannounced.”

The woman leans in slightly, eyes gleaming with recognition and just the right amount of entitlement. She lowers her voice so only Rio can hear her. “Sugarplum, we both know I’m not just other people .”

And Rio knows it. Of course she does. Maybe that’s exactly why she’s so hellbent on getting this woman as far away from the building as possible. Six months ago, Rio would’ve slapped herself for acting like this. But before Rio can say anything else, a voice speaks up behind them.

“Natalia?”

“Aggie!” The blonde’s face literally lights up as Agatha walks in.

Aggie? Rio fights the urge to visibly flinch. She straightens up, then looks at Agatha like an obedient soldier waiting for orders. “I told her you were in a meeting and she didn’t have an appointment but—” 

“I asked her to come.” The words unexpectedly hit Rio like a dagger to the chest.

“You asked her to come?” Rio repeats, almost to herself.

None of them seem to have heard it, except for Agatha, who then turns her attention to the blonde. “I’m sorry I didn’t call you about the meeting. It came up at the last minute. Did you wait long?”

“Oh, not at all. No worries. I just got here,” the woman says easily. 

Agatha only responds with a polite smile, then turns back to Rio, who, for some reason, is still standing there like she forgot how her legs work. 

“Rio, would you be so kind as to get me a double espresso? Scalding hot. My head’s still spinning from that meeting,” she says, in the most sugar-coated, fake-polite tone Rio’s ever heard from her. Then, with a sweet smile, she turns to the blonde. “And you, sweetheart? Would you like Rio to get you anything too?”

Sweetheart? And the dagger just twists a little deeper.

“Just a latte,” the woman replies.

Agatha then shoots Rio a look. “You heard her. A double espresso and a latte. Now, please be so kind and do your job.” With that, she turns and strides toward her office, the blonde following close behind.

And Rio doesn’t know why she feels like she’s about to burst into flames, or why her eyes suddenly burn with something else. 

The days that follow are harder for Rio, especially because it’s her own damn decision to shove down whatever feelings she’s been carrying and just act the way Agatha clearly wants her to: indifferent and professional. Agatha wants her to do her job, so that’s exactly what Rio’s doing. 

No stolen glances, if she can help it. No soft smiles that won’t be returned. And most especially, no lingering eye contact. In fact, she’s doing her best not to look Agatha in the eyes whatsoever. 

Because if Rio doesn’t know how to use them around the woman without giving herself away, then maybe it’s better not to use them at all.

It seemed to have worked, whatever switch flipped, it cooled the wildfire in Rio’s chest, or maybe Agatha just miraculously decided to stop flirting with everything that walked and went back to just lashing out about everyone’s incompetence instead. 

Rio had managed not to take it personally, as long as it wasn’t directed at her. That was the plan, after all. Finish the year, keep her sanity, and eventually move on to a job her heart actually wanted.

Though lately, her heart’s been a little unclear about what it really wants.

But just when Rio thinks she might actually survive a few more months of this job, another storm rolls in. 

This time in the form of Evanora Harkness, looking like hell’s personal emissary as she storms into Agatha’s office without so much as a glance at Rio or a nod to Jen, who barely gets out a polite, “Ma’am, I’m not sure if—” before being completely ignored.

“You ungrateful, insufferable, selfish child!” The office door’s wide open when Evanora slams her palm against Agatha’s desk hard enough to make the glass tremble.

Rio is already halfway out of her chair, instinctively moving toward the open office when she hears Evanora say, “What do you think you’re doing, huh? You think you can pull something like that and just get away with it?” But before she can even reach the threshold, Agatha is suddenly there, standing in the doorway, like she knew Rio would come.

“Don’t,” Agatha says. And after days of avoiding her eyes, Rio’s heart feels like it’s breaking just from looking into them now. Because the way Agatha’s eyes speak to her is not of warning, but of a plea. 

And that’s what makes her stop.

Rio’s left with no choice but to stay outside as Agatha shuts the door, cutting off most of the sound. Through the thin frosted glass walls, she can only watch: Evanora’s hand furiously slicing through the air while Agatha stands still, saying nothing. Their voices don’t carry clearly, but Rio doesn’t need to hear the words to know it’s serious. Whatever this is, it’s not just a mother scolding her daughter.

“Jen, call security,” Rio says, her eyes locked on the heated argument behind the office glass. She tries to keep her voice even and calm, but her hands are already clenched.

“What?” Jen blinks, clearly just as stunned.

“I said call security.”

“But Agatha told us not—”

“Jen, I said call security. Right fucking now,” Rio snaps, not caring what her coworker might think. Her only priority is getting Agatha the hell away from her vile excuse of a mother. “Please.”

Though confused by Rio’s loaded reaction, Jen doesn’t argue. She scrambles up, snatches the phone off the receiver, and punches in the number.

Inside the office, the muffled voices swell like a storm.

“…don’t talk to me like I’m one of your staff—”

“...I won’t let you destroy everything I’ve built just to settle a score—”

“…this is about you dragging someone else into this—”

“…you really think this protects her?”

Before Rio can fully piece together the conversation, the security personnel Jen called finally rush in, and without thinking, Rio steps forward and pushes the office door open, as if she’s been dying to do so for the past ten minutes.

Evanora whips her head toward them, still full of rage.

“I’m sorry, Mrs. Harkness, but I’m afraid I’m going to have to ask you to leave,” Rio says, summoning every ounce of courage she can gather. She glances at Agatha, who meets her eyes with an uncertain kind of relief, along with something else Rio can’t quite name.

“How dare you call security on me?” Evanora hisses, whipping her attention back to her daughter.

Agatha straightens. “They’re only here to escort you out. Unless you’d rather I have them physically remove you,” she says, schooling her features into something more unreadable. “Now please go, Mother. You’ve already disrupted enough of my day.”

Evanora’s mouth twitches, like she’s biting back one last insult, but she holds her tongue. She turns on her heel, but not before her eyes briefly land on Rio. Just for a second, there’s a vestige of recognition before snapping back at Agatha. Whatever she sees, whatever she realizes, it curls at the corner of her mouth in the form of a cold, knowing scoff. Then she walks out, not saying another word.

“Are you okay?” Rio asks, keeping her distance, though she doesn’t miss the way Agatha’s shoulders seem to sink the moment Evanora is gone. 

But she doesn’t answer.

She walks around her desk instead, back turned, one hand pressed against her temple like she’s trying to hold her thoughts together. Then, finally, without turning around. “Why did you do that?”

Rio freezes. “What?”

She turns, eyes locked on Rio with a stare that’s almost angry, hurt, and disappointed. “I told you not to interfere.” Her lips are pressed tight, like she’s holding back something else she wants to say. 

“I was just trying to help.” 

“That was none of your business!” The shout is so loud, the glass walls seem to vibrate. 

And in all the time Rio has worked for her, Agatha has never, not even when furious over someone’s incompetence, raised her voice like this. 

Rio stares at her, then looks down at her hands which are shaking even more than they were before she worked up the courage to face Evanora. This is not how she expected the day to go. 

“What was I supposed to do? Sit on my hands while you let your own mother tear you apart?”

“You were supposed to do your job!” Agatha looks like she’s one second away from throwing Rio out. “Which didn’t include throwing yourself into something you don’t even understand just because you felt like playing a fucking hero!” 

“I wasn’t playing anything!” Rio’s eyes are wide now. “She stormed in here and insulted you. Again, what was I supposed to do? I couldn’t just stand there and let her do all that to you.”

“It’s not your place to decide how I deal with my own mother,” Agatha says, holding on to what’s left of her composure. “That’s my problem, not yours! You really think making a scene in front of the entire floor makes anything better?”

“I wasn’t trying to make a scene. I was trying to stop one!” Rio fires back. “She was out of line!”

“You’re the one who’s out of line!” Agatha’s hands slam on the desk. 

Rio freezes at the words, her chest rising and falling as she tries to speak. 

“Only because I couldn’t just stand there and do nothing.”

Agatha scoffs, rubbing a hand down her face. “God, you really don’t get it, do you?”

“Get what?” Rio shoots back. “That I care,” is what she wants to say next, but the words get caught somewhere between her throat and her pride.

Because the truth is, what she feels for Agatha isn’t just some stupid crush or passing admiration. 

Rio knows it’s something more. Because Agatha, with all her sharp edges and impossible walls, became someone who mattered to her. And that’s the thing. That’s why she couldn’t just stand there and watch someone talk down to her, touch her wrong, or look at her like she was anything less.

Because Rio cares. So deeply that the only thing running through her mind when Evanora stormed in was the need to protect her. Because somewhere along the way, Agatha stopped being just a job. Because suddenly, when it comes to Agatha, Rio's instinct isn’t just to stand beside her. It’s to stand in front of her.

“That I give a damn?” she says instead.

Her boss still seems to understand what she means, and she softens just a little. And Rio instantly feels like the worst person alive for raising her voice, especially with Agatha looking more vulnerable than she’s ever seen her. But the feeling only lasts three seconds.

“I think it’s clear this arrangement is no longer working.”

Rio doesn’t move. Doesn’t even breathe. After the heat that just came off both her and Agatha, it’s obvious someone’s hanging by a thread. And judging by the look on Agatha’s face, Rio knows exactly who it is, and pretty soon, everyone on the floor will too.

“I need someone who knows when to do their job, and when to stay the fuck out of things that don’t concern them. And lately, you’ve been terribly failing at both.”

Rio wants to scowl, wants to throw the damn hypocrisy back in Agatha’s face, because if anyone’s been crossing lines, it’s her. But she doesn’t. She can’t. She won’t. 

“So, what, you’re firing me now?” she mutters under her breath. 

Her eyes feel glassy, but she doesn’t let the tears fall.

Agatha slowly walks to her chair and turns it to face the window, instead of looking at Rio. 

Then she calls out, “Jen!” who practically stumbles through the door, eyes wide, and breathing hard. Her eyes jump between Rio and their boss. She must’ve heard enough from outside to know something’s gone very wrong.

And then with a low, displeased voice from behind the chair. 

“Please escort my former assistant out of my office and inform Human Resources that I will be needing a replacement by tomorrow. As of this moment, Miss Vidal is no longer employed here.”

Chapter 3

Chapter Summary

“I’m a very busy woman. Can we not do this in the middle of the street?”

“Then don’t.” Rio shrugs, eyes flat. “Nobody asked you to.”

“You told Jen I should ask you myself.”

“Yeah, well, clearly Jen didn’t catch the sarcasm.”

“But now I’m here. So can we not do this out in the open? Just get in the car.”

“Again, why would I ever get in a car with you? You’re not my boss anymore. So why don’t you do us both a favor and drive back to whatever corner of hell you crawled out of.”

She hears Agatha sigh through gritted teeth. “Rio, I swear to God, I’m not getting out of this stupid car to chase you in my Jimmy Choos! Get in, or I’ll have Javier drag your ass inside!”

Chapter Notes

sorry this took a bit longer. and yes, the chapter count has changed. story’s ending in chapter 4, folks. am i happy i still get to write them for a little while? yes, abso-fucking-lutely. but im also a bit impatient, because i really want you to read how their love story ends. but i swear im not doing it on purpose. not really. it’s just that when i sit down and write, something kind of possesses me and i get lost in it. or maybe i just have issues. either way, i really enjoyed writing this chapter.

anyway, a lot has happened to me these past few weeks lmao (and if you’re on twt, you probably know some of it). just glad i finally finished this, and im excited to hear your thoughts.

Three days later, Rio finds herself half-melted into the couch, surrounded by a mess that eerily resembles the aftermath of her first real heartbreak back in college. 

She’s in a hoodie she hasn’t washed in a week. Around her are crumpled takeout bags, a teetering tower of Coke cans and Red Bulls, a few half-drunk Budweisers, a spoon stuck in a bowl of what used to be ice cream and is now just sad, milky sludge, and a half-eaten bag of chips. 

She just finished watching Carol for the second time, or maybe the third. Hard to say. Her head hurts. Her stomach feels worse. She’s not sure she’ll ever move again.

“Jesus, dude,” Alice says as she walks in from work, drops her bag by the door, and takes one look at Rio. “Unemployment really does not look good on you.”

“I’m thriving,” Rio rasps, not bothering to lift her head.

Alice crosses the room, plucks the bag of chips off Rio’s stomach, and tosses it onto the coffee table.

“You’ve been marinating on that couch for days. Tell me you’ve at least packed.”

“Don’t say that word,” Rio groans into the cushion.

“I’m serious.” 

“Well, I don’t need to pack much. We’re only going for a couple days. And I’ve got stuff at your place anyway.” She turns her head just enough to look at Alice with one bleary eye. “But are you sure you wanna come? You really don’t have to, you know. I can go by myself. I don’t want you missing that gig on Friday.” She pauses, then smirks a little. “You’ve been talking about debuting that song where you rhyme ‘heartbreak’ with ‘car brakes’ for, like, three weeks.”

Alice snorts. “Please, that song bangs and you know it. But I can drop it whenever. Also, I’m still figuring out the bridge anyway. Maybe a little hometown misery will help.” She grabs a can off the floor and chucks it in the bin. “Besides, it’s your parents’ anniversary, I’m way overdue for a trip to see my mom, and not to mention, it’s your damn birthday. You really think I’d let you and her celebrate it without me?”

Rio stares up at the ceiling, blank and unmoving. She’d almost forgotten her birthday. Figures. The universe had really gone all in this week, leaving her jobless, mildly humiliated, and just the right amount of heartbroken to kill her appetite for pretty much everything. What a thoughtful little gift box.

“Now that you mention it…I don’t even feel like celebrating.”

Alice snaps her head toward her. “Oh, come on. We always celebrate your birthday.” She studies Rio for a beat, then shoves her legs off the couch and drops down into the cushions. “You’ve been sulking for days, you seriously need a shower, and despite what your mood suggests, the world’s not actually ending. Yet.” She grabs a chip from the coffee table. “There are still jobs out there. Didn’t you say that journo from Sesame Street wanted to see your stuff?”

“Wall Street,” Rio snorts, but Alice ignores the correction. Whatever. Rio gets the point. “It’s not like I can just send her my stuff out of nowhere. We talked once. I doubt she even remembers me.” She pauses, frowning at nothing. “And even if I did send something, that doesn’t mean I’d land a job. There’s still the whole question of whether my work’s even good enough.” Then another thought hits her, an uglier one, with a familiar name behind it. “And let’s not forget the very real possibility that a particular someone might have already blacklisted me from every publication in New York.” 

It frustrates her that she can’t even bring herself to say her name now.

Alice looks at her, already knowing who she means. “Come on. You really think your ex-boss would do that? Are you seriously thinking she’d go that far? Is she really that heartless?”

Rio’s frown deepens. Is Agatha Harkness heartless? 

She wants to believe that. She really does. It’d be easier if it were that simple. But then she thinks about those blue eyes, how they’d soften every time they landed on her, like Rio was someone worth paying attention to. The way Agatha smiled at her dumb jokes, or every time she said something weird just to get a laugh. The way she held her that night, like it actually meant something. If Agatha Harkness is really that heartless…then what the hell was all that?

“I don’t know,” Rio mutters. “And I don’t even care anymore.” She yanks the cushion over her face, her voice muffled. “Now just let me sulk in peace before I make it your problem.”

“No. I’m done with this. I’m officially drawing the line on day three,” Alice says, standing up and yanking Rio’s arm like she’s trying to haul her out of the underworld. “You need to stop sulking, pack your stuff for tomorrow, and for the love of God, take a shower. I’m not letting you stink up the apartment. Also, email your stuff to that hot journo from Sesame Street or whatever. Worst-case scenario, she doesn’t respond. Big deal. At least you tried.” She waves a hand at the disaster zone around them. “And this? This is not healthy. If Mom hears about any of this, you’re gonna get an earful the entire time we’re back home.”

Rio lets out a long, miserable groan and smashes her face into a cushion again. Alice pats her leg like she’s consoling a dying animal. Then, slowly, like a corpse reanimating, Rio peels herself off the couch. 

“There we go,” Alice says, hands on her hips like a smug coach. “Look at you. Rising from the ashes.”

“God, you’re annoying,” Rio grumbles, flipping her off halfheartedly as she shuffles down the hall. “I don’t know why I haven’t smothered you in your sleep yet.”

“It’s the unbearable love you have for me. I get it.” 

And Alice is not mistaken, because Rio does unbearably love her. In that gloriously dysfunctional, obstinate, sibling way that has her chasing Alice through the mayhem of Penn Station the next morning, running on autopilot, gripping her coffee like it's the only thing keeping her upright. 

Last night, Alice had made her shower, put on clean clothes, even helped her pack, but none of it helped her actually sleep.

Alice checks the board, then glances over her shoulder. “Alright, I’m gonna go grab the tickets and see if I can find something edible since someone decided we were too depressed for breakfast.” She eyes Rio’s coffee cup. “You good here?”

Rio simply nods, grateful she doesn’t have to move.

“Uh-huh. Just try not to pass out while I’m gone,” Alice points at her before disappearing into the crowd.

Rio stays where she is, cradling the last of her lukewarm coffee. 

She’s just about to get up and toss the cup in a nearby trash bin when her phone starts ringing.

“She wants you back,” Jen states the second Rio picks up and can’t even be bothered with a greeting.

A dry, incredulous scoff immediately escapes Rio. “I’m sorry, she wants what now?”

“She already fired three writers in the bullpen,” Jen goes on, like she’s been waiting to drop this and fully expected Rio’s reaction. “Then another one yesterday, an editor this morning, and probably someone else after lunch. That’s five or six people in under four days. And the issue goes to print next week.” 

Rio squints at her phone. “And what exactly does that have to do with me?”

“You need a job,” Jen says slowly, like Rio’s the one not connecting the dots. Rio bites her tongue, resisting the urge to snap “and whose fault is that?” but her former coworker just keeps going. “The magazine’s underwater right now, staff-wise. Half the applicants can’t even properly string a sentence together. She needs someone who actually knows what the hell they’re doing.”

“Un-fucking-believable.” 

People pass by on either side of Rio, hauling luggage, yelling over announcements, but she just stands there, wide awake now, and furious.

“So?” Jen asks. “Are you interested?”

“In working for Agatha Harkness again?” Rio scoffs. “She just fired me last week, remember?”

“And since then, she’s been clearing house. You’re not the only one. Now do you want the job or not?”

Rio pinches the bridge of her nose. “Again, Jen. She fired me.”

“I know that. I was there,” Jen snaps, irritated now. “But is that a yes or a no?”

Rio finally tosses her coffee into the trash with more force than necessary. 

“I don’t know what Agatha thinks she’s doing, but—” 

“She wants you in the pit. Am I not being clear?” Jen cuts in. “She wants you back here as soon as possible. Said she needs someone she can actually rely on to do the job. And she told me to tell you…it comes with the thing you’ve been chasing since day one.”

“What? Is she offering me a pony?” 

“Rio, she’s offering you a shot to actually write,” Jen declares, clearly starting to lose her patience.

Rio stops to think, just for a second. Then, like a punch to the gut, she remembers Agatha’s face, how she looked at her with anger and disappointment. The way she raised her voice. The way she dismissed her like she was nothing more than an easily replaceable employee.

“No. You can tell her I said no,” Rio says flatly. “If she thinks dangling a shiny little carrot is enough to get me crawling back and kissing the ground she walks on, she’s out of her damn mind.”

“She knew you’d say no at first.”

“At first?” Rio barks out a bitter laugh. “No, Jen. I’m saying no completely.”

Jen sighs, like Rio’s the one being unreasonable. And Rio thinks, not for the first time, that she and Agatha really are a perfect match as boss and assistant. 

“Alright, what’s going on with you? You used to talk my ear off about how badly you wanted to write. You literally lit up every time Agatha asked your take on a piece. And now you’re just…what? Dropping it? She’s handing you an actual shot here, Rio.” 

Rio stares out at the crowd, teeth clenched, like she’s trying to freeze whatever is swelling up in her chest. Then she groans, mostly at herself, for even bothering to argue with Jennifer Kale of all people. 

“Fine. Then riddle me this,” she muses. “Why does she really want me back?”

“She said you'd ask that too, by the way.”

Rio resists the urge to roll her eyes. “And?” 

“She said it’s a professional decision,” Jen supplies, and Rio pretends it didn’t hurt something in her. “Now, should I tell HR to start drafting you a new contract?” 

Rio lets out a breath and stares at the floor. “No. Tell your boss I don’t sit back down in burned chairs.”

“Fine. Your call. I could rattle off a dozen writers who’d sell a kidney for this kind of shot. But if clinging to your pride makes it easier to pretend this isn’t exactly what you want, even when it’s clear as day to someone like me, who barely even cares about you, then go ahead.” 

Rio sends out an impatient sigh. “You’re missing the whole damn point, Jen,” she scowls. “If Agatha Harkness wants me back, she can get off her high horse and ask me herself. And make damn sure she hears that, word for word.” She finishes the call with a quick jab of her finger.

Delaware has always felt the want to breathe again after keeping it in for too long. The second they cross state lines, it’s as if the world finally takes its foot off the gas. 

It’s definitely much calmer here. 

Less traffic, fewer people, less bullshit. Just open roads, rows of trees, and that unique serenity that only little towns like Hockessin seem to hold. The sort that allows Rio to hear her own thoughts.

Her old neighborhood looks pretty much the same. The houses are still spread out, each with a big, slightly uneven yard. Mailboxes leaning just a bit. Porch swings creaking in the breeze. A kid’s bike lying on the grass, like someone ran in for dinner and forgot all about it.

Their cab slows as it rolls past Mr. Miller’s house, and Rio can’t help but smile a little. Same white picket fence. Same crooked birdhouse hanging on by one stubborn nail. The same dented mailbox from when she crashed her bike at five. There’s even a pile of dry leaves by the gate that looks a lot like the one she and Alice accidentally set on fire.

She can almost hear herself telling that story. Almost hears Agatha laughing at it. Then she catches herself and shakes the thought off. She’s home to clear her head, not let that woman’s voice take up space again.

The cab pulls up in front of a familiar house, and there on the porch is Lorna, waving them in with both arms. “Well, if it isn’t my two city girls,” she grins, stepping down to meet them. “Look at you, skin and bones. What the hell have you been eating in New York?”

Alice groans as she steps out, grabbing her backpack. 

“Mom, come on. We talked about this. You can’t say stuff like that anymore.”

“What? I’m just calling it like I see it,” Lorna huffs, pressing a kiss to her temple and ruffling her hair like she’s still five. Then she turns to Rio, arms already open. “And you, young lady. Have you even been sleeping? Or is that boss you once told me about still being a pain in the ass?”

Rio doesn’t respond right away. She just shakes her head and steps into the hug, letting herself be squeezed tight. Lorna still has no idea she got fired, and Rio’s not about to start now. There’s no point in making it someone else’s burden. “I missed you too,” she mumbles into her shoulder instead.

“Welcome home, little bao,” Lorna says gently. She seems to sense Rio’s holding something back but lets it slide. “Now come in, both of you. I’ve got pot roast in the oven and lemon pie on the counter.”

“Now that is the best thing I’ve heard all week,” Alice says, pushing the door open.

“Well, good. Just wash your hands first. God knows what you touched in that city.” 

Dinner rolls around, and soon the kitchen fills with the sound of clinking plates, clattering silverware, and Lorna’s running commentary about the neighbors, local politics, and how the new ‘mailman’ has absolutely no idea where to leave the packages. 

Alice fires back with her usual dry sarcasm, tossing in updates from work, band drama, run-ins with drunk regulars, and a bald guy named Rick who keeps texting her at 2 am asking if she’s “still up for that jam session.”

Rio smiles and nods along, nudging chunks of pot roast around her plate. 

But the truth is, she’s barely catching anything. 

Her phone buzzes again in her lap, for the sixth time now, and she just presses the mute button without looking up. She already knows who it is. Has that tight feeling in her stomach about it. And she’s not in the mood to even hear that voice tonight. 

It’s only hours later, after the dishes have been cleared and Lorna and Alice have retreated to their rooms, that Rio steps out of the shower in a large shirt and boxers, her damp hair sticking to the back of her neck, and a towel hanging loose over her shoulders. The hallway light is dim, and the floor creaks beneath her bare feet as she heads toward the spare room.

It’s the same room she and Alice used to crash in during summer breaks, the one that eventually became hers after her mom died and Lorna took her in like family. Two twin beds pushed together, faded posters still taped to the walls, and a corkboard with a few lonely pushpins left behind. Some of her old books still sit on the shelf, and she makes a mental note to flip through a few while she’s here.

Rio walks over to the window and pulls the curtain aside. Across the street sits their old house. Same porch swing, though now it has a pair of mismatched cushions. Same big tree out front, still leaning slightly to the left. The shrubs appear different, trimmed in a way her mom would’ve complained about. Warm yellow light spills from the windows, like the place hasn’t changed at all, even though it has.

She used to swear she’d never sell it. But in the end, it helped her get through college without drowning in student debt. It had been a hard decision, but Lorna once told her that it was just a house. 

That her parents, the love, the memories, the real parts of home, were what she carried with her, no matter where she went.

Now there’s a new family living there. A mom, a dad, twin girls who leave their pink bikes scattered across the lawn, and a dog that barks every morning at six. Lorna used to say it drove her nuts, but like everyone else on the block, she eventually got used to it.

It doesn’t hurt to look at their old house, not exactly. But it’s strange, seeing someone else living in it. 

The place used to be where her mom and dad drank coffee on Sunday mornings. Where she scraped her knees, did homework at the kitchen table, blew out candles year after year.

It still looks like home. Even if it isn’t hers anymore.

She’s just about to set an alarm for her visit to the cemetery tomorrow when her phone buzzes again. Rio groans, grabs it off the nightstand, and finally answers, more out of pure irritation than anything else.

“What the hell do you even want? I already said no. Is that really so hard to understand?”

There’s a beat of silence on the other end, but it doesn’t cool the blood still boiling in Rio’s veins. Does Agatha even know how to leave things alone? 

Then a familiar voice cuts through, and for a split second, Rio freezes.

“Okay, not the greeting I was expecting but—”

“Hela?”

“Glad to know that outburst wasn’t meant for me,” Hela says, a little amused. “I’ve been trying to reach you, but you keep dropping my calls. Is everything okay over there?”

“That was you? Shit, I’m so sorry. I really thought you were someone else.” Rio sighs, dragging a hand down her face. “Wait, you’ve been calling me? Did you get a chance to read the stuff I sent?”

“I did. Haven’t finished all of it yet, but from what I’ve read? It’s good. Actually, kind of impressive.”

“Wait, seriously?”

“Seriously,” Hela affirms, and for once she’s not teasing, especially with her voice sounding all business. “If you’re up for it, I can put you in touch with my editor. He’s tough but he knows good work when he sees it. I can arrange an interview as early as tomorrow, if that works for you.”

Rio flops back on the bed, towel still draped over her shoulders, eyes fixed on the ceiling. 

“Uh...yeah, of course. That sounds great. I’d really love that. It’s just that I’m not in the city right now. I’m home for a bit. Well, not home-home, but back in Delaware. Visiting family. I’ll be here until Sunday, so if the interview could be after that, I’d be all in.”

“Delaware?” Hela repeats, as if she’s trying to picture what kind of place could’ve possibly raised Rio.

“Yeah,” Rio says, sitting up a bit straighter.

“Alright, so Monday then,” Hela says, the tiniest smirk in her voice. “And I’m guessing the fact you finally sent those files, and are actually saying yes, means you’ve officially broken free from Agatha’s clutches?” 

Rio exhales. “It’s a long story, but yeah. That’s why I’m free on Monday.”

“Glad to hear it,” Hela says. “Like I said, working with Agatha Harkness was never going to be a long-term arrangement. I’m not sure how you made your exit, but what matters is that you did. I’m looking forward to working with you, Rio. See you Monday.” 

The call ends before Rio can say anything else. She sets her phone on the nightstand, hair still damp, and lies back, staring at the ceiling with an unsure smile. But then, just like that, Agatha’s face pops into her head again. She frowns, swings her legs off the bed, and crosses the room to hang her towel on the hook behind the door.

The next morning, as if the neighbor’s dog barking across the street was her personal alarm clock, Rio wakes up early and decides to visit the cemetery alone. She walks out to the front yard, picks a bunch of azaleas from one of Lorna’s bushes, and wraps them in a plain brown paper. She does not ask Alice or Lorna to join her, and they are both aware that this is something Rio prefers to do on her own.

The cemetery’s nearly empty when Rio gets there. Just the groundskeeper trimming the grass, birds calling from the trees, and the soft crunch of gravel under her sneakers. 

She spots the headstone right away, kneels down, and places the azaleas gently at its base. Then she brushes off a few dry leaves and rests her hand on the cool marble.

“Hi, Mom. Hi, Dad.” 

She sits cross-legged on the grass beside them, letting the silence settle around her. 

For a while, she doesn’t say anything else. She just sits there, fingers running lightly over her parents’ names. Eventually, she starts talking. About New York. About her job, or what used to be her job. About how messed up things have been lately. And about this woman, the one at the center of it all, the one she can’t seem to stop thinking about no matter how hard she tries.

She tells them she misses them. That some days still feel heavier than others. But that she’s still doing okay, well, mostly okay, despite getting fired, and despite the mess of emotions that came with being fired by the woman she kind of likes. Or liked. Or whatever the right word is. Then she tells them about their old house, how one of the twins living there now waved at her on her way over.

It’s probably been over three hours when Rio finally pushes herself to stand. Her knees crack a little, and she lets out a soft laugh, muttering that she must be getting old, then remembers her birthday tomorrow. She brushes the dirt off her jeans, gives the headstone one last look, and walks back down the path. 

It’s a bit of a walk to town, but Rio doesn’t mind. 

She shoves her hands in her pockets and just keeps going, watching life happen around her. 

The sun’s up, but some gray clouds are rolling in, and the air smells like it might rain soon. 

The streets are slow. People are walking their dogs or sitting outside the town’s only decent coffee shop with their drinks. Kids zoom past on bikes. She walks by the familiar diner, the hardware store, and the old bakery that used to hand out free cookies to her and Alice when they were little. 

She doesn’t even notice how far she’s gone until her legs start to ache.

That’s when she hears a car slow down behind her. A familiar black one. Too shiny, too sleek to belong to anyone from around here. She takes one look over her shoulder, just to confirm, then snaps her head forward with a sigh as the window rolls down.

“Get in the car,” Agatha says, and just the tone of it makes Rio instantly angry.

She doesn’t stop walking. “What the hell are you doing here?” 

“I’m not here to argue.” 

“Well, that’s too bad,” Rio mutters, still moving. “Because I’m very much in the mood.”

Agatha leans closer to the window. “Can you just get in?”

“And why would I do that?” Rio says, not even glancing at her.

“Rio.” 

“No. No way.” 

“I’m a very busy woman. Can we not do this in the middle of the street?”

“Then don’t.” Rio shrugs, eyes flat. “Nobody asked you to.”

“You told Jen I should ask you myself.” 

“Yeah, well, clearly Jen didn’t catch the sarcasm.”

“But now I’m here. So can we not do this out in the open? Just get in the car.”

Rio scoffs. “Again, why would I ever get in a car with you? You’re not my boss anymore. So why don’t you do us both a favor and drive back to whatever corner of hell you crawled out of.”

She hears Agatha sigh through gritted teeth. “Rio, I swear to God, I’m not getting out of this stupid car to chase you in my Jimmy Choos! Get in, or I’ll have Javier drag your ass inside!” 

Rio stops walking the second Agatha raises her voice, and she hates how fast it still works on her. With a groan, she turns around, yanks the door open, and slides into the seat beside her, stiff as stone. She doesn’t even look at Javier in the front seat. Just folds her arms and stares hard out the window.

Agatha’s lavender perfume hits her first, like a slap and a hug all at once. It’s ridiculous how familiar it is. Annoying, too, because of course it still gets to her. The real betrayal, though, is that she actually missed it. Stupid, backstabbing, emotionally-compromised nose.

“Whatever you came here to say, just say it. I’ve got better places to be.”

“In this town?” Agatha says, one brow lifting, almost amused.

Rio glares. “Are you seriously mocking me right now?”

Agatha shakes her head right away. 

“No, I didn’t mean it like that. I just meant, where else would you even wanna be?”

“Obviously, literally anywhere but here with you.”

A heavy silence settles between them.

“Why won’t you take the job?” Agatha finally asks.

Rio lets out a dry, bitter laugh. “You’re seriously asking me that?”

“Yes.”

Rio still doesn’t look at her. “For someone so smart, it’s impressive how clueless you are, or how good you are at pretending to be. Why the hell would I want to work again for the woman who fired me — for sticking up for her, no less. To her bitch of a mother.”

“I meant what I said. It wasn’t your place to defend me.”

“Well, fuck me then. Sorry for actually caring, I guess.” It slips out too fast, and Rio clears her throat right after, like the noise might cover up the fact that it was too honest.

“Don’t you want to write?” Agatha asks, obviously trying to steer the conversation somewhere safer.

“Of course I do.”

“Then what exactly are we arguing about? I’m offering you a job that lets you do just that.”

“You’re offering me a job right after firing me. Humiliating me. I mean, who does that?”

“Can we not go in circles? Yes, I fired you. But I didn’t humiliate you. I would never do that—” Agatha pauses, recalibrates. “It was because you overstepped. Whether you admit it or not, it wasn’t your place.”

“So what is this, then?” Rio says. “Some weird power move? A slow-burn punishment? I overstepped, so now you’re offering me a job just to prove I was wrong?”

“You really think that’s how my mind works?”

“Beats me how your mind works!” Then their eyes finally meet. And in that pause, Rio sees the way Agatha’s hurt sits just beneath the surface. It catches her off guard and softens her, just a little.

“You’re a conundrum,” she adds, not with heat this time, but with something closer to the truth.

Agatha lets out a quiet breath at the familiar word, and her eyes drop to her lap. 

“Well, you seem to share the same affliction.” 

Another stretch of silence settles between them, barely inches apart, until a pointed throat-clearing from the driver’s seat snaps them both out of it. 

“I can’t believe you dragged Javier all the way out here for this,” Rio scoffs, turning back to the window. “Hope she’s paying you well, man.” Javier doesn’t say a word. Just keeps his eyes on the road.

Agatha straightens in her seat, ignoring the jab.

“The job is on the table. It’s yours. Whether you take it or not, it’s your call. Do whatever you want with it.”

Rio hesitates, then asks, “Did you regret it?” The question had been sitting in her head since Jen called yesterday and said Agatha wanted her back. “Firing me that day?”

Agatha pauses, thinking it over. Then she shakes her head. 

“I made that decision for a reason. You crossed a line, and while your intentions may have been good, I didn’t ask to be defended. I am fully capable of doing that on my own.”

Rio fixes her with a glare. “You dismissed me out of your office like I didn’t matter. Like I was just another name on your payroll, someone you could easily replace.”

“You are not just another name,” Agatha meets her eyes again. “I was angry, yes. Furious, even. But that doesn’t mean I ever saw you as disposable. I don’t—” She exhales, the words catching for a beat, then adds instead, “I’d never treat you like that.”

“You actually believe that?”

“I do,” Agatha says simply.

Rio licks her lips, nerves crawling up her throat, but she asks anyway. “And what about us? What happens to us if I do take the job and work for you again?”

Agatha blinks, as if robbed of her armor. “Us?” And Rio notices something in her face that she can’t quite recognize, but it makes her chest squeeze nonetheless. “You’d be writing for the magazine. I’d be the one signing your paycheck. What kind of ‘us’ do you think that leaves room for?”

“So that’s it?” Rio presses, fidgeting with her sleeves. “Like none of it happened? You firing me...and everything else before that?” 

She doesn’t say the rest out loud, but it’s loud in her head: their talks, that almost-kiss or whatever it was, the way Agatha looked at her like she wasn’t just some random person in her office. The way Rio noticed it and missed her when she wasn’t there. Was it all just going to stay inside her head? Was that really it?

Agatha opens her mouth like she’s about to say something else. Her nostrils flare. Then, calmly, like she’s locking it all away, she says, “It’s easier that way.”

“Right. That’s what I thought,” Rio mumbles. She lets out a long sigh. Javier glances at them in the rearview mirror, and Rio taps the window. “Puedes parar aquí, Javier. Por favor.” 

“What?” Agatha snaps, a hit of panic and disappointment breaking through as the car slows to the curb. Suddenly, she understands what Rio just said. “You can’t just take off without—”

“I can, Agatha,” Rio cuts her off, pushing the door open. “And I’m not taking the job.”

Before her former boss can say another word, Rio slips out into the overcast day. 

She hears Agatha calling after her, but she doesn’t look back. She rounds the corner without slowing down, letting the shouts fade until all that’s left is the pounding of her own heartbeat in her ears.

Later that night, the same black car sits parked down the block, barely visible through sheets of heavy rain and the low rumble of distant thunder. Lorna asks, just in passing, who it might be, and Rio shrugs, saying it’s probably just someone visiting the neighbors. 

In her room hours later, Rio stands by the window, arms crossed, watching the car idling beneath the streetlight. She wonders how long Agatha plans to keep this up, whatever this is. 

And though she hates herself for it, she also wonders how Agatha’s holding up, especially with the rain and thunder that haven’t let up all night. 

With a tired sigh, she switches off the light and steps away. When she peeks out again a few minutes later, the street is empty.

The next morning, Rio wakes up early again. 

Something about being home always pulls her out of bed with the sun. She throws on a hoodie, tightens her sneakers, and heads out for a run. Just a couple of laps around the block, enough to get her blood moving and clear her head a little. 

It’s become a bit of a tradition by now, starting her birthday with a run, like it might help set the tone for the rest of the day.

By the time Rio makes her way back to Alice’s place, she’s sweating and already preparing herself for the usual breakfast chatter with Lorna, who’s probably up by now, halfway through flipping pancakes, and for her daughter to be dragged out of bed like a stubborn high schooler. 

She steps into the kitchen, wiping sweat from her brow with her hoodie sleeve, but suddenly freezes when she notices Lorna and Alice aren’t alone.

“Morning, birthday girl,” Lorna calls out cheerfully from the stove, completely unaware of how Rio has frozen in the doorway. “Look who wandered in today.”

There’s an open white box of pastries on the table. And sitting right in front of it, legs neatly crossed, wearing a sleek deep mulberry coat like she owns the goddamn place, is Agatha fucking Harkness.

“You didn't tell us your boss was in town,” Lorna adds, looking over her shoulder.

Across from her, Alice sits frozen in her pajamas, clutching a cup of coffee with an expression that screams this is not at all her fault. She catches Rio’s stare and quickly mouths, “I didn’t invite her here,” before sneaking a pointed look behind her at her mom and mouthing again, “Blame her.”

Agatha seems to notice the wordless exchange between them and gives Rio an overly polite smile, showing all her teeth and blue eyes that look like they could start a fight at eight in the goddamn morning.

“I hope you don’t mind the visit. Alice’s mom was kind enough to let me in.”

“And she brought cake,” the clueless older woman pipes up from the stove again. “You’ve told me plenty about your boss, but somehow you conveniently left out the part where she’s actually thoughtful,” she snorts, shaking her head.

Rio bites back the urge to say she’s not her boss. At least, not anymore. If Lorna had any clue this woman kicked her out of her office less than a week ago, she wouldn’t be making eggs and offering her a seat at the family table. But Agatha, with that whatever-it-is charm she usually saves for investors and sponsors, clearly worked her magic on Lorna too.

“It’s purely a coincidence,” Agatha goes on smoothly. “I have several important meetings in the area and thought I’d drop off something for Rio. My other assistant mentioned it was her birthday.”

Rio knows it’s a lie. A well-packaged one, sure, but a lie. First off, Jen probably doesn’t even know it’s Rio’s birthday. And second, what important fashion meeting could there possibly be in the middle of nowhere Hockessin? Still, her chest does a stupid little flip just thinking that Agatha remembered at all.

“Well,” Rio forces a smile and reaches for Agatha’s arm, ready to pull her out of the house. She’s not in the mood to linger. “That’s very kind of you, Miss Harkness. But I’m sure those important meetings are waiting for you right now. We both know how busy your schedule is. Allow me to see you out. And thank you for stopping by…and for the cake.”

“Actually, I don’t mind staying a while. Lorna invited me for breakfast,” Agatha says, evidently settling in now that she’s been granted access to the house. “I might’ve let it slip that I’m not a fan of the food at the hotel I’m staying at.” 

What a witch. Whatever spell Agatha used to charm billion-dollar donors clearly works just as well on suburban moms.

“I did! And you’d be glad you said yes, because I make the best scrambled eggs and flapjacks around here,” Lorna says proudly, already rummaging through the kitchen cabinets. “I bet you never had anything like them. We use eggs from our neighbor’s chickens. Fresh and straight from the backyard. All from scratch. None of that store-bought, factory stuff you’re used to in the city.” 

Rio shoots another look at Alice, who looks like she’s holding herself together by sheer willpower. The tension between Rio and her so-called boss is thick enough to choke on, and her own mom, blissfully unaware, is not helping in the slightest.

“Right.” Rio clears her throat, trying not to snap. “Would you excuse us for a second?” she says, stepping forward and finally grabbing Agatha by the arm with a too-sweet smile. “Pretty sure Agatha here would love to personally see where those fresh eggs come from.” With that, she quickly drags her out the back door before anyone can argue.

The second they step into the backyard, out of earshot from the others, Rio lets go of Agatha’s arm like it burns. “What the hell are you still doing here?” she finally snaps, letting herself say it. “I already told you, I’m not taking that damn job.”

The other woman smooths down her coat as if she wasn’t just dragged through someone else’s kitchen.

“And I’m not accepting that rejection.”

Rio stares at her in disbelief. 

“You told me I could do whatever I wanted with that offer. I said no already. How many ways do I have to say it?” She paces a bit, then stops and looks right at her. “What do you actually want, Agatha?”

“I thought that was obvious. I didn’t suffer through a four-hour drive from fucking New York City and spent the night in some godforsaken roadside hotel in Hockessin for nothing.” 

She also looks like she might combust, but Rio just raises an eyebrow, waiting. 

Finally, like dragging teeth, Agatha spits the words out, each one sounding like it physically pains her. 

“Okay, fine! I’m here to apologize. I shouldn’t have taken my anger at my mother out on you.” She clears her throat. “Rio, I want you back.”

A beat.

“At work. I want you back at work,” she clarifies, almost too quickly.

Rio crosses her arms tightly over her chest. “You said that already. And my answer is still no.”

“Well, you should know by now, I don’t take no for an answer,” Agatha says, exhaling. “I really mean it, Rio. I need you back.” 

Rio exhales too. “Well, that’s too bad, because I already found a job.”

“You did?” 

Rio nods, ignoring the way Agatha’s eyes suddenly deepen with something like loss and disappointment.

“Yeah. I start Monday.”

Technically a lie, since it’s still just an interview. But there’s no harm in a little manifesting. And honestly, she’d say just about anything right now if it meant getting Agatha off her tail.

Agatha stands straighter, as if the last three seconds didn’t happen. 

“I’ll raise your salary then. Whatever that company’s offering you, I’ll double it.”

Rio lets out a bitter chuckle. “You really think that would change my mind? I don’t need the money, Agatha. What I needed was to be treated with basic respect. I was good at that job. Damn good. And you threw me out over something I only did for you.”

Agatha doesn’t deny it. She just breathes slowly, like her ribs are too tight. 

“Okay. I said it already, didn’t I? I said I was sorry. I was wrong to lash out. Isn’t that what you wanted to hear?” she says. “But I still stand by what I did. I didn’t need protecting, Rio. I didn’t need you to defend me. That’s not what I needed from you!” 

“Then what the hell do you need from me?”

“I just—” Agatha’s eyes find Rio’s for a second before looking away again. “I need someone who can keep up with me, who can see what I can’t see. Someone who actually gives a damn about the work.” 

“And you really think that’s me?” Rio asks, arms still crossed.

“I know it’s you,” Agatha puts forth, like it’s a fact. 

Rio sighs. “And what happens the next time I overstep?”

“I’ll be expecting you not to make the same mistake twice.”

Agatha looks at her again, but this time, for a long second. Her eyes soften a little, but not nearly enough.

Rio curses herself for looking at those almost-pleading blue eyes, how easily she gets blinded the second they show even the slightest bit of vulnerability.

She groans, presses her fingers to her temple, and starts pacing again. Kicks a pebble across the yard and fights the urge to scream at this infuriating woman who's somehow making her blood boil and her heart race like she just downed three shots of espresso.

“Okay, fine! I’ll take the fucking job,” Rio snaps. “But only on one condition.”

Agatha straightens up, her eyes instantly filled with optimism and something else Rio still can't quite put her finger on. Those stupid, stunning, hypnotizing ocean-eyes of hers. God, they were annoying.

“Which is?” 

Rio points a finger at her, heat rising in her chest. 

“Every damn time you look at me like that, or whatever the hell that face means, you tell me what you’re thinking. Whatever it is, I get to ask. And you have to tell me.”

Agatha squints at her. “What?” 

“You heard me.”

“That’s not even a reasonable condition.”

“It is now.”

Agatha just stares at her, baffled. “You want me to narrate my thoughts every time I look at you?”

“Only if I ask.” 

“You can’t be serious.”

“I am serious.” 

“And if I do say yes?” 

Rio comes out with, “Then you stop chasing me around.” She stares at Agatha like she’s daring her to back down, but the latter seems just as determined. “And I start Monday.”

They stare at each other for a while before Agatha finally lets out a breath, her shoulders dropping just a bit. “Okay. If that’s what you want, then fine. I accept your stupid condition. Now, I expect nothing but to see you on Monday, Miss Vidal.” She turns to head back to the house, but stops and looks over her shoulder. “Oh, and I almost forgot. Happy birthday.” 

Rio stands there a moment longer, hands on her hips, staring up at the cloudy sky like it might give her a sign. If she could call Zeus and ask for a lightning bolt straight to the face, she probably would.

“I’m such an idiot,” she mutters to herself.

Then she groans once last time and heads back inside after Agatha, like the absolute clown she is.

It must’ve been dumb luck, or maybe just Rio’s weird superpower of making friends with people who somehow always managed to keep their jobs, that not a single one of her bullpen buddies had been fired by Agatha in the week since Rio herself got booted out of the building.

The bullpen down on the lower floor is nothing like the glass-walled fortress Rio used to work in as Agatha’s junior assistant. That top floor, where the so-called beast of Nocturne reigns alongside her army of well-dressed, stiletto-sharp demons, is a whole other species.

The bullpen is its own strange beast entirely.

A systematic maze of boxes that looked like they hadn’t been updated since flip phones were cool. Half the desks were buried under old printouts, mood boards, empty coffee cups, and the occasional lip balm.

The other half had at least one aggressively cheerful quote taped to the wall, usually sitting beside a picture of Troy Bolton (if the person was gay), Keira Knightley in Bend It Like Beckham (if the person was also gay), or a chunky ginger cat in sunglasses (if the person was barely holding it together).

Somehow, Rio had ended up with a desk right in the middle of all three varieties. 

“You know,” Shuri, the youngest of the bunch, says around a mouthful of sandwich as she wheels her chair over to Rio’s desk, “we should seriously build a shrine in your honor down here in the pit.”

Rio gives her a look. “And why exactly would we do that?”

“Cause you earned it,” Shuri says, pointing at her with half a sandwich. “Like, who else gets fired by Agatha freaking Harkness and actually comes back? Nobody. I’m pretty sure you’re the only person in Nocturne history to ever get that kind of special treatment.” She shakes her head, still kind of in awe.“That’s some real phoenix energy, dude. Rising straight from expensive-ass, designer-smelling ashes.”

Rio rolls her eyes. If she had a nickel for every time someone compared her to a phoenix, she could’ve bought herself a better chair by now. Still, she can’t help but smile, thinking Shuri, Alice, and especially Billy would get along just fine if they ever crossed paths.

“Nah,” Darcy calls out from across the row, eyes still glued to her screen. “Still feels like a downgrade, if you ask me. Getting tossed down here with the rest of us when you could’ve stayed up in Fortress Harkness with the fashion angels and that stupid fancy coffee machine? Sounds more like punishment than anything. Down here? When it rains, it rains hellfire.”

“I don’t know,” comes Bob’s gentle voice from the next cubicle. “I think Rio is already starting to like it here. Right, Rio?” Bob, bashful and sweet, peeks over the divider like a shy meerkat. Darcy once pointed out that he probably says “sorry” at least five times before lunch. And one of them was to a chair.
