Rio looks at all of them. “Well,” she says, stretching her arms behind her head, “Bob’s right. I think I do like it here. At least here, I actually get to write.”

And at least here, she doesn’t have to spend the whole excruciating day pretending not to look at Agatha.

It’s been almost a week since she started down here, and the only glimpse she’s had of the so-called fortress beast was when she had to swing by the deputy editor’s office for some random paperwork.

“Hey, Rio?” A woman from the other side of the bullpen taps lightly on the edge of her cubicle. “Melina wants to see you,” she says, then turns and walks off before Rio can even get a word out.

All three of Rio’s nearby friends turn to look at her, probably wondering the same thing she is. She just shrugs, grabs the hoodie draped over her chair, and pulls herself away from her desk.

One of the few things she actually likes about working down here in the pit is that there’s no need for blazers, heels, or stiff trousers. Just hoodies, sneakers, and whatever gets you through the day without crying into your keyboard. The perks of being a writer who rarely has to deal with visitors.

She heads toward Melina’s office, tucked in the far corner of the floor. It’s bright and unassuming, nothing like Agatha’s intimidating tower upstairs. Open space, just a single divider, a cluttered desk, and a large glass window with a view of the neighboring building.

Rio knocks once on the doorframe. “You wanted to see me?” she says, already stepping inside.

Melina looks up and gives a quick nod. “Yes, Rio. There you are. I need you to drop these proofs off at Agatha’s office,” she points to the pile in the corner of the table before turning back to her keyboard. “She needs to review all of them before tomorrow’s editorial meeting.”

Rio immediately stiffens at the idea of going up to Agatha’s office. She hasn’t set foot there since the incident, and definitely not since she came back. 

“Me?” she asks, hoping maybe her deputy editor meant someone else. Anyone else.

“Yes, you, Rio,” Melina says, barely glancing at her. “Is there a problem?”

Yes. Because if she had even an ounce of a choice, she sure as hell wouldn’t be hauling herself upstairs. Working here would be infinitely more tolerable if she never had to lay eyes on Agatha Harkness, on most days, or any damn day, really.

“No, of course not,” she quips, grabbing the proofs from the desk and walking out.

The walk to the elevator feels way less like a quick errand and more like Orpheus heading into the underworld, except somehow, she’s going up. Her legs keep moving, but her brain is spinning.

Maybe, if she slows down just enough, some poor intern will come running after her to say Melina changed her mind and spare her the whole ordeal.

But Rio seems to have lucked out, because by the time the elevator doors slide open, her palms are clammy and her heart’s pounding like it knows something she doesn’t.

The first person she sees upstairs is the girl who ended up replacing her. The new assistant looks exactly like someone the company would hire. Someone who might have been grown in a lab specifically to match Agatha’s aesthetic, and the whole floor of corporate plastic clones. Flawless posture, a polished veneer of a smile, and no soul behind the eyes. Poor thing.

Then Jen looks up from her desk and gives Rio a once-over, making her painfully aware of what she’s wearing, which is nowhere near top-floor aesthetic in her faded college hoodie and worn-out ripped jeans.

“She’s been waiting for that,” Jen says, trying very hard not to comment on the outfit directly.

“Nice seeing you too, Jen,” she greets her former floor-mate, then heads toward Agatha’s office.

Inside, Agatha doesn’t look up when Rio enters, her eyes locked on the screen. But it’s clear she’s been expecting her since she doesn’t even need to look to know who it is. 

“I was beginning to think you’d already forgotten how to find your way up here.”

“Sorry.” Rio clears her throat. “Here are the files you asked Melina for.”

Agatha doesn’t say anything else and just points to the side table, still without looking up.

Rio walks over and places the stack beside the other piles. 

But she freezes abruptly as she notices a familiar little succulent sitting right on top.

It’s not dead. Not even a little wilted. It’s green, and actually thriving.

Rio had honestly assumed Agatha would’ve tossed it the second she was gone. Either that, or let it rot out of pure indifference. She wasn’t the plant-caring type, as she’d pointedly told Rio once, but the thriving succulent seemed to say otherwise. 

Did Agatha actually take care of the plant Rio gave her?

She shakes herself out of it. “Well, that’s all she sent me,” she says, turning back. “If you need anything else, you can just call her, I guess.”

She’s halfway to the door when Agatha speaks.

“Did I say you could leave?”

Rio stops in her tracks. “Huh?” 

“I have a presentation to finish for Stark in about an hour,” Agatha says, still focused on her laptop. “While I’m doing that, you can go through the drafts. Pick the ones you think fit for our next issue.”

“Here?”

Agatha finally looks up. “Is there somewhere else you’d rather be?”

Rio opens her mouth, then closes it again.

I’d rather be anywhere than sitting here trying not to look at you, her brain offers.

Instead, she says, “No. Fine. I’ll just...sit here, then.” 

It’s barely been twenty minutes since Rio sat down, but it already feels like she’s being slowly roasted alive. She tries to concentrate on the pages in front of her, but it’s hard when she can feel Agatha sneaking stares her way. 

And she knows she’s not imagining it. She got a full eight hours of sleep last night. This isn’t sleep-deprived paranoia. Agatha is definitely looking at her. 

The most annoying part, though, is that Rio can’t look back without being obvious. All she gets are quick peeks from the corner of her eye, which is totally unfair.

However, it seems like some gay god of yearning heard Rio’s silent plea, because not long after, there’s a knock at the door and Jen pokes her head in.

“Agatha? Paris is on the line. They’re asking to speak with you directly.”

“Transfer it,” Agatha says, already reaching for the wireless phone. She then answers it mid-turn, walking toward the large glass window behind her desk.

Rio thinks about leaving, but then again, Agatha didn’t tell her to. So she stays in her seat and pretends she’s not hearing any part of the conversation. But it doesn’t take long for the calm to break.

“No, I’ve seen the numbers,” Agatha says into the phone. “And no, I’m not concerned. Why would I be? I’m not about to let a temporary spike throw off months of planning. Let her have her little win.”

A moment later, the French starts. And Rio really tries not to listen. But it’s hard to ignore a storm when it’s happening three feet away. Not that Agatha seems to care what Rio hears.

The latter then lets her eyes travel toward the other woman. There’s something tired about her today, more than usual. Dark circles beneath her eyes, mostly covered by makeup, but not enough to fool Rio. 

Has she even been sleeping?

Then Rio notices the lunch. A perfectly cooked steak, golden potatoes, and a little side salad on a sleek white plate, sitting untouched beside her laptop. She glances at the time. It’s almost three in the afternoon, and Agatha clearly hasn’t eaten yet. 

Has she even taken a break all day?

But before Rio can dwell on it, Agatha turns halfway around, and she quickly snaps her eyes back to the pages in front of her like a kid caught staring. 

Agatha’s voice rises again. Whoever’s on the other end of that call is definitely pissing her off.

“Je sais ce qui est en jeu. Don’t insult me by thinking I don’t. Valentina peut brandir ses chiffres toute la journée, qu’elle le fasse. Je m’en fiche. I have no need to compete with people beneath me.”

Rio frowns, trying to catch bits of the meaning from the one French class she took back in her first year of college. But before she can make sense of it, Agatha ends the call sharply.

“No, we’re done here. And yes, I’m sure I’ll have a lovely day. Though certainly not because of you!”

Agatha slumps back into her chair at the same time she drops the phone back into its receiver.

“Imbéciles,” she mutters, running a hand down her face and leaving it there. 

That’s when Rio stands slowly, papers in hand, and walks over to the desk. She sets the stack down gently in front of her, just as Agatha pulls her hand away and looks up.

“What’s this?” she asks. 

“I think some of these drafts are good to go. But you can go through them yourself too, just to be sure.”

However, Agatha is eyeing the Snickers bar Rio had placed on top of the stack, pulled straight from the pocket of her hoodie. “I meant this,” she says flatly, pointing at it.

Rio doesn’t answer right away. Agatha definitely doesn’t need to know she noticed the untouched lunch, or that, for a second, she thought Agatha looked one phone call away from passing out.

“You’re not you when you’re hungry,” she says with a shrug, trying hard to keep her face free of any trace of concern and hoping a bit of dry humor might cover for it, too. “If you don’t need anything else from me, I’ll head back downstairs,” she adds, hands slipping into her pockets.

She turns and walks out before Agatha can say anything, doing her best not to overthink the way she can still feel Agatha’s eyes on her all the way to the door.

The days that follow feel like a slow, cruel experiment, one specifically designed to test Rio’s tolerance for Agatha Harkness, or maybe just to see how long she can hold out before being sucked back into her orbit like some helpless satellite.

Because somehow, Agatha has been seen in the pit more than usual.

Sometimes she’s heading to Melina’s office. Sometimes she’s supposedly checking in on layout progress. And sometimes, Rio swears, she’s just walking through for absolutely no reason, like a lion casually strolling through a petting zoo.

Even Shuri noticed. “She’s down here again?” she had whispered one afternoon as they watched Agatha’s heels disappear around a corner, pointing out how she rarely ever set foot in this part of the building. Normally, prey came to her. “But now, it’s giving: an apex predator on a casual hunt,” Shuri had joked.

Rio and the others had laughed it off. 

Obviously, Agatha wasn’t down here because of her . That would be ridiculous. Why would she be?

Still, the theory gets harder to dismiss when, one morning, a box of fresh coffee arrives in the bullpen, ordered, apparently, by Agatha herself.

And sure, maybe she’d been making some team-wide announcement about an upcoming deadline. Rio honestly couldn’t say, because she hadn’t heard a single word of it. Because all she could focus on was the way Agatha had walked past the desks, barely sparing anyone a glance, and then wordlessly placed a cup of coffee — Rio’s usual, not-too-sweet cup of coffee — right on her desk.

But despite all the little things piling up, despite her ongoing hypothesis that maybe Agatha keeps showing up in the pit for her, Rio refuses to let it get to her head. She’s not about to start spiraling over a cup of coffee and a few unexpected hallway sightings.

So instead of having lunch with her friends in the noisy company cafeteria, she grabs her sad little takeout, and heads out for a walk. The nearby park isn’t anything fancy, just a stretch of green and a few scattered benches. People are walking dogs, eating ice cream, and scrolling on their phones.

Rio finds a spot under a tree and sits down, unwrapping her lunch. She watches people for a while: an old man feeding birds, a young couple arguing, a kid trying to chase a pigeon, and lets the buzz of everything around her fill the space that Agatha’s been taking up in her brain.

She’s halfway through her cold sandwich when she hears a sharp curse from a nearby bench.

“Maledizione.”

Rio looks up. The voice belongs to an older woman, fussing with something in her lap. She’s draped in layers of fabric: flowy, bright, a mess of color. Big rings, jangly bracelets, a scarf that keeps slipping off her shoulder. A sketchpad rests across her knees.

Rio watches her for a second. Then, not one to let people struggle alone, she asks, “Everything alright?”

The woman huffs, patting her clothes like she’s lost something. 

“I can’t find my glasses. I had them with me when I sat down. I know I did.”

Rio stands and walks over, trying not to smile when she sees the said glasses, resting perfectly on top of the woman’s head. “Uh,” she says gently, pointing upward. “You mean those?”

The woman freezes, then bursts out laughing. A loud, full laugh that turns a few heads.

“Oh for heaven’s sake,” she says, still chuckling. “Getting old is hell.”

Rio chuckles as well. “Happens to the best of us.”

She adjusts the glasses and settles back into her seat, still smiling.

Rio lingers a moment. “Are you an artist?”

The woman raises an eyebrow like Rio just asked if she breathes air. 

“Well, you could say that.” 

Rio nods and the woman regards for a while. 

“Heart troubles?” 

“Sorry?” 

“People don’t come here at this hour just for the view, dear. They come because they’re either chasing a bit of inspiration, or trying to hush something in their chest that’s been making too much noise.”

Rio then understands what the older woman means. 

“Oh, no it’s not. It’s not like that.” then a pause. “I’m just having some trouble at work, that’s all.”

The older woman only gives her a look and hums. “And where do you happen to work?” she asks. Rio hesitates, unsure if she wants to burden a stranger with her troubles. “You know what they say, it’s easier to share things with strangers,” the woman adds, sensing her hesitation.

Rio sighs and sits on the far edge of the bench. There is a strange comfort in telling things to a stranger. But how was she supposed to explain her mess of a work life, let alone anything involving Agatha Harkness? “I work at a fashion magazine,” she says instead, keeping it vague.

“You? At a fashion magazine? Do you even like fashion?” the woman asks, all genuine surprise.

Rio considers being offended, but maybe that’s just how old people talk. Blunt and no sugarcoating. “I do get that a lot,” she says politely and chuckles. “I used to be an assistant to someone who’s basically a genius when it comes to fashion. Now I write for the same magazine, even if I still don’t know half the things I probably should.”

“Is that why you look so miserable?” the woman asks, but not unkind. She doesn’t wait for Rio to answer. “If you don’t love it, why are you still doing it?” she adds, squinting at her like the question genuinely baffles her. “Life’s too short to waste on things that don’t light you up, sweetheart. Trust me, I’d know.”

“I did leave. Or more like, I was forced to leave,” Rio says, rubbing the back of her neck. “But then my boss asked me to come back, and I couldn’t exactly say no to her. Which is stupid, but—”

“Does your boss know?” the woman hums.

“Does she know what?”

She glances at Rio’s name tag, her eyes landing on it with a faint smile. 

“That you like her, Rio.”

Rio blinks. “What?”

“So she doesn’t,” the older woman concludes. “And why haven’t you told her?”

Rio just stares at her. “Because I don’t—” She cuts herself off. No way was she about to explain to a complete stranger how her hormones basically snapped to attention whenever Agatha was within ten feet. It was already pathetic enough that she’d admitted it to herself.

“Oh, kid,” remarks the older woman. “I’ve lived long enough to know that look when I see it.”

Rio swallows. “What look?”

The woman smiles gently. 

“You seem like a smart young woman. I think you already know.” She sets her sketchbook aside and gives her knee a gentle pat. “So? What is it you’re so afraid of?”

Rio still wants to deny it, but what’s the point of lying to someone who doesn’t even know her, and somehow clocked her in seconds? 

“Well, it’s kind of complicated. Okay, not kind of. It’s really complicated. She’s not exactly the kind of person you can just say things to. Not without thinking she’ll walk away the second you do.” Her thumb runs along the seam of her sleeve. “Even though...lately, it kinda feels like maybe she wouldn’t.

The woman studies her for a moment, intrigued.

“Then why can’t you tell her? What’s the worst that can happen?”

Rio lets out a small, dry laugh. “My job, for starters.” 

But the older woman isn’t done. She tilts her head, like she’s piecing something together.

“But you said it kind of feels like maybe she wouldn’t. Why’s that?”

Rio hesitates, wondering if she should even mention the almost-kiss. Or the kiss that was more than almost. Or all the moments in between. But then she realizes how weird it would be to spill all that to a stranger who doesn’t even know her. So instead, she settles for the smaller, safer truths.

“I don’t know if I’m imagining it. But somehow she keeps showing up where I am. I mean, yeah, we work in the same building, but I think you get what I mean. And then she does these little things. Like remembering exactly how I take my coffee. Or asking me to work in her office. I’m really trying not to read into it. I really am. I don’t want to make something out of nothing. But she’s making it very hard.”

“Why is she making it hard? Did she ever hurt you?”

Rio shakes her head slowly. “No. Not exactly.”

The woman looks at her, eyes crinkling with something knowing. And she smiles, one of those smiles people have when they’ve lived through every shape of love and loss. “The thing is,” she drawls, “some people don’t realize they’ve left a mark on you until they finally see the shape of it when you walk away.”

It’s so vague and doesn’t seem to make sense for Rio, but she sits with that for a second.

“And what am I supposed to do with that?”

The woman shrugs. “That depends. Do you want her to see it? Or are you trying to forget it’s there?”

Rio doesn’t answer. She just allows the words to rest between them for a time before steering the conversation elsewhere. There is no need to burden this poor woman with her problems.

“You don’t exactly look like you’re supposed to be here either,” she quips instead, nodding at the woman’s sketchpad. “Let me guess, out hunting for inspiration?”

The woman cackles and shakes her head, like the words coming out of Rio’s clueless mouth are stupidly endearing. “I do find inspiration in the oddest places, yes,” she says, though she doesn’t seem too eager to elaborate, and Rio respectfully doesn’t press. 

The younger woman is just about to say something else when her phone buzzes. It’s a text from Darcy.

Better get your ass back here. Fortress Harkness wants everyone in the conference room in 30.

Rio sighs, slipping her phone back into her pocket. “I guess I have to go. Lunch break’s over,” she says, standing from the bench with a half-apologetic smile. “I hope you find whatever it is you’re looking for here, whatever kind of inspiration this place is supposed to give.”

The older woman nods, brushing invisible crumbs off her lap.

“Oh, I think I already did, kid.” 

By the time Rio gets to the conference room on the top floor, it’s already packed. Practically everyone from the pit is there, clustered around the long table or standing along the walls. She scans the room instinctively and spots Agatha right away, up front, pacing with a phone pressed to her ear. As per usual, whoever’s on the other end is clearly getting torn to shreds.

Melina sits up front too, arms crossed, watching the room like she’s already predicting bloodshed.

Rio weaves her way to the corner where Darcy, Bob, and Shuri have carved out a spot. Bob looks like he might pass out. “What’s going on?” she whispers, sliding into the seat next to him.

“Numbers,” he mutters, not even looking up as he squeezes one of his neon, squishy stress balls.

“What about it?” 

“Reader stats. Stark saw the latest analytics and apparently threw a fit.” 

Just then, Agatha ends her call with a vicious stab at her screen, jaw clenched so tight it’s a miracle her teeth don’t crack. She doesn’t so much as glance at Melina or the other senior editors beside her. Just stares straight ahead like she’s counting down to detonation.

Rio watches her from where she’s sitting at the far end of the room. And then, like she can feel someone staring, Agatha’s furious blue eyes land on her. For a second, something in her shoulders eases, and her face softens. Like seeing Rio is the only thing in the room not currently driving her insane. But it’s gone just as fast and the mask snaps back into place almost immediately.

Agatha clears her throat, strides to the front, and picks up the mic. She doesn’t even bother with pleasantries, and doesn’t wait for the room to settle down. “I’ll get straight to the point. Mr. Stark has raised concerns about Nocturne’s engagement numbers dropping compared to some rival magazines, and I’m not in the mood to waste anyone’s time with a slideshow about it.”

“But while that’s happening,” Agatha goes on coolly, “it just so happens we might also have the exact story that could pull our numbers back up. Has anyone here heard of Lilia Calderu?”

A ripple of recognition moves through the room, a few murmurs rising, but Rio just blinks and furrows her brows. “Who’s Lilia Calderu?” she whispers to Shuri.

Shuri twists sharply in her chair to stare at her. “Are you serious right now?”

Rio shrugs, palms up. “I don’t know, is this one of those things I was supposed to be born knowing?” 

“She’s practically a legend,” Shuri says, her voice dropping low so the people up front won’t hear. “Like, people in fashion call her the Oracle. They say she dreams of her designs before she even sketches them. Like fashion just visits her in her sleep.” Rio raises a brow, but Shuri’s not done. “She’s been MIA for fifteen years. Some say she retired in Italy. Others think she just lost it.”

Agatha eventually cuts through the chatter. 

“Lilia is a notoriously elusive designer who hasn’t given a single interview in over a decade. But it’s been confirmed she’s back in New York for the City Ballet Fall Fashion Gala. And that gives us a rare opening. If we can secure a sit-down with her, it won’t just be a strong feature, but it could also spike our numbers across print and digital. Though, we’ll need a standout pitch to cut through the noise. Especially since De Fontaine and her team at Oxe are after the same story. They’ve been chasing her for years. We cannot let them get there first.” 

She then turns to Melina. 

“Miss Vostokoff and I have already decided who’s taking the lead and which team’s handling it. She’ll call you into her office shortly. I expect a confirmed interview by the end of the week.”

From the back, Darcy lets out a quiet, almost pitying, “Well, good luck with whoever that is.”

Rio looks over at her. “Why?”

Darcy glances up from her nails. “Because whoever Melina sends might not even get past Lilia’s front door. Not if Lilia knows who Nocturne’s editor-in-chief is.”

Rio frowns. “What do you mean?”

“Rio, you really need to brush up on your company history, girl,” Darcy says with a teasing shake of her head. “The last person to land an exclusive with Lilia Calderu was none other than baby Agatha Harkness. Back when Satan’s mistress was still just one of the spawns,” she adds in a mock whisper. 

She leans in a bit, lowering her voice. “And let’s just say, the piece wasn’t exactly flattering. Might have even been what pushed Lilia off the grid. But to be fair, that article also made Agatha a name. Like, front page, overnight-sensation kind of thing. Can’t really blame her for riding that wave.”

Later that day, Rio’s back at the pit when she sees Mary Jane Watson walk out of Melina’s office. Of course it’s Mary Jane. One of Nocturne’s more seasoned fashion writers. She and her team were behind that Zara labor exposé and the Vogue burnout profile that ruffled all the right feathers.

Rio drops into her chair, still thinking about what Darcy said, about that article Agatha wrote.

The one that might’ve pushed some mystery designer to disappear for fifteen years. 

She turns to her computer and types in the right keywords. 

Not much comes up. No press photos. No profile pictures. Barely any interviews, and the few that do exist are written, nothing on video. It’s like Lilia had someone scrub the internet clean. All that’s left are runway photos with her name flashing faintly on an LED wall in the background.

What the hell did Agatha write to make someone just vanish?

She scrolls further, clicking through dead links and buried fashion archives, until her eyes finally land on an article, with a familiar name on the byline.

The Illusionist: Inside the Strange Genius of Lilia Calderu

By Agatha Harkness

Published: November 2010, Nocturne Magazine

“Genius,” they say, “walks the line between brilliance and madness.” In Lilia Calderu’s case, that line is an unpredictable, obscured runway, one that defies convention, logic, and any clear sense of direction.

To call Lilia Calderu a fashion designer is to call a thunderstorm “a bit of rain.” She’s unlike any other. She doesn’t conform to anything resembling a standard process. She dreams. Literally. She wakes up and scribbles designs on the backs of receipts, napkins, sometimes even on her own skin, she says. And the fashion world has long eaten it up with a gold spoon. Hungry for the myth, starved for meaning.

But what happens when the myth doesn’t hold?

Calderu greeted me barefoot in her Brooklyn brownstone, and she offered me rose tea and wore an embroidered robe. Coffee, I was told, was unwelcome in her home, something about caffeine and restless spirits. Her speech wandered the way her thoughts did: wispy, scattered, dipped in mysticism. She spoke of her fabrics like they were haunted, ghosts she was trying to stitch into submission.

The thing is, she is fascinating. There’s a reason the fashion world hailed her as a visionary. Her pieces are haunting. Ethereal. Unbelievably intricate. But beneath all the silk and smoke, you start to wonder: where does the art end, and where does the performance begin?

After nearly two hours of spiraling talk about past lives, moon cycles, and a dress that supposedly weeps when worn by the wrong person, the illusion began to fray. Strip away the mystique, and what’s left is a woman propped up by the industry’s endless appetite for the eccentric, the unknowable, the myth of the so-called genius that defies definition.

She is allergic to labels, but conveniently benefits from every one they give her: “witch, oracle, prophet in couture.” Calderu claims to hate stereotypes, but plays right into them when it suits the story. She is deeply private, yet willingly mythologized. She refuses the mainstream but hosts trunk shows in palazzos. She is somehow a contradiction, an illusionist who dares you to call her out on it.

And then there’s the question no one wants to ask: what happens when the magic runs out?

Sources close to her team describe missed deadlines, spontaneous design changes hours before shows, entire collections scrapped because of a ‘bad dream.’ One former assistant, who requested anonymity, said, “You don’t work for Lilia. You orbit her. And eventually, you burn out.”

In person, Calderu was charming. Kooky, but kind. It’s easy to fall under her spell, to believe in the mythos. But charm doesn’t build a legacy. And kindness alone can’t dress a model. At some point, a designer must descend from the clouds and face the ground.

What Calderu creates is beautiful, sometimes even extraordinary. 

But so are shooting stars. And both disappear just as quickly.

The industry needs more than dreams. It needs discipline, clarity, and, dare I say, reality. Perhaps it’s time we stopped chasing illusions and started asking: what, really, is worth worshipping? Because at the end of the day, even the most haunting magic trick still leaves you staring at an empty stage.

Rio finishes reading and just stares at the screen. She’s not sure what to think. But three things are clear.

First, no wonder Agatha Harkness is where she is now. How do you even write like that at twenty-three? 

Second, of course it was Agatha. Of course a twenty-three-year-old version of her walked into a legend’s house, called her kooky to her face (and to half a million readers), and somehow made the woman disappear from the whole industry for over ten years. Who else could pull that off and still sleep at night?

And third, most embarrassing of all, is the way Agatha writes. It’s kind of hot. Like, disturbingly hot. And Rio has no idea what it says about her that someone’s writing style is suddenly turning her on.

The piece is brutal. But there’s also something weirdly respectful in it. It’s honest and raw. Like Agatha wasn’t out to humiliate Lilia, but simply expose the cracks. Hold up a mirror and ask, “do you even see what you’ve become?” Which makes Rio wonder, what kind of mirror would Agatha hold up to her?

But before Rio can even begin to rewire her brain to deal with that thought, her phone lights up with a text from Jen: She summons you. 

Rio frowns, slips her phone into her pocket, and gets to her feet.

She finds Agatha mid-call in her office. “Yes, I know that,” she says, spotting Rio but continuing. “Oui, Natalia, je sais ce que je fais. Oui, I might have to call you back. Of course. Take care of yourself.” 

Rio stiffens as it sinks in who’s on the other end of the call. 

From the bit of French she caught, it’s not hard to guess. She pretends her heart didn’t just drop. 

So maybe Agatha and her blonde ex were back together. Why wouldn’t they be? They’re practically the perfect magazine power couple. Natalia’s exactly the type Agatha would proudly have on her arm, someone she wouldn’t mind being seen with.

Rio shifts on her feet, frowning. Why the hell did Agatha even call her up here?

The call ends but instead of speaking to Rio, or even looking her way, Agatha just sinks back into her chair and starts typing away on her laptop. So Rio clears her throat, hovering a safe distance away. 

“You called for me?” 

Agatha doesn’t look up. “Have you chosen a suit yet?”

Rio blinks. “A suit?”

“Yes. Didn’t Monica show them to you?”

“I have no idea what you’re talking about.”

Agatha exhales through her nose, still not looking up. “The suit you’ll be wearing to the Gala on Saturday.”

Rio suddenly remembers their whole floor had been strongly encouraged to attend the Gala. 

But she’d already decided in her head she wasn’t going. 

For very specific, totally rational reasons. Which absolutely had nothing to do with the fact that it was the New York City Ballet’s event. Or that someone from there just so happened to be someone she’s trying to avoid. And now, thanks to Agatha’s little reminder, Rio remembers exactly who that person is.

Why on earth would she willingly subject herself to being in the same room as Agatha and her blonde eye candy, breathing the same damn air, when she could be at home, horizontal on the couch, wrapped in a blanket, sad-boying to Boygenius, and eating chips straight from the bag?

“I’m not going,” she says flatly. 

Agatha finally looks up. “And why not? Didn’t your floor receive an invite?”

“We did. But it’s not even mandatory, so—”

“Do you want me to make it mandatory?”

Rio blinks. “I don’t even know what I’d do there.”

“It’s called networking,” Agatha says, like it physically pains her to explain the concept. “Many editors will be there. Journalists you might actually want to meet. Doesn’t that interest you?”

Rio hesitates. Why would Agatha care if she meets other editors? Unless…was this some elaborate way to make firing her again easier later? The audacity of this woman.

“I mean, it does. But—”

“Then you’re going,” Agatha cuts in. “There’s a selection of suits waiting for you downstairs. I already had Monica pull some options. Just go pick whatever you want.”

Rio squints at her. “Do the rest of the employees get this kind of special treatment too?” 

She knows it sounds bratty and ungrateful even to her own ears, but she can’t help it. 

Why was Agatha suddenly all up in her wardrobe like this?

“Only the ones who clearly need it,” her boss comments, giving Rio’s current choice of ensemble a slow once-over: rumpled navy tee, washed-out jeans, beat-up boots, and an oversized flannel that looks one dry cycle away from disintegrating.

Rio opens her mouth to fire back, but Agatha’s already dismissing her with a wave. 

“Now go on. Don’t keep Monica waiting. And tell her to come see me after.”

Rio would blame being fashionably late to the gala on the impromptu haircut Alice and Billy gave her earlier that day, not on the very real, very valid reason of not wanting to be there in the first place. It was just supposed to be a little trim, but Billy insisted she’d look cool with a short bob–wolfcut hybrid that would “frame her cheekbones.”

She actually thought about skipping altogether. But then she saw the outfit Monica had picked out for her: a deep burgundy Alexander McQueen suit with sharp lapels, a striped shirt underneath, and a tie that was already perfectly knotted. Backing out suddenly felt like a waste.

Monica has good taste. Of course, it comes with the job of being a stylist. But more importantly, Monica’s nice. She doesn’t deserve to be ghosted. Also, Rio’s not stupid enough to end up on her bad side.

Alice drives them in Billy’s mom’s car, because obviously, Rio can’t ride the subway in a suit that probably costs more than their monthly rent.

When she arrives, she walks through a handful of camera flashes. Not because anyone knows who she is, she’s just background noise to the rich and powerful inside, but someone must’ve thought she looked important. Still, she doesn’t stop for photos.

Her plan: find one person she actually wants to talk to, and cling. Her friends from the bullpen didn’t bother showing up (which, to be fair, neither would she have). 

But any coherent plan falls apart the second she steps into the venue and sees Agatha.

Agatha stands at the center of the room, half-turned, deep in conversation, but Rio’s eyes go straight to the gown she’s wearing. The bodice is fitted and sculpted, leaving her neck bare, while oversized puff sleeves drape over her shoulders like folded clouds. The color is nearly identical to Rio’s suit.

Did Agatha coordinate their outfits?

No. That’d be ridiculous. Absurd. Stupid.

But what’s even stupider is how Agatha’s blue eyes easily find hers across the room and Rio swears she sees the faintest twitch of a smile tug at her mouth.

However, what’s most stupid is the heat blooming in Rio’s ears when she also spots the blonde Agatha’s speaking with. Oh, great. Of course, Agatha’s blonde ballerina is here. Time to drown herself in champagne and pretend her heart isn’t the dumbest organ in her body.

“I didn’t expect to see you here.”

Rio turns, and there’s another blonde. This one is familiar in a more tolerable way.

“Hela.”

“Didn’t peg you for the type to actually show up to these things,” she greets, sipping her drink. “Especially now that you’re not her assistant anymore,” she adds, subtly nodding toward the woman in burgundy in the middle of the room. “Which, by the way, I’m still a little salty about, because somehow, you still didn’t actually leave her. But whatever. So, how’s the glamorous life of a fashion writer treating you?”

Rio smiles, a bit apologetic. 

“I’m actually really sorry about that. If it’s any consolation, I was seriously considering it, and I was grateful, really. But then things just shifted, and I couldn’t take it. Work’s been going well, though.” 

Surprisingly, writing-wise, it is going well. She’s still on the short, back-page stuff since she only started recently, but it’s still progress. Though, part of her wishes she was writing something else. Something grittier. But Hela doesn’t need to know that.

“I hope she’s worth it.” 

“What?”

“Agatha,” Hela says simply. “I just hope she’s worth whatever you’re putting on hold for yourself. People like her…they don’t make it easy to feel things for them. I just hope she doesn’t burn you out.”

Rio’s jaw goes slack. 

Has she really been that obvious? Heart eyes and all? Even people she barely knows are clocking it? Jesus. Is she really that transparent? Why does her stupid face have to give everything away?

“Oh please,” she scoffs. “I don’t have feelings for her.”

“You turned down a perfect shot at doing what you really want, just to work under her again…at her request. If that’s not feelings, I don’t know what is.” Hela takes a sip of her drink, while Rio wishes she could melt right into the marble floor from sheer embarrassment. “I’ve ghostwritten enough memoirs to recognize that look. You’ve got it bad, darling.”

Rio lets out a breath, rubbing the back of her neck. “It’s not like I’m putting things on hold for her, okay? Going back to Nocturne was my call. I thought maybe I’d try something different first, see what it’s like before chasing the stories I actually care about. Maybe it was a stupid move, but it’s mine to make.”

Hela hums, amused, and grabs a flute of champagne from a passing server. 

“Oh, Rio. You’re charming and foolish to a fault.” She hands it to her.

Rio chuckles, about to fire back, when another server approaches them. 

“Excuse me, Miss Vidal. Miss Harkness would like to speak with you.”

Rio’s brows pull together just as Hela says, “Well, looks like your ice queen’s calling.” She takes a sip of her drink, eyes darting toward Agatha. “I’ll let you go, then. But if you ever have a change of heart, my offer still stands. I can still put you in touch with my editor. Think of it as your safety net, for when all this inevitably blows up in your face.” She winks, then turns and glides off, drink in hand.

When Rio walks over, Agatha doesn’t waste time.

“So. Who was that?”

Rio pauses, glancing sideways at her. The blonde Agatha had been talking to earlier is nowhere in sight now, and it’s just the two of them. Jen’s nearby, but thankfully caught up in another conversation.

“Just someone I know,” Rio replies. “From Wall Street.”

“Wall Street?” Agatha lifts a brow. “Huh. And here I thought you were aiming higher.”

Rio blinks. Was that supposed to be an insult? A joke? A weird compliment in disguise? She doesn’t get the chance to figure it out when Agatha is already turning and walking ahead, nodding for her to follow.

“I heard Meredith from the Times is here,” she adds over her shoulder. “Bit of a jump, I know. But Jessica’s around too. She handles the weekend section. Do you want me to introduce you?”

Rio looks at her. “And why would you do that?”

“Didn’t I say this event is for networking? Or do you need a crash course on how that works?”

Rio knows how the whole networking game works. But what throws her off is Agatha being the one to push her toward it. “Why would you even want me talking to other editors?” she asks, frowning. “I mean, isn’t that kind of unethical? I currently work for you.” 

She doesn’t bother hiding how confused she is. None of this makes sense coming from Agatha.

“If that’s how you see it,” Agatha draws in that usual neutral tone, matching her face. “Then I worry about how far you’ll actually get. This industry doesn’t reward loyalty, Rio. You should learn the difference between that and opportunity, before it costs you both.”

Rio’s jaw tenses. Her blood starts to simmer.

“Of course you’d say that,” she mutters. “You always know how to twist things just to make it work in your favor, even if it means stepping over people to do it.”

It came out harsher than Rio meant, and she sees it land as Agatha’s face stiffen for a split second before she smooths it over like it didn’t hurt. Okay, perhaps Rio went too far. She’s just about to take it back, or at least say something a little less cruel, when someone else steps in front of them.

“Agatha Harkness. What a vision.”

They turn, and an older woman with silvery-streaked hair and a too-sharp smile is gliding toward them.

“Valentina,” Agatha greets tightly. “I could say the same.” They do the double-cheek kiss thing, all très chic, and Rio swears she can feel Agatha’s shoulders stiffen.

Both their smiles don’t even reach their eyes. 

“Though I’m surprised to see you here,” Agatha adds, tilting her head. “Weren’t you supposed to be in Shanghai? I heard Fashion Week there is always a little dull without you.”

Valentina clutches her chest like she’s touched. 

“Oh, and miss this? Never. Besides, I’ve got more pressing business here in New York. Our numbers are looking fabulous, if I do say so myself. Couldn’t really stay away.”

Agatha swallows whatever profanity is on her tongue. “Of course. Quite the stellar issue you’ve got this month. Let’s just hope it’s not a fluke, and that it actually lasts. Readers these days can be so fickle.”

That hits something in Valentina. 

“Oh, it’ll last,” she replies, all sugar and threat. “And I’m very committed to making sure it does.”

Agatha lets out a too-sweet laugh. “Aren’t we all?”

Valentina matches it, plastic and tight.

“Well. Ciao, chérie. I need to make a few calls. My assistant left the studio’s lookbook in Milan, can you believe it? Sometimes I wonder how civilization survived this long with so many idiots walking around.” 

And just like that, she spins off, already tapping at her phone. 

Agatha exhales once Valentina’s out of sight. “God, I need a drink.”

Almost an hour passes, and Rio stays planted near the entrance, well out of Agatha’s orbit, who, at some point, apparently decided to drink more than necessary. 

Not that she’s sloppy about it. She still moves with the same cool elegance of someone who’d never been caught drunk in public. But her cheeks are definitely pinker than usual, and Rio can’t help but notice. 

Should she stop their boss from downing another glass? Then again, isn’t that Jen’s job? Or maybe the job of her ballerina girlfriend, who’s suddenly nowhere in sight.

“When I had a feeling that day wasn’t the last time I’d see you, I didn’t think it’d be this soon.”

Rio turns and sees the familiar older woman from the park.

“Hey. Hi. You’re here,” she blurts, a little caught off guard.

The woman lets out a warm laugh. “Oh, sweetheart. There’s nowhere else I’d rather be.” 

Before Rio can say anything, there’s a sudden ripple in the room. People start looking their way, and camera flashes go off like fireworks aimed in their direction. Rio blinks, thrown off for a second, and gets the creeping feeling she’s missed something important.

“Lilia, over here!” a photographer shouts, and Rio’s jaw drops.

“Wait. Lilia? You’re Lilia Calderu?”

Lilia laughs again. “Oh, you better close that mouth, kid. You don’t want them snapping photos like that. Trust me, it’d cost you a huge fortune to get them taken down,” she says with a wink. “And I’m sorry I didn’t introduce myself sooner. I just figured you’d catch on eventually.”

Rio snaps her jaw shut. “I, uh, God, I feel so stupid.” 

“Oh, don’t be. Happens to the best of us,” Lilia chuckles again, and Rio can’t help but smile at hearing her own words echoed back at her. “So, I’m guessing you’re not here alone?”

Rio shakes her head. “No, I’m not alone,” she says, then quickly realizes who she’s actually with, and what that might mean to Lilia. Oh god. This woman’s probably going to hate her now, isn’t she? “I’m actually here with my boss,” she adds, trying not to sound too guilty about it.

“Your boss?” Lilia repeats, and there’s a coruscation of knowing in her eyes. 

And because the universe is a cruel little shit, her boss materializes right then.

“Rio,” Agatha throws out as she steps up beside them, smelling like champagne and lavender. “You didn’t mention you knew Lilia.” Her eyes are all on the older woman now. That same tone she used with Valentina is back. “The one and only. Nice to see you back, Miss Calderu. How’s Sicily this time of year?”

Lilia ignores her and turns to Rio instead, brows raised. “ She’s your boss?”

Rio nods slowly, throat suddenly dry.

Lilia’s smile fades entirely. What’s left looks a lot like disappointment, maybe even a little betrayal. She looks at Rio like she’s trying to make sense of something, and whatever it is, it makes Rio want to disappear into the floor.

Agatha watches them both like she’s already done the math. “I take it I’ve come up in conversation,” she chirps, and where she’s getting this much confidence from, Rio has no idea. “All flattering, I hope?”

Lilia’s smile returns, but this time it’s cold and a little disbelieving. She turns fully to Agatha. 

“Oh, you wouldn’t believe it, Harkness.”

Monday rolls around, and Rio’s juggling four cups of coffee and tea, doing her best not to spill any when Mary Jane Watson suddenly bursts out of the elevator, shoulders shaking and bawling her eyes out.

Rio nudges Darcy with her elbow as she passes a cup. “What happened to her?”

“Lilia, the Oracle, turned her down. Didn’t even let her inside her house. Slammed the door right in her face and left her standing in the rain for hours,” Darcy says, taking her drink. “Told you, whoever gets stuck with that task is doomed. Even picture-perfect MJ never stood a chance.”

“I heard she even called her a hack and a washed-up gossip columnist,” Bob mumbles, clutching his cup. “And, um, I think Agatha might’ve said something even worse just now. Poor Mary Jane.”

Rio winces. She suddenly remembers the look on Lilia’s face when she came eye to eye with Agatha after all those years. Yeah, poor Mary Jane. She indeed never stood a damn chance.

“Wait. Is Agatha firing her?”

“She wouldn’t be crying like that if she wasn’t,” Shuri mutters, already typing away. “Jesus, I hope I don’t get that assignment. I actually like my job.”

Rio looks over to where Mary Jane is silently shoving her things into a cardboard box. Her mascara’s halfway down her cheeks. They weren’t exactly close, but Rio still feels bad. She’s about to say something to her when Melina appears at their cubicle.

“Rio. What are you working on right now?”

She scrambles to minimize the browser tabs and pulls up her draft. 

“Uh, I’m working on a piece about the underground designers who crashed the Faeber Runway. Still on the first draft. Just need one more decent quote before—” 

“Drop it and give it to Bob,” Melina cuts her off. “That alright with you, Bob?”

Bob nods a little too fast. His cheeks go pink. “Y-Yeah. Sure.” 

Then Melina turns back to Rio. “Agatha wants to see you. Come with me.”

All three of her coworkers look up at once, eyes wide.

“Did she say why?”

“Did Jesus say how he turned water into wine?” Melina deadpans.

Fair enough. Agatha usually makes her own calls anyway. Half the people who work with her can’t even tell what the hell’s going on in that mind of hers.

Rio follows Melina to the elevator, and they ride in silence to the top floor. When they reach Agatha’s office, the woman herself is standing at the window, back to the door. She doesn’t turn until they’re inside.

“There you are,” Agatha says. Then she turns to Melina. “You can leave us, Melina. Thank you.”

Melina only gives Agatha a look Rio can’t quite read before nodding and walking out. 

Whatever it was, Rio doesn’t like it one bit.

Agatha turns back to the window. 

“Do you want something to drink? Water? Coffee? I can have Jen bring your usual tea, if you’d like.”

Rio shakes her head. “I’m good. I just had one downstairs.”

Agatha nods but doesn’t say anything for a moment, just keeps watching the city outside.

This isn’t going to be one of those conversations, is it? Where Rio just stands around waiting for Agatha to finally talk. So she lets out an impatient sigh. “Why am I here, Agatha?”

Her boss’s shoulders rise and fall in a slow breath. 

“Lilia agreed to an exclusive interview with the magazine.”

Rio thinks back to Mary Jane bawling downstairs. 

“And what’s that got to do with me? Didn’t Mary Jane already—?”

“Miss Watson has formally dropped the assignment, and her position at the company,” Agatha says, finally getting to the point as she turns to face her. “Lilia has agreed to grant Nocturne the exclusive, but only under one condition — that you handle the interview and write the piece. No one else. Just you.”

Rio blinks. “Me? Why me?”

“It seems you’ve made quite an impression on her, and from my experience, that’s no easy feat. But somehow, you managed it, whatever it is you did. And now the magazine has to follow her terms. Even if you haven’t done a piece like this before, I have no choice but to assign it to you.”

Rio’s mouth goes dry. Agatha’s right. She’s never written anything like this. And she’s not stupid. She knows this is basically a world exclusive. A story that could tip the scales for the magazine’s reputation.

Agatha takes a step closer, eyes on Rio like she’s trying to say more than what the words will let her. 

“This is important, Rio. Really important. To the magazine, and to me. And I’m not trying to dump any pressure on you, I swear I’m not. And if I had any other option, I wouldn’t—” she quickly stops herself. “But maybe Lilia’s terms are weirdly working in our favor, because if there’s anyone here I trust to pull this off, it’s you.” She hesitates, bites her bottom lip, then tries again. “I just need to know, do you think you can do this? Can I count on you?”

Agatha’s words still echo in Rio’s head as the company car pulls up outside Lilia Calderu’s brownstone, four days later. 

Rio had done all the research she could: dug through old interviews, combed through dusty archives, even pulled a quote from a fashion spread in Vogue Italia that Lilia probably gave in passing back in the nineties. Darcy, Bob, and Shuri had all helped, though not without giving her a look before she headed out. The kind that said good luck and you're gonna need it without saying a word.

But really, what could go wrong? Lilia had seemed kind enough at the park. Warm, even. Okay, sure, maybe she hadn’t known at the time that Rio worked for Agatha, but would that really change things? 

Alice had offered two theories over beer and cold pizza the night before. One: Lilia was out for revenge. Against Nocturne and by extension, Agatha Harkness. And Rio, unfortunately, was just going to be collateral damage. But Rio didn’t buy it. Lilia didn’t strike her as the vengeful type. 

Which left her with theory two, the one Rio is now clinging to for dear life: that maybe Lilia had simply enjoyed her company that day in the park, and that maybe she’d seen something in Rio that made her want Rio to be the one to do this interview and write this piece, and no one else.

“I’d offer you coffee, but I can’t in good conscience serve you anything that tastes like motor oil,” Lilia says with a dry smile as they settle into the living room, teacup in hand. “Coffee here in America has never quite suited my taste.” She then gestures for Rio to relax. “Make yourself comfortable. I’ve got about an hour before I’m dragged into another meeting. Seems like a lot of people caught wind that I’m not staying in New York past the weekend, so they’re trying to squeeze in whatever they can.”

“You’re not staying?” Rio asks as she pulls her notepad from her bag.

“Did you really think I came back to New York for good, like everyone else?” Lilia laughs, shaking her head. “My life’s not here anymore, kid. I only attended the gala because my granddaughter’s one of the newest ballerinas. She’s always been a beautiful dancer, our piccola cigno , even when she was little. Left Italy to chase her dreams. How could I say no to that?”

Rio nods and flips through her notepad of questions. She’s just about to speak when Lilia beats her to it. 

“Oh, sweetheart, put that notepad away. I’m not answering anything you’ve written there. Not if you want this interview to actually happen. I want this to feel like a real conversation, like what we had at the park. That wasn’t so hard, was it?”

“I, uh, I’m sorry. Of course, we can do that,” Rio stammers, unable to meet her interviewee’s eyes. 

For Pete’s sake, she’s about to screw this up big time. 

She can even practically see Agatha’s disappointed look from miles away.

“You’re not nervous, are you?” Lilia asks, watching her closely, but not unkindly.

Rio’s eyes snap up. 

“What? No. I mean…” She groans and gives up. There’s no point in pretending when it’s written all over her face. “Okay, yes. To be honest, I’m really nervous. I haven’t done anything even close to this before. I mean, I did interviews back in college, but those were with student council officers, alumni who ran cafés, local politicians, labor organizers. You, on the other hand, are world-famous. And I didn’t even realize who you were at first, which makes me feel like the biggest idiot alive.”

She watches Lilia’s mouth twitch but she blabbers on. 

“Why did you even pick me, Lilia? And why our magazine, considering…” She trails off.

“So you’ve read the infamous article,” Lilia supplies. “The one your amore so mercilessly wrote.”

Rio flinches. “Agatha is not my—” She cuts herself off and sighs. There’s no point in arguing either. “I did. I read it. I also had to, so I could prepare myself for this. And, well, curiosity got the best of me.”

“Oh, stop that. Don’t look so guilty. Curiosity’s what keeps the world turning, kid. The rest just sit around waiting to be fed,” Lilia explains vaguely. Then she looks at Rio like she’s figuring her out. “So, since you have read it, what did you think of the article?” 

Rio looks back at her, puzzled. 

Wasn’t she supposed to be the one doing the interview, not the other way around? 

Still, she clears her throat.

“I’ve actually been thinking about it, and I think it was brutal,” she drawls. “Brutal in a way only Agatha can be.” Lilia nods and Rio hesitates, but pushes forward. “But if you’re asking what I really think of it...I also think it was honest. The kind of honesty only someone like her is capable of. And perhaps, someone bold enough to say it to a person who actually needs to hear it.”

Rio questions whether starting the interview with such honesty was a wise idea. She sees Lilia's expression change into something unreadable, brows up, lips slightly open, and braces herself to be kicked out of the brownstone at any time. But then Lilia gives her a knowing nod.

“I never actually liked that article,” she says. “Read it once. Couldn’t bear to read it again.”

Rio tries not to visibly sweat, though her underarms are dangerously close to betrayal.

“But maybe that’s just human nature. We don’t like the truth when it’s thrown in our faces,” she continues, taking a sip of her tea. “What Agatha wrote, brutal, as you called it, made me realize there’s more to life than the glitter and noise of fashion. That world…it was very exciting, yes, but it was also an illusion. At least, for me. They called me the Oracle, yet I couldn’t even see my own marriage falling apart, or my children slipping away from me,” she says somberly. 

“I had my time in fashion. A long, glorious run. But Agatha, bless her sharp tongue, reminded me that maybe it’s time I did just as well in the other aspects of my life. And now, I finally am.”

Rio just stares at her, trying to catch up with everything she’s just heard. But Lilia goes on. 

The interview, which was only supposed to last an hour, ends up stretching into the rest of the afternoon.

At some point, Lilia cancels all her scheduled meetings and tells Rio to stay. She gives her a full tour of the brownstone, four floors and nearly six thousand square feet of fashion history and personal relics, then leads her through photo albums she’s had for decades. 

They’re stacked in drawers, lined on bookshelves, tucked behind glass cases. Page after page of Lilia’s life, with her running commentary full of warmth, bite, and all the little details only she would remember. 

She talks about her two children, both now living quiet lives back in Sicily. One of her grandchildren even calls during the tour, and Rio gets a glimpse of the villa Lilia has in the Italian countryside: sunlit, peaceful, and nothing like the world she once ruled, but fitting for the woman she’s become.

What Rio also gets to see are Lilia’s old sketches, designs she never had the chance to bring to life during her reclusive years in Italy. Some are delicate and romantic, others bold and strange in ways Rio wouldn’t have expected. She tells Lilia how stunning they are, how full of feeling, and admits that even though she’s never been a fan of skirts, she’d wear one of them in a heartbeat.

Since Lilia hasn’t allowed photographers into her home, she lets Rio take photos on her phone, on the condition that nothing unflattering makes it to print. Now Rio can only hope the editors back at Nocturne can turn her iPhone shots into something worthy of the pages they will publish.

It’s already dark outside when Lilia walks her out after a delicious dinner, the company car waiting at the curb. “I might want a word with your beloved tyrant of a boss before the piece goes to print. Can you arrange that for me, Rio?” she asks as they step outside.

“Of course. I’ll let her know,” Rio says, tucking her hands into her coat pockets against the chilly air. She’s just thanked Lilia for the interview and the meal when the older woman calls her back.

“Let me be honest, kid. Don’t let it get to your head, but it’s rare for me to like someone this quickly. But it also doesn’t take much for me to know you’re a good egg. I gave your magazine this exclusive, mainly because of that. Because of you. Make sure they know that. And you should know too, you’ve earned whatever comes from this. Maybe even more. And fine, maybe a smidge because of Agatha, though I still think she’s the biggest pain in the ass this side of the Atlantic.”

She waves a hand, like brushing off lint, while Rio just stands there trying to process.

“But if someone like you ended up falling for her, maybe she’s not all storm and undertow after all. Just be careful, though. Sometimes the thing you think is anchoring you is actually the thing pulling you under. Don’t let that happen to you. And if she really feels the same way, she won’t let it. She’ll let you swim.”

It’s creeping past nine when Rio steps out of the company car, her bones tired but her heart electric. 

The day had gone better than she could’ve expected, from something that started with nerves and ended with laughter, tea, dinner, and someone she hadn’t expected to like so damn much. 

She mumbles thanks to the driver, still grinning as she turns toward the apartment, only to stop short as a familiar black car rolls up to the curb.

“About time,” drawls a familiar voice as the tinted window slides down. “I was starting to think you’d been held hostage by that wispy old witch. What’d she do, start the story from the day she was born? Javier’s circled your neighborhood so many times he could probably give guided tours by now.”

Rio squints at the car like it might be a hallucination. “God forbid someone actually enjoyed my company.” She crosses her arms. “What the hell are you even doing here, Agatha? Is this a new hobby of yours? Pulling drive-by check-ins on your employees?”

“Just get in,” Agatha demands, suddenly clipped and imperious as ever.

“I’m actually kind of beat. Can we just do this tomorrow?”

“I said get in.”

Rio stares her down, weighing at least a hundred different ways to tell her where to shove that bossy tone. She’s halfway through picking the juiciest Italian curse she learned from Lilia when Agatha says something that stops her cold. Two words she’s never heard come out of her mouth in the same breath.

“Please, Rio.”

“Where are you even taking me?” Rio complains as she sinks into the backseat beside Agatha, keeping the usual few inches of distance between them. “I’m not kidding about being tired. Whatever this is, please make it quick. I had a really long day and all I want is to sleep in an actual bed.”

“I know,” Agatha agrees calmly. “That’s why I’m bringing you to my estate in Scarsdale. We’re taking the team there tomorrow, and you’ll be writing Lilia’s feature from there.”

“I’m sorry, what?”

“Did you really think I’d risk leaving you and that exclusive sitting in your apartment, just waiting to fall into the wrong hands?” Agatha stares at her and smiles. That rare, full smile of hers. It’s the kind that says she’s thoroughly enjoying the confusion written all over Rio’s face. “I’d never let that happen.”

Rio squints at her. “I still don’t get the exact reason why I have to write it at your estate,” she says, dragging out the last word and pretending to gag at how rich it sounds.

“I have a feeling Valentina’s already sniffed out that we landed Lilia’s exclusive,” Agatha says simply. “And I don’t want her hovering around you for it. Now, is that enough reason?”

“Why would you even worry? Don’t you trust me?”

Agatha doesn’t even hesitate.

“Of course I trust you. It’s the people who’ll be trying to get close to you that I don’t.”

The rest of the drive passes with Rio holding out her phone and Agatha hunched slightly toward it, scrolling through the photos Rio had taken earlier. 

She talks her boss through each one, where it was taken, what Lilia had said, and how some of the shots might actually work as cover options with a little help from Nocturne’s layout team. 

But what Rio’s really enjoying is the look on Agatha’s face, wide-eyed, lips parting every now and then in something close to awe, completely taken by the photos, especially the ones of Lilia’s unseen and unreleased designs, carefully laid out like memories across a worktable. Rio watches her with a kind of smug delight. It’s not every day you get to see Agatha Harkness look like a kid in a candy store.

Rio had half-joked that Lilia’s designs were basically Taylor Swift’s vault tracks in fashion form, only to be met with a blank stare from Agatha, like she’d just been spoken to in Morse code. 

Rio had nearly choked from laughing. Of course her nearly forty-year-old, chronically offline, pop culture-dodging boss wouldn’t know the sacred language of Swiftie lore.

It doesn’t escape Rio how easily they’ve slipped back into the familiar intimacy they had before the firing, the arguments in the streets, and all the awkward, avoidant stares. Whatever resentment or leftover anger she still has toward her boss is suddenly gone. And maybe she should hate herself for that. But right now, hearing Agatha laugh and seeing her smile, Rio doesn’t even care.

“She really said we can publish these?” Agatha grabs the phone from Rio and scrolls to another image. Her eyes widen. “Why the hell is Lilia keeping all these designs in her archives? Oh, I would kill to wear this.” She’s referring to a sharp, architectural piece with a plunging neckline and sculpted shoulders. 

“She signed the release forms and gave us full permission to publish all the photos I took, as long as nothing unflattering makes it to print. She also asked for physical copies once the story’s out. And she also wants a private word with you before it runs.”

Agatha doesn’t look away from the screen. “Did she say why?”

“Nope. Guess you’ll have to call her.”

“I’ll have Jen set that up.”

She swipes again and pauses. The next photo shows Lilia holding one of her old, unreleased designs, looking at it like she’s just remembered a part of herself. But instead of looking sad, she’s smiling, bright and real. There’s also something unguarded about her in the picture, something almost youthful. Like the years had peeled back for a second. 

“This is the one. This should be the cover,” Agatha says, touching the screen. “It might take a bit of work to get the quality print-ready, but our editors can work magic when they want to.” She lingers on the photo, then turns to Rio with a soft, almost bashful smile. “But these are beautiful, Rio. I hope you know just how incredible your work is. You should be really proud.” 

Rio is thankful it’s sort of dark inside the car, otherwise, Agatha would definitely see how red her face is from blushing. She takes the phone back from her, their fingers brushing for a second too long before she slips it into her bag. But when she looks up, Agatha is still watching her with that same proud look. Then something passes over her face, like a sudden, loud thought, and she quickly looks away.

Rio, who’s learned the language of Agatha’s tells and micro-reactions, squints at her.

“What is it?” 

“Nothing.” Agatha shakes her head. “Just a thought. I’ll tell you once we’re at my place.”

Agatha’s Scarsdale estate turns out to be a modern two-story house, maybe four thousand square feet, with sleek black-framed windows and a pale gray brick exterior that glows under the porch lights. The front garden is a patch of lawn wide enough to host a wedding, and a few Japanese maples scattered like curated brushstrokes. 

It’s simpler and a bit smaller than Agatha’s family estate in Morris County, but Rio still knows she can’t even begin to guess how much this all costs.

“The guest room’s at the far end of the hall. That’s where you’ll be,” Agatha explains as she leads the way through a quick tour. “My room is on the opposite end.” Rio immediately frowns at that. It’s not a long walk, exactly, but it feels too far for her liking. But she doesn’t say anything.

“If you need anything later, just knock,” Agatha adds without looking back. She pauses at a linen closet halfway down the hall and opens it. “Extra blankets in here, it gets very cold in the early mornings. There are toiletries in the bathroom. Towels. Hairdryer’s in the cabinet under the sink. And I already had my housekeeper leave a few sets of clothes on the bed. That is…if you don’t mind wearing some of mine.”

Rio pauses for half a beat, her brain snagging on the image of her in Agatha’s clothes. “I don’t mind,” she replies. Then adds, with just enough bite to hide the flutter in her chest, “Though if you had let me pack earlier and, I don’t know, not basically kidnapped me and dragged me here, that wouldn’t be necessary.”

Agatha just rolls her eyes and keeps walking.

“The whole team’s getting here tomorrow at ten. You’ll have enough time to rest before the madness starts. And make no mistake, it will be utter madness.” She stops at the end of the hall, turning to face Rio. “I’ve put the entire print schedule on hold for this piece. That means every department is waiting on you. Including me. You get to call the shots now, Rio. But you’re on a very inflexible deadline. You still think you can handle that?”

Rio takes a breath. The nerves are still there, sure, but so is something else. A buzz in her chest that feels a lot like readiness. She already knows how she wants to shape the piece. She can feel the bones of it settling into place. She’s never written a feature on someone before, especially not someone in fashion, but she can be passionate and perceptive if she puts her mind to it. 

And that interview with Lilia had been one of the most meaningful, and unexpectedly enjoyable, interviews she’d ever done. It did something to her. Loosened a knot she hadn’t even realized was there. And now, all she wants is to chase that feeling. Put every bit of it into words.

“I’ve got it,” she says. “Just make sure the coffee and tea keep coming tomorrow.” 

Agatha gives her another one of her rare smiles and opens the guest room door. 

“Here you are. I better leave you to it,” she exhales. But just before turning to leave, she adds, “Rio, I hope you know how big this is for the magazine. And how much of that is because of you. De Fontaine can shove her numbers up her smug little binder once your piece drops. I honestly can’t wait to see her face if she even thinks about competing.” She steps back. “Anyway, if you need me, I’ll be downstairs.”

Rio watches her disappear down the hall toward the stairs, still stuck on that weirdly soft little paroxysm in Agatha’s piercing blue eyes. 

It might actually be the happiest she’s looked since Rio came back to Nocturne. Like something dangerous in her had finally lit up again. The thrill of the kill. 

And, annoyingly, Rio finds that stupidly attractive.

Rio takes a quick shower, letting the hot water wash off the long day. After, she slips into one of Agatha’s matching flannel pajama sets. They look barely worn, but they still carry that faint lavender scent that clings to Agatha. She blow-dries her short hair, then gathers what she can into a half-hearted ponytail before heading downstairs, the sleeves of the pajama top brushing past her knuckles as she goes.

She finds no sign of Agatha. Maybe she’s upstairs getting ready for bed or in the shower. So Rio wanders into the living room. It’s all too tidy but a little colder than she expected, probably because the fireplace isn’t lit. Shelves line the far wall, filled with books. Some titles she recognizes, others she doesn’t. 

On top of the cabinet under the window are framed pictures, but not the kind you’d normally see in someone’s house. There are no baby photos of Agatha, no family portraits.

Most of the photos are with people from the industry, smiling at cover launches, clinking glasses at packed events, caught mid-laugh in some dimly lit office. 

There’s one of her as a fresh-faced intern at a publishing house called Coven Press, then a few more from her early days as a writer at Nocturne. And finally, several with Stark, but this time with her name on the masthead: Editor-in-Chief.

Rio takes it all in. Agatha had come a long way, despite her filthy rich background, despite the easy assumptions people probably made about her. And unlike the usual nepotism babies Rio knew, Agatha had actually worked her ass off to get to the top. 

She fought her way up, earning every inch of it.

Then it dawns on her, how much trust Agatha’s putting in her now. How she hasn’t even heard the full interview. How she’s only seen the photos. How Rio isn’t even sure Agatha’s ever read a single thing she’s written. And yet somehow, she believes Rio can do it.

Her chest aches at the thought, and a sudden rush of sadness and something bitter creeps in before she can stop it. She scowls, dragging her hands down her face. She should be celebrating. So why does it feel like something’s sinking in her gut? What the hell is going on with her?

Rio sinks into the couch and pulls out her phone, scrolling through the quotes from Lilia she’d jotted down in her notes app. When she’d typed them out, she hadn’t expected the night to bend into whatever this was now. But then it hits her, Agatha had been saying it all along, in the way she looked at her, in every little thing she said since the car ride and the second they walked through her door.

She got the job at Nocturne hoping that one day, Agatha would give her a recommendation, something that could get her into any publication she wanted. 

Rio isn’t dumb. With Lilia’s story right in front of her, she knows this could be her ticket out. Once she finishes the article, she could finally leave Nocturne and go after whatever dream she had before Agatha came into the picture.

And she knows Agatha knows that too. 

That’s probably why she looked a little weighed down back at the office when she gave Rio the assignment. But she still gave it to her, knowing it might mean letting her go once it’s all done.

A sound pulls her out of her thoughts, and when she looks up, the very conundrum at the center of her tangled mess of feelings is standing in the threshold, watching her. 

She’s already changed into an adorable set of Gucci pajamas, holding a glass of red wine in one hand and a black folder in the other.

“So,” Agatha says, “you finally figured it out.”

Rio doesn’t answer. She just watches as Agatha walks over and takes the seat across from her.

“I knew I had to let you go the second Lilia called and said she wanted you to write her piece. I’m not even sure what really got into me, bringing you here. Perhaps part of it was I wanted to secure the exclusive, but mostly, I think I just wanted to see you one last time, like this…by my side.”

“You know, I don’t even have to quit,” Rio says quickly, trying to piece her thoughts back together. “I mean, sure, I’ve got other doors open for me now, I know that. But I could still be working for you—” 

“Rio.” Agatha stops her. “Why did you take the job as my assistant months ago? And please don’t say it was for my warm and charming personality, we both know you had no clue who I was before you applied.”

Rio gives a weak laugh, then looks down. “Because I wouldn’t have picked Drive Monthly even if someone had a gun to my head, or hell, a knife to my throat.”

“Cute.” Agatha mirrors her laugh. “But I’m being serious. Be honest. You already answered this once, if I remember right.”

Rio sighs. 

“It just made sense at the time, okay? Working for you looked really great on paper. It’s a solid line on my resume, and Nocturne’s one of the best. I figured it wouldn’t hurt to try it out, even if it was just for a year.”

“Is that it?” 

“I also hoped I’d get on your good side and maybe earn a recommendation, though I found out later that’s extremely rare, since you barely ever give those.” 

“All my employees hope for that. But why did you even want mine?”

“Because you’re Agatha freaking Harkness. Your name’s like a press pass to anywhere. If I had your reference, I could land a writing job at The Times, or pretty much anywhere I wanted.”

Agatha nods slowly. “Exactly. Which is why I’m telling you something I’ve never told anyone who worked for me before.” She leans in. “You no longer need my name, Rio. And you don’t need me.”

No. I do.

The words hover on Rio’s tongue, but she swallows them back. 

She turns Agatha’s words over in her head. Is she right? Yes, probably. Why would Rio even go back to writing about things she barely cares about, when what she really wants is to chase stories that truly matter to her, to do the kind of journalism she’s dreamed of since she was a kid?

The truth is brutal and unpleasant, worse than getting fired right then and there. Sure, she always meant to leave the magazine eventually. But now the thought of not seeing Agatha anymore, of not being in her orbit, of not being around her all the time, hurt more than she wanted to admit.

She tries to smile, but it barely holds, and she looks away. 

Agatha sets down the folder and a pen on the table between them. 

“I had Jen draw this up earlier. It outlines how you’ll move forward with Lilia’s story. I went through it myself to make sure you have full creative control. The final edits and what gets published are completely up to you. You can have a lawyer review it if you want, but for now, take your time reading through it.”

Rio flips through the pages, scanning the legal terms. The agreement grants her full ownership and copyright of the article, even if she parts ways with Nocturne. The payment also extremely exceeds her expectations, enough to give her a real shot if she decides to go freelance afterward.

And this is exactly what Rio’s been wanting all her life, isn’t it? It’s the most sensible thing anyone can do when they’re finally, finally chasing their dreams.

Sometimes the thing you think is anchoring you is actually the thing pulling you under. Don’t let that happen to you. 

She looks down at the pen and the contract, fully aware that Agatha gave it to her knowing exactly what’s inside and what it all means. It seems Agatha has quietly taken care of everything for Rio, making sure the road ahead is hers to choose.

And if she really feels the same way, she won’t let it. She’ll let you swim.

Rio picks up the pen.

“Are you really sure about this?” Agatha asks.

There’s something in her voice that makes Rio stop and look up. She’s seen that look before, right after closing a deal with an investor or winning an argument against Stark or some other hardheaded shareholder, when Agatha lights up with pride and that unstoppable fire. But this time, there’s something else underneath, like an unspoken sadness. 

Could it be that even her boss, who everyone swears is Satan’s mistress, might actually feel a little hurt? Would she even miss Rio as much as Rio’s going to miss her?

Rio gives herself a mental slap. She’s clearly imagining things. Why would Agatha miss her, after letting her go once and now doing it all over again? No. Agatha Harkness doesn’t miss people. The thought almost makes her laugh, but she shoves it down.

She skims the contract one last time, nods at Agatha, then signs.

She will miss her.

The rest of the night stretches in the living room, scattered with bits of conversation. 

Rio talks loosely about the tone she already has in mind for the piece, and how for once, she’s actually excited for people to read it. 

Somewhere between that, she also drifts into stories about Lilia’s time in Sicily: how she allegedly scammed someone out of his Vespa, and started a limoncello business with a nun. None of it had anything to do with fashion, and definitely not what you’d expect from someone like Lilia Calderu.

At one point, as their knees nearly touch on the couch, Agatha laughs and says, “I still don’t get it. How someone that private, basically a hermit for fifteen years, just opens up to you and starts telling absurd stories like that after two meetings. Not many people in this industry have that kind of pull and charm. I didn’t even get that close when I interviewed her. You’ve got a gift, Rio. No doubt about it.”

Rio, who’s never quite known what to do with compliments, especially the rare, genuine kind from her boss, keeps her eyes on her glass and hides the heat rising to her cheeks by gripping it a little too tightly.

“I don’t know about that. Maybe Lilia’s just easy to talk to. Turns out she’s kind of a professional rambler.” She takes a sip of the wine. It’s rich, velvety, and tasting unmistakably like wealth. “Jesus. I think you’ve officially ruined beer and cheap liquor for me because nothing else is ever going to come close.”

Agatha swirls her wine. 

“Consider it a rite of passage. You’ll be drinking more of that once you start landing bigger writing jobs, whatever publication you set your sights on. After Lilia’s story drops, people won’t just be knocking at your door. They’ll be chasing you. And not just editors, either. You might not know this, but a lot of very attractive women in the industry get something close to an orgasm from a smartly written piece.”

Rio almost chokes, sputtering into her glass. “You’re not even a hundred percent sure how the article’s going to turn out. What if it’s not even that smartly written, like you put it?”

“Oh, I’ve never been sure of anything in my life.” She smiles at her again, and maybe it’s the wine talking, but it takes a lot of effort for Rio not to lean in and kiss her. “But I meant what I said. After this exclusive, there’ll be a line just for you. And more than a few of them will want you in their bed within twenty-four hours of it going live. You’ll have options laid out like a buffet. All you’ll have to do is pick.”

“Well, I don’t want women lining up for me,” Rio admits, setting her glass down. “And besides, I already know who I want in my bed. I’m just not sure if that person feels the same.” It comes out so honest, so bare, that the silence that follows feels thick and too loud.
