She instantly regrets letting the thought slip. “I mean, realistically, with the work I’ve got ahead of me, I probably won’t be in anyone’s bed anytime soon anyway,” she adds, with a small, self-conscious smile.

Rio immediately catches Agatha’s expression of surprise. She clears her throat, also sets her glass down, and taps her knees once before standing. “I suppose it’s getting late. And it’s going to be a very big day tomorrow. Especially for you. And trust me, you don’t want to face what’s coming with a hangover.” 

“Right. We should probably get some rest.”

Rio stands and gathers their glasses, heading to the kitchen. Agatha follows quietly, tidying up a few things along the way. Rio washes the glasses while Agatha dries them with a cloth and places them back where they belong. Once everything’s taken care of, they walk upstairs together. 

At the top landing, just as they’re about to part ways, Agatha calls out to her.

She exhales slowly. “I know you haven’t fully wrapped your head around it yet. But you have absolutely no idea what you’ve managed to do, how you somehow waltzed in and pulled off the kind of story most writers chase for decades. This is going to change everything for you, Rio. It’ll make your career.”

She pauses, then looks at Rio in a way that steals the air from her lungs. “I’d be lying if I said I’m not a little jealous of everyone else getting to have you after this. I really wish I could’ve kept you by my side just a little longer. But that wouldn’t be fair, to you or to me. You’re meant for more, Rio. And they’re all about to find out just how brilliant you are. I just hope you already know.”

Rio is speechless after hearing those words from Agatha. Something about it makes everything feel more real, how close morning is, how close she is to everything she’s worked for. In just a few hours, she’ll be chasing her dreams. And that also means leaving Agatha behind, at least a little.

Maybe they’ll still see each other now and then. Maybe they’ll stay in touch. But Rio would be lying if she said that’s all she wants. She doesn’t want glimpses or quick hellos in passing. She wants more. She wants Agatha — all the time, if the world would just let her.

She’s been sucked into Agatha’s orbit for a while now, drawn in, held there, like gravity had a name and it was hers. And now, with everything changing so suddenly, the thought of breaking free, of drifting out into the world without that pull anchoring her, terrifies her more than she wants to admit. 

Rio is not sure she can do it. She’s not even sure she wants to try.

“Agatha,” she calls after her as she starts to walk in the other direction.

When Agatha turns, all the noise in Rio’s head falls away, leaving just one thing.

She incontinently crosses the space between them and, without a second thought, claims her lips. It’s nothing like the quick, unsure kiss they shared before. This one is full and deep, her lips parting against Agatha’s. She hears her gasp softly into it, and that sound alone nearly knocks the breath out of her.

To Rio’s surprise and utter delight, Agatha kisses her back just as fiercely, as if she’s wanted this too, maybe for just as long. And for one breathless moment, Rio stops thinking. She lets herself fall, completely and without fear, lets herself be taken under by it. By her.

Rio has no idea how long the kiss lasted, only that when Agatha slowly pulls back, everything feels different. Rio opens her eyes, heart hammering, and looks at her nervously. But Agatha doesn’t look shaken like Rio expected her to be. She doesn’t even look like she regrets any of it.

If anything, she looks sure.

She lifts a hand and gently cups Rio’s face, her thumb brushing softly across her cheek.

Then she gives a small, warm smile. 

“Get some sleep. I’ll see you in the morning.”

And with that, Agatha turns and walks away, leaving Rio frozen in place, heart pounding, thoughts rushing back in. But for the first time since she got here, her thoughts are evident and clear.

Agatha will miss her, too.

Chapter 4

Chapter Summary

“You’re just doing this to annoy me.”

“No, I’m doing this to convince you.”

Agatha scoffs. “You’re unbearable.”

Rio grins. “So is that a yes?”

Agatha looks away, but she’s clearly trying not to smile. “Fine. If, and I mean if, that ever happens, I’ll give you your ten bucks. And your stupid ice cream.”

Rio beams. “Told you I was very persuasive.”

“I just said yes so you’d shut up. And to prove how wrong you are.”

Rio’s smile stretches, the little gap between her teeth unapologetically showing.

“Still counts.”

“Will you please stop that?”

“Stop what?”

“You know exactly what.”

Chapter Notes

some parts of this fic are lovingly inspired by the paperbacks that kept 18-year-old gay me company in a lonely dorm room. if some scenes feel vaguely familiar, you probably read it in 2017 too.

also, just found out that ending on an even-numbered page is apparently a magazine sin. this was supposed to be four chapters, but now it’s five, because i respect the craft (and also because i have no self-control). you’re welcome slash im sorry.

tw: childhood neglect and parental rejection related to agatha’s sexuality.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio wakes up without really knowing how she fell asleep after everything that happened last night.

She grabs her phone to check the time. A little past eight. The team’s not arriving until ten, so she has at least an hour to brace herself for the madness Agatha warned her about.

Which, of course, brings Agatha right back into her thoughts.

How Agatha had assured her the article was going to be great, even though she hadn’t fully heard the interview or gone through Rio’s notes. 

How she kept saying, almost too many times, how proud she was of her: in her words, in the way she looked at her, and of course, in the kiss they shared.

She lifts her fingers to her lips, almost without thinking. 

And for a second, it feels like the phantom of Agatha’s kiss is still there, the kind of kiss that could’ve been a dream, if not for the way her heart still stumbles at the memory.

Then her eyes land on the door, slightly ajar, even though she clearly remembers closing it last night. 

Had Agatha come to check on her while she was still sleeping? Rio swallows, feeling the blush creep up her neck. God, she hopes she wasn’t drooling if Agatha really did come in. 

Hearing faint rustling from downstairs through the narrow gap, she swings her legs off the bed and pads out.

She expects to find Agatha, but stops short when she walks into the kitchen and sees a woman, probably a bit older than Lilia, standing by the stove, flipping something that smells surprisingly good.

Rio hesitates at the doorway, unsure whether to step back before the woman mistakes her for a burglar.

But before she can retreat, the woman speaks without turning. “I take it you slept well?” She finally glances over her shoulder and catches Rio mid-step, looking exactly like a kid caught sneaking snacks.

“You must be Rio,” the woman adds, gesturing to the tall chair across the kitchen counter. “Go on, have a seat. I’m almost done with breakfast. There’s fresh tea in that pot if you want it. But Agatha said you prefer coffee in the mornings, so help yourself to the other one.”

Still half-asleep and thoroughly confused, Rio perches on the tall chair, now wondering two things: Where the hell is Agatha? And who is this warm, sprightly older woman talking to her like they’ve known each other for years, or at least like she knows exactly who Rio is?

“Oh, for heaven’s sake! I’m so sorry, where are my manners?” the woman says with a laugh. “I’m Susan, but Agatha calls me Marmee, so feel free to do the same if you’d like.” She throws Rio a quick grin over her shoulder. “I live in that very average-looking house across the street,” she adds with a playful wink. “I’d come over and shake your hand, or give you a big old hug, but I’d rather not burn your breakfast on our very first meeting.”

Rio blinks, still trying to catch up, but before she can say anything, Marmee’s already talking again. “How do you like your eggs?” she asks, as if they’ve done this a dozen times before.

Rio opens her mouth, then closes it again. Still processing.

“Scrambled or sunny side?” Marmee prompts, waving her spatula.

Rio clears her throat. “Sunny side, please. Thank you.”

Marmee hums, as if that was the right answer, and turns back to the stove.

Rio glances around the kitchen, then asks, “I’m sorry, but…have you seen Agatha?”

“Oh, she’s probably in her office, taking calls,” Marmee answers brightly. “She was already up when I got here.” She turns to Rio again with a smile. “Do you like jam or honey on your toast?”

“Honey’s fine,” Rio says, pouring herself a cup of coffee. 

There are a dozen questions racing through her head, but she keeps them all to herself.

“You’re probably wondering why some old lady is in Agatha’s kitchen,” Marmee chuckles, and Rio flushes, a little startled she basically read her mind. “Well, brilliant as that kid is, she still can’t boil an egg to save her life. And her housekeeper’s off today. So she roped me in. Said you’re a real breakfast person and would come looking for actual food the second you woke up.” Marmee laughs again. 

Rio tries not to blush, hiding behind her mug, but the thought of Agatha making sure she’s being taken care of does something to her. It’s ridiculous, and stupidly unprecedented, coming from her boss. 

Making sure she’s eating properly isn’t exactly the same as giving her flowers or a love letter. And yet, somehow, the gesture feels more intimate than either.

Not wanting the silence to stretch too long, Rio blurts out a question, right as Marmee slides a plate of sunny-side-up eggs and toast in front of her. “So, how long have you known Agatha?”

“Oh, since she was a little girl,” Marmee says, turning back to the stove. “We used to live next door to her family’s estate on the Morris side. She’d sneak into our house for snacks and end up beating my husband at chess on the front porch. Drove him absolutely nuts.”

Rio can’t help the image that pops into her head, tiny Agatha, brows furrowed in concentration, completely outsmarting a grown man in a chess match.

“But then we had to sell the house,” Marmee continues. “He got sick, and we moved here to be closer to the cancer center. He never did get better, but I ended up loving the place, so I stayed.”

“I’m sorry about your husband.” 

Marmee hums. “It’s alright. Wherever he is now, I just know he’s not hurting anymore. And we had good years. Real good ones.” She smiles faintly before continuing. “Anyway, a few years after he passed, Agatha bought this house. Right around the time she became something fancy at that magazine company of hers. She said she wanted a place to clear her head when the city got too loud,” Marmee adds, chuckling. “But I know better. She just missed my cooking.”

“Does she come here often?”

“Only when work really gets to her. Though she did stay here for nearly a week last month, the longest she’s stayed all year, I think. She’d drive back and forth to the city but always came home to sleep. Poor thing looked like she hadn’t rested in years.” 

Rio nods and realizes it was around the same time Agatha fired her. 

So Agatha had been staying here then.

She takes another sip of coffee, attempting not to think too deeply about it.

But as she looks up, Marmee is staring at her, as if she knows something about Rio that Rio has not yet figured out.

“Sorry, is there something on my face?” Rio asks, giving the older woman a shy smile. She’d be mortified if she drooled in her sleep and still had dried spit on her face, especially since she forgot to wash up before heading downstairs.

Marmee just chuckles. 

“No, nothing like that. You’re just exactly how Agatha described you.”

Rio’s head perks up. “She’s been talking about me?”

“She’s mentioned you once or twice,” Marmee answers with a smile. “Said you were the first person ever to lie to her just to get out of work.” She laughs. “I think you left quite an impression after that.” 

Rio winces, then laughs under her breath. 

“Yeah, that was a mistake,” she admits, “but I’m not really starting to regret it now.”

“Well,” Marmee says knowingly, “you shouldn’t.”

Before Rio can dwell too long on what that means, the sound of footsteps padding across the hardwood draws her attention, and then Agatha appears in the doorway, mid-call, and everything else blurs. 

She’s in a purple morning robe, soft curls falling around her face, glasses perched low on her nose. Breathtaking. Effortlessly so.

Rio swears her heart skips, or maybe stumbles. 

Either way, it’s a miracle she doesn’t drop her mug right there and then. 

“Then send the other transcriptionist,” Agatha snaps, waving a hand like the caller can see her. “Yes, whoever. I don’t care if it’s one person or a whole damn typing cult, just get me someone who can transcribe a five-hour interview before lunch.” She ends the call with a forceful tap and sets her phone on the counter. “I swear to God, it’s like herding lobotomized cats.”

Agatha exhales loudly through her nostrils, squeezing the bridge as if she could somehow wish patience to exist.

She doesn't even notice Rio is staring until Marmee clears her throat pointedly. 

“Now, what did I tell you?” Marmee says, turning a slice of French toast in the pan. “It’s not good to start the morning with furrowed brows, young lady. You’ll scare the poor girl away.” 

“Don’t worry,” Rio chuckles, lifting her mug. “I’m kind of used to it by now.” 

Marmee snorts as she flips another toast. “Of course you are. You poor thing.”

“I see you two are getting along.” Agatha walks over and settles into the seat across Rio. Whatever had her all worked up seems to ease off her shoulders the second their eyes meet. “Did you sleep okay?”

Rio wants to say she barely remembers falling asleep. 

That she spent hours tossing and turning, thinking about last night, and that, at one point, she even considered knocking on Agatha’s door, since the latter had told her to knock if she ever needed anything.

And Rio had needed answers. 

But now, seeing how Agatha seems perfectly calm and normal about the kiss, Rio just nods and takes a sip of her coffee instead.

“I did,” she says. Then, because she needs at least one answer today, she asks, “Did you?”

Agatha appears to catch the implication underneath the question, and for a second, something small but telling slips through her calm, collected demeanor. Not enough for most people to notice, but Rio does.

Maybe because she’s been watching too closely, or maybe because she’s known for a while now how to understand the way Agatha communicates without words.

“Yeah,” Agatha answers softly, then reaches for the coffee pot and pours herself a mug.

Marmee seems to notice something between the two of them. Her eyes move from Rio to Agatha before she clears her throat again, turns off the stove, and sets the pan in the dishwasher. “Well, since you both look caffeinated, fed, and settled, I’m gonna go check on my Fanny.”

“Who’s Fanny?” Rio asks.

“Marmee’s dog,” Agatha says.

“She’s a very sweet Mastiff,” Marmee chimes in proudly. “Agatha adopted her from a rescue about a year ago and gave her to me. You’re welcome to swing by the house anytime if you want to say hi. Fanny loves meeting new people.”

Rio perks up again. She’s always had a soft spot for dogs, but having one was never really an option.

It was either too expensive or too cramped in their apartment, and with her and Alice both working nearly all day, it just never felt possible.

“Really? I’d love that,” she says, smiling. “I’d love to meet Fanny.”

“And Fanny would probably love to see you too,” Agatha adds. “But only after today. May I remind you, you’re about to walk into hell. I’m not letting you get distracted by a dog’s charm offensive.”

Marmee chuckles. “Agatha’s right. My Fanny can be very distracting. She’s got this one wrapped around her little paw almost every time.” Rio tries not to visibly smile at the picture of the ever-composed Agatha Harkness softening up for a floppy-eared Mastiff. 

“Well,” Marmee adds, wiping her hands on a dish towel, “you two enjoy your breakfast. And good luck with whatever hell you’re walking into today.” 

With that, Marmee heads out of the kitchen. Agatha murmurs a soft thanks, and Rio echoes it a beat later. 

On her way out, Marmee throws Rio another look, one of those knowing, lingering ones she’s been giving her since she walked in. 

And if Rio’s reading it right, it almost feels like Marmee’s the one who’s thankful for her.

As soon as they’re alone, Agatha doesn’t give the silence a chance to settle.

“Jen should be here in a few minutes. She’s coming ahead of the rest of the team. I gave her full control over what you’ll wear today.” She shoots Rio a look before the latter can protest. “Relax. I told her to keep it within the bounds of whatever it is you call comfort, and to somehow attempt to match your famously impeccable taste.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “What's wrong with my clothes from yesterday? Also, I couldn’t find them in my room.”

“I sent them out for laundry.”

She opens her mouth to speak, but Agatha cuts her off again. 

“Don’t worry. You’ll get your precious subway clothes back by the end of the day.”

Rio doesn’t even have it in her to look annoyed. Her brain immediately stutters at the fact that Agatha did not only walk into her room, but also picked up her clothes and sent them off to be cleaned, which explains why the door had been slightly open earlier.

But what really mortifies Rio is knowing that Agatha saw her sleeping. Again. That's the third time now. And something about that feels unfair. Unbalanced. 

Rio’s seen Agatha asleep twice, and she wouldn’t mind seeing that again. And again. Preferably with the two of them in the same bed, in the warm glow of morning light, perhaps with a lazy arm thrown over her waist. Agatha’s bed or hers, it doesn’t really matter. Just as long as she’s waking up beside the woman in front of her.

The same woman, sipping her coffee and going on about the day ahead, who seems completely unaware of the disarray unfolding, like last night’s kiss hadn’t completely rearranged the furniture in Rio’s brain. 

She wants to bring it up. She really does. 

But the more reasonable part of her is screaming that this isn’t the right time. 

Today is going to be huge. 

She needs every ounce of focus she can wring out of herself.

“Do you have any other specific requests besides the endless stream of coffee and tea?” 

Rio blinks out of her thoughts, eyes focusing on Agatha, who’s still glued to her phone. 

“Nope, that’s about it,” she says, taking a long sip of coffee. She needs to shake off the fog and wake up fast. “Wait, actually, one more thing. Think I could get a pack or two of Spirits? I’ve got a backup stash at my place, but—”

Agatha finally looks up from her phone, brows lifting.

“You smoke cigarettes?”

“Only when I’m about to write a beast of a piece. Helps me shut everything else out.”

Agatha gives her a long look, like a girlfriend catching her boyfriend sneaking a beer before noon. Then she sighs, muttering, “Fine. I’ll have Jen pick some up. But just one. And you’re not smoking it in here.” She starts typing into her phone, still grumbling. “Can’t believe you smoke that crap.”

“Says the woman who made me smoke a ten-year-old weed,” Rio shoots back, laughing under her breath.

That gets Agatha to pause for half a second. Right. That night. The first time Agatha had kissed her.

The look on Agatha’s face is enough to keep Rio from bringing up last night. And she gets it. She understands. Whatever happened between them can wait. 

Today is all about business and keeping things as professional as they can manage.

“This is so good, by the way,” Rio says, pointing her fork at the French toast, eggs, and a couple strips of bacon. “Marmee just earned a spot right under Lorna for best breakfast.”

She says it half-jokingly, hoping it patches up whatever unease she might have caused.

Agatha, after all, is still technically her boss, for a few more hours.

“That’s why I keep her around.” Her lips twitches close to a smile before hiding it behind her mug.

Rio nudges the conversation elsewhere. “She mentioned you used to play chess when you were a kid.” 

“I did. One of the few things my parents forced on me that I actually ended up liking. Mostly because I enjoyed watching grown men lose to a little girl. Although, Henry wasn’t one of them. He and Marmee were the only ones I could stand in that neighborhood.”

Rio figures Henry must’ve been Marmee’s late husband.

“So, what other things did they put you through that you didn’t absolutely hate?”

Agatha considers that, still nursing her mug. 

“Just chess, I’m afraid. My father tried to make me play tennis, but I hated being sweaty and flat-out refused to chase balls like some Labrador. Though I’ll admit, a racket did come in handy when I was one minor inconvenience away from smashing someone’s skull. Meanwhile, my mother shoved me into ballet class, but Madame Lévesque promptly told me I had two left feet and the grace of a drunken duck.”

Rio chuckles. “You? With two left feet? I don’t buy it.”

Agatha tilts her head at her. “Do you honestly think I dance?”

“You’re telling me you’ve never danced?”

“Oh, honey. You’re more likely to see a raccoon pirouetting across Fifth Avenue than catch me dancing.”

Rio grins. “What if I bet on it?”

“Bet on what?”

“You. Dancing. I’m betting you’ll cave and dance before I see a raccoon do a pirouette.” 

Agatha smirks. “Well, that’s a bet you’re going to lose.”

“I don’t think so. Back in high school, girls were ditching their prom dates just to dance with me.” 

“So what, you think I’m gonna be next?”

“That’s the idea.”

Agatha narrows her eyes. “You really think I’d dance with you?”

“I think it’s very possible,” Rio answers with a shrug. “And I’m persuasive.”

“You’re the opposite. You’re easily persuaded.”

“I let myself be persuaded when I want to be. Totally different.”

“That makes zero sense.”

“You can think whatever you want. But I’m going to be the first person to get Agatha Harkness to dance.”

“You poor, deluded thing. That’s never gonna happen.”

“Never say never, baby.”

The nickname slips so naturally off Rio’s tongue, even herself doesn’t catch it in time. And judging by the slight jolt of expression on Agatha’s face, she didn’t expect it either. So, Rio adds —

“And when I manage to do it, you’ll owe me ten bucks. And a trip to the ice cream store.”

Agatha lets out a genuine laugh. “What are you, twelve?”

“I sometimes do have the cravings of a twelve-year-old. But I’m not ashamed of it. And I’m also dead serious. Ten bucks and an ice cream date, Miss Harkness.”

Agatha shakes her head. “No. I’m not taking orders from someone who just openly admitted to having the cravings of a middle-schooler.”

“You’re just scared you’ll lose.”

“Trust me, I’m not.”

“Trust me, you are.”

“I’m not.”

“You totally are.”

“You’re just doing this to annoy me.”

“No, I’m doing this to convince you.”

Agatha scoffs. “You’re unbearable.”

Rio grins. “So is that a yes?”

Agatha looks away, but she’s clearly trying not to smile. 

“Fine. If, and I mean if, that ever happens, I’ll give you your ten bucks. And your stupid ice cream.”

Rio beams. “Told you I was very persuasive.”

“I just said yes so you’d shut up. And to prove how wrong you are.” 

Rio’s smile stretches, the little gap between her teeth unapologetically showing. “Still counts.” 

“Will you please stop that?”

“Stop what?”

“You know exactly what.”

Agatha lifts her mug again, sipping her coffee like it’ll protect her from smiling.

But Rio takes it as an opportunity to really look at her. Ever since she woke up this morning, she’s been wondering if last night actually happened.

But now, watching Agatha smile, laugh, and spar with her like this, there’s no doubt.

It happened. 

She kissed Agatha. 

Agatha kissed her back.

And while she may not be able to talk about any of it with her just yet, she’s content with this. 

They’re talking. Agatha’s laughing. Agatha’s smiling. And it’s all because of Rio.

Then Agatha’s phone rings.

Rio takes a bite of her toast and watches the woman across from her start to rebuild her fortress, or perhaps just the mask, as she answers the call.

“Yes, Tony, I’m well aware of what’s happening. The decision to pause the print run was mine.” Agatha’s tone is curt, and it’s only a matter of time before she runs out of patience. “Yes, we’re changing the cover. I know the board will have opinions, but that’s not my concern right now. Trust me, this story is worth it.”

Her eyes meet Rio’s for a second before she looks away again.

“It’s a world exclusive. And while I understand you’re looking at this from a business standpoint, you, of all people, should know that a bit of short-term fallout is basically nothing compared to what we’re about to pull in. You told me to fix the numbers, and that’s exactly what I’m doing. The boost in readership and revenue will more than justify this decision.” She doesn’t blink. “Frankly, instead of wasting my time with this lecture, you should be thanking me for landing the biggest story this magazine has had in years.”

She stops, listens, then her brows cross. 

“What do you mean I’m overdue for humility?” She’s clearly not happy. “Don’t you dare insult me, Tony. You know better than to compare me to her.” Another beat, then her voice drops a degree colder. “No. I’m the editor-in-chief. I know what the magazine needs. We’re running this story. And that’s final.”

The call ends with Agatha nearly slamming the phone down on the counter. Whatever smile she had earlier is gone, replaced by a hard look and a clenched jaw. 

Rio watches her, and against all logic, finds it kind of hot. Hotter than it should be.

This angry, commanding side of Agatha. 

There’s something about the way Agatha takes control that gets into her bloodstream. 

And Rio wants to be the one to find out just how far that control goes.

“Stark doesn’t want to run Lilia’s exclusive?” 

It is safer to ask a question than let herself spiral in her own burning thoughts.

“No, he’s not worried about that,” Agatha says, a touch calmer now. “He’s just being stupid, worried about the few thousand he’ll lose changing the cover at the last minute. As if that actually matters. He knows how explosive this issue is going to be. For all I know, he just doesn’t want to dip into his yacht fund to cover layout revisions and press overtime.”

“So, you’re still running it? I’m still writing the piece?”

Agatha turns to look at her, and this time the anger in her blue eyes completely melts away.

What remains is all conviction. And something far gentler. 

“Yes, Rio. You’re still writing the piece. And no one, not even Stark, not the board, not anyone, is going to stop me from running it. You deserve to tell this story. And I’ll fight like hell to make sure it sees print.”

Rio is honestly kind of surprised, and pretty grateful, that Jen didn’t hate her enough to hand over whatever Barbie-coded uniform the girls at the Fortress wore daily. 

Instead, she gave her a perfectly comfortable Alexander Wang shirt, a pair of soft Tom Ford jeans, and even tossed in a new pair of Calvin Klein underwear, still in the packaging.

Fresh out of the shower and dressed, Rio eventually heads downstairs. 

The house isn’t quiet anymore like it was earlier. 

The living room and kitchen are full of people from Nocturne. 

Some are in suits, others holding tablets or coffee. Everyone’s talking, moving, busy with something. 

And it’s slowly hitting Rio that she’s about to be right in the middle of all of it.

“I don’t care if you have to walk twenty-five miles to get here, David. I made it perfectly clear we’re on a tight schedule. So if the best you can do is complain about traffic, don’t bother showing up at all. I can easily find someone who actually knows how to do their job, unlike whatever brand of incompetence you’re pulling right now…” 

Rio turns toward the voice, and of course, it’s Agatha on the phone again. 

She’s ditched the robe from earlier and is now in a light cerulean button-down and tan pants.

Rio almost never sees her in pants, and for some reason, that makes her stare a second longer than she probably should.

“Everything okay?” Rio asks when Agatha catches her staring. She only realizes how soft her voice sounded when Agatha gives her a neutral look in return. Right. They’re not alone anymore. 

“Everything’s fine,” Agatha answers coolly. “Jen uploaded the first part of the interview transcript on that laptop. You can work wherever you want. The kitchen, the living room, the study, the patio. Your choice. But I’d prefer if you stayed inside so we can keep an eye on your progress.”

Rio hesitates for a beat, thrown by the sudden switch in tone, but she nods. 

“Uh, yeah, the kitchen’s fine,” she says. “I’ll work here. With everyone else.” 

“Good,” Agatha nods. “Kale’s at your disposal today. Whatever you need, just ask her.” She points at her assistant, and Rio follows her gaze. Jen doesn’t exactly look thrilled but manages to keep a straight face.

“Now if you’ll excuse me,” she adds, already picking up her phone again, “you should start writing. I still have a few calls to make.”

Rio doesn’t know how many hours have passed since she started typing.

It simply felt like the second she opened the laptop, something inside her snapped into place. She can’t remember the last time she’s been this focused — this fast, this clear. 

She’s never written a feature like this before, but something about that interview with Lilia sets her on fire. Her fingers move like her head might burst into flames if she slows down. 

And somewhere in the middle of it, she thinks of her dad. 

How he used to vanish into his office and come out with a story. 

She wishes he could see her now. 

Would he be proud? Of course he would. 

A world exclusive, bigger than anything the men in their family have ever landed. 

Mateo Vidal would be the first to cheer her on.

Every now and then, someone drifts by her side. 

Jen would set down a fresh cup of coffee without saying a word, sometimes a granola bar, sometimes a warm croissant, or a powdered sugar donut on a small plate.

Melina would also swing by to check if the tone felt right or if a sentence sounded too bold for print. 

A guy from layout, Rio keeps forgetting if his name is Johnny or just John, would also float in and out with a tablet, asking where the photos should go or if she had picked a pull quote yet. 

It’s like being in the eye of a well-oiled storm. Everyone’s moving around her.

It’s maybe another hour later when Rio finally notices the dull ache in her back and butt from sitting too long, and the strain in her fingers from typing nonstop. 

Still, the work feels never-ending. 

Coffee and tea come and go, same with plates of food she can’t even remember eating, if she ate them at all.

She’s also lost count of how many yuppie sticks she’s lit, despite Agatha’s warning not to smoke indoors. 

Not that Agatha’s been around to stop her. 

She seems to be the only one who hasn’t checked in since Rio started writing.

The words are starting to come together, but now Rio’s running into an issue with making everything make sense and coherent, and if she’s being honest, it’s an absolute mess. 

Her draft skitters from one piece of Lilia’s life to another, from one absurd adventure to the next, each scene loud and strange, but none of them landing quite right. 

Somehow, the tick of the clock isn’t just ticking anymore, it’s drilling into her skull. 

Footsteps from the kitchen to the living room and back echo like a metronome gone rogue, slipping in and out of her focus, while the clinking of plates, cups, and silverware scrapes her nerves like nails on a chalkboard. 

And the different voices: the talking, the rambling, the arguing over what goes where, bleed straight through what’s left of her concentration. 

All of it presses in, too close, like the walls themselves are inching forward. 

The words on her screen start to blur, drowned out by everything outside it, and it feels like if one more thing breaks her focus, she just might fucking burst.

“Can everyone just shut their noise holes for two goddamn seconds?!”

She hadn’t exactly thought about how everyone might react to her snapping until the whole house goes dead quiet.

Conversations stop mid-sentence, coffee cups freeze halfway to mouths. Heads turn. Eyes widen. 

And there’s Rio, suddenly the center of attention, having just silenced a room full of people who outrank her, out-age her, and have probably been working at Nocturne since before she even knew the magazine existed.

Jen is the first to catch her eye, staring at her with wide, stunned disbelief. 

But what really makes Rio want to sink into the floor is how the crowd seems to part, like a divine curtain peeling back, revealing Agatha standing just a few feet away, phone suspended mid-air, eyes locked solely on her. 

From the speaker of her phone, a voice crackles: “Hello? Miss Harkness, are you still there?”

Agatha doesn’t answer right away, and just stares at Rio. There’s something disbelieving in her eyes, like she’s just caught a glimpse of what else Rio might be capable of.

And if Rio’s not imagining it, Agatha swallows once, subtly, before her mouth sets into a tight line.

“Yes, but I’ll have to call you back,” she says, then hangs up without breaking eye contact.

Nobody dares speak after that, and Rio starts to wonder if she took it too far.

But Agatha finally pulls her eyes away, looks around the room, and says, “Everyone clear out of this space and keep your voices down.” Then she turns to Jen. “Make sure no one disturbs Miss Vidal again.”

And with that, she walks out.

Jen opens her mouth, probably to rally the troops, but Rio beats her to it. Embarrassed by the attention, she gets to her feet in a hurry. “No. No, it’s fine. You all stay. I’ll move to the study,” she blurts out, grabbing her laptop and backing out fast.

She slips into the study, finally alone, her cheeks still warm. And as much as she wants to melt into the floor, there’s a small part of her that kind of genuinely enjoyed it.

The way the whole room fell quiet at her voice. The way Agatha looked at her. The way it felt like she was the one holding the reins.

Hours later, there’s a knock at the door, finally pulling Rio out of her screen. Her eyes sting from staring at the laptop too long.

She blinks, then glances at the clock, only now realizing it’s already close to five. 

She expects Jen, or maybe someone else checking in, but it’s Agatha who steps through the door. “Is now a good time?” she says, settling into the chair across from her. “Or am I about to get yelled at again?”

Rio rubs the back of her neck. “Yeah, sorry about that.”

“Don’t be. Everyone was breaking your focus, you had every right to do that. If it were me, I would've done worse. And I did say you were the one calling the shots today.” She pauses, gives Rio a look as she crosses her legs. “Turns out, having control suits you,” she adds, like it just slips out.

Rio just nods and turns her head away, refusing to meet the way Agatha’s looking at her. 

She better not be blushing right now. 

“First draft’s done,” she tells her. “I sent it to Melina about twenty minutes ago. I’m just rereading in case I missed anything. Lilia’s life is just so full and interesting, I didn’t want to leave out something good. Do you think it was smart to open with her getting kicked out of the Vatican gift shop?”

Agatha unexpectedly lets out a short laugh. “Oh, that’ll grab anyone’s attention. No doubt about that.”

Rio feels her exhaustion slip off the second she hears it, her eyes crinkling into a smile.

“Do you want to read it? It’s just the first draft but—” 

Agatha doesn’t wait. She crosses the room and leans down just enough to be level with Rio’s laptop. The sudden closeness makes the latter forget how to breathe for a second.

“I’ll just take a quick look,” Agatha says, her eyes already scanning the screen. “But I’ll give the final draft a proper read once Melina and her team have polished it for publication.”

Rio just nods and takes the chance to quietly watch Agatha as she scans through the article. 

She realizes she’ll never get tired of that familiar lavender scent, or of tracing the slope of Agatha’s nose with her eyes, or of looking at the soft creases that form when she almost smiles.

And then it dawns on her that there’s a real chance she might not get to do any of that anymore after tonight.

Agatha seems to notice her staring and turns to her, their faces now only inches apart. Rio tries to act normal, as if her heart isn’t suddenly pounding in her chest.

Agatha doesn’t say anything at first. But she doesn’t really have to. Her eyes subtly lower to Rio’s lips for the briefest breath. And Rio does the same.

Then their eyes meet again, right at the same time. And Agatha looks at her in that way she always does, the one that makes Rio’s heart trip over itself, again and again. And just like that, she remembers.

“What are you thinking, Agatha?”

She throws the question almost under her breath, as if saying it too loud might scare away whatever frail thing is hanging between them.

Agatha looks a little caught off guard, like the question tugged something loose. Then she also remembers their deal back in Delaware and says, “You know I’m not required to answer that anymore. That only counted when you were still working for me.”

“Technically, I still am. My last day’s not over yet.” Rio nods toward the clock. They’ve still got five minutes before five. “So why don’t you hold up your end of the deal and tell me what you’re thinking?”

Agatha lets out a small breath, like she finds it funny. “I think you’re a great writer. I think anyone who reads this will see that. And they’ll be lucky to read anything you put out.”

Rio realizes this is the first, and probably the last, time she gets to pull the card she and her boss agreed on. So she’s going to make it count.

“What else?” She swallows. 

“While I do think your article is strong, I still think Melina’s going to tear your draft apart with edits,” Agatha informs her. “She might be nicer than me, but she’s ruthless when it comes to clarity and tone. She won’t let anything slide, especially not with something this important.”

Rio lets out a dry little laugh. “I did expect that.” She pauses, searching her face. “But what else, Agatha?”

Agatha’s blue eyes drop to her lips again, and Rio feels her whole body go still.

“I think you’re…” she breathes, as if weighing the cost of saying more than she usually allows. “I think you’re an exceptional writer, and any publication with half a brain would be foolish not to want you.”

To Rio’s dismay, Agatha stands up straight and takes a small step back, putting space between them again. Whatever was building in that moment slips away immediately after. 

She clears her throat. “Now, while Melina’s team tears through your draft with their red pens, I’d say this calls for a celebratory drink. Perhaps a glass of…” She walks over to a shelf and picks out a bottle of Macallan. “I think you’ll like this.” Then she grabs two glasses and pours a generous amount into each.

Rio watches her the entire time, trying not to show the disappointment on her face. And when Agatha hands her a glass with the smallest smile, Rio takes it and tries to smile back.

“To the job they say a million girls would kill for,” Agatha practically announces, lifting her glass. “And to the job you’ve always truly wanted.”

Rio looks at her for a moment, still trying to figure out what’s going on behind her eyes. But then she lets herself settle into whatever Agatha is offering. She raises her glass and clinks it lightly with hers.

“And to whatever comes next,” Rio adds, almost to herself.

“Whatever comes next?” Agatha repeats, glass halfway to her lips. “Which means?”

Me finding a way to stay in your life, and you finding a reason to let me, Rio wants to admit.

But instead, she says, “Just that we don’t become complete strangers after this.”

Agatha hums, but there’s something a little sad in the sound. 

“Right,” she mumbles, lifting her glass again. “To whatever comes next, then.” 

She then downs her drink in one go, sets the glass on the table, then claps her hands once and shakes her shoulders lightly.

“Anyway, the layout’s all arranged, your photos included. Why don’t you finish your drink, take a breather, and come see how your work looks on the page?” 

She’s smiling, but Rio can tell it’s forced.

“I’ll meet you outside.” 

Rio only nods. 

She turns to leave but slowly pauses at the doorway. She looks back at Rio one last time, and somehow, it feels like the last. They simply regard each other before Agatha says — 

“I want you to know that this is just the beginning.” 

Then why does it feel like goodbye?

“You have a whole world ahead of you now.” 

Will Agatha want to follow her into it?

Agatha gives her another one of those small smiles, the kind that almost reaches her eyes.

“Congratulations...” A passing beat. “Congratulations, Rio.”

Rio used to picture this day as nothing short of magic when she was a little girl. Blue, clear skies. Birds singing outside her window. Even the sound of cars would feel like music to her ears.

The sun would be beaming, like it was proud of her. But instead, she wakes up to the sound of her skull complaining.

Her first world-exclusive, hopefully not the last, is out today. 

Her name on newsstands, in bookstores, and basically anywhere that sells magazines.

And all she can think is: ow.

Was it wise to knock back a few cans of Heineken alone in her room two nights after leaving Agatha’s Scarsdale estate? No. Definitely not.

But it was the only feasible thing Rio could think to do, just to fall asleep, just to shut off the thoughts about “whatever comes next.”

Now with the very real possibility that whatever comes next doesn’t include Agatha anymore.

A knock on the door pulls Rio out of her musings. She hasn’t moved an inch from where she’s curled up, limbs tangled in the sheets. But before she can even sit up, the door swings open.

Alice walks in first, and behind her, Billy nearly trips over himself, arms raised, clutching something like it’s a sacred artifact. “Guess who’s famous now?” he grins, waving the glossy magazine.

Rio blinks. “Good morning to you, too.”

Alice tosses a smug look over her shoulder as she shuts the door behind them. 

“Trust me, we tried to wait until ten.” 

Billy practically throws himself onto the bed beside her, already flipping through the magazine with the energy of someone who had sugar for breakfast.

“Look! Look! Page five.” He jabs his finger at the byline. “Rio Vidal. Right there. Your name. In print. On real, dead-tree paper that people actually pay for.”

Alice flops down on the other side, boxing Rio in the middle. The bed’s obviously too small for three people, and Rio lets out an annoyed sigh.

“Can you believe it?” Alice grins, just as wide as Billy’s. “We’re friends with a published writer. Not just published, but front cover, big-shot published. Mom’s gonna go absolutely ballistic over this.”

“I’m gonna cry,” Billy says, fanning his face. Rio scrunches her nose at him. “I’m buying, like, six more copies. Maybe twelve. And I’ll literally do whatever you want today, anything, just to make you sign them. Then I’m selling them on eBay or Etsy and buying myself a giant Squishmallow. Or one of those tiny skincare fridges. But I’m not sure yet. I’m still deciding.” 

“I'm not signing anything,” Rio laughs. Still half-asleep, and still somewhere between disbelief and awe. She takes the magazine from him, tracing her name with her eyes. 

Her name. In a real magazine. Out in the world.

The two on either side of her keep rambling, something about Alice saying, “We should frame the page,” and Billy chiming in with, “If you won’t sign to sell, maybe you could sign some of my friends’ copies for five bucks.” Rio just nods along, but her eyes stay fixed on the name. 

She’s genuinely happy for herself. She really is. 

And yet, all she can think about is Agatha.

Would she have knocked on Rio’s door too, grinning, breathless, ready to jump on the bed with her?

Would they have read it together, side by side, and stayed under the covers all day, marveling at the thing?

It’s Rio’s first real achievement as a writer, but even now, even here, she wonders what it would’ve felt like if Agatha had been part of this moment. Someone with a thousand victories already, but maybe still soft enough to make room for one more.

After a long, hot shower and an even longer, meandering breakfast packed with overlapping chatter and half-finished stories from Alice and Billy, Rio finally makes it back to her room, only to find her phone buzzing like a kicked beehive. Missed calls. Voicemails. Texts. Dozens of them.

Agatha hadn’t been joking when she said people would come running the second the story dropped. 

It’s like the whole world decided to storm Rio’s doorstep all at once. 

But the first thing Rio wants to know is who the hell gave her number to the entire planet?

She listens to a few in stunned silence. Vogue wants to interview her about how she landed the story with the ever-elusive Lilia Calderu. The CBC left a message asking if she could share a bit about the experience, what it was like, and how she pulled it off.

Vanity Fair and Harper’s Bazaar both want her to call them back, both “very eager” to talk about what comes next for her.

Even The Drew Barrymore Show, for God’s sake, wants her to come on and talk about Lilia. Or maybe with Lilia. Rio stares at the message and shakes her head.

She loves Drew, adores her, but absolutely not. There’s no way she’s getting on TV. Nothing on earth, not even Drew’s radiant smile or the promise of a cozy couch interview, could make her do it. Over her dead body. And probably someone else’s, too.

With texts still flooding in, Rio dials the one person who might have answers.

“Oh great. Ruining my perfect workday wasn’t enough, and now you have to go and call me like everyone else? What do you want?” comes the greeting, laced with annoyance.

“Hi, Jen.”

“You’re really starting to become a full-time problem in my life, you know that? My inbox has been blowing up since your article dropped. I can’t even pick up one call without three more coming in. People are acting like I’m some kind of customer service hotline because of you. And I’m not exactly thrilled about it.”

“Yeah, so about that,” Rio mutters, rubbing the back of her neck. “My phone’s been blowing up too. I was just wondering if maybe, possibly…you gave out my number?”

“Well, isn’t that what you’ve always wanted?” Jen snaps on the other end. “But no, I didn’t give anyone your number. If I hated you that much, I’d rent a damn billboard and throw your home address on it too.”

“You wouldn’t actually do that…would you?” Rio asks, half-joking, half-concerned.

“I just might. Three more annoying calls and I’ll be googling billboard rates.”

“Jen!” 

“Oh, relax your size six ass. For all intents and purposes, you happen to be on Agatha’s protected list now. You’re off limits to the press, unless it’s your choice. She made it real clear that anyone who leaks any of your private info loses their job on the spot.”

“What? She did that?” 

“No, Rio. I hallucinated it during my morning meditation,” Jen deadpans.

“Did she say why?” 

“Of course I asked her why,” Jen says dryly. “Then we had a lovely little tea party and braided each other’s hair while talking it over in her office.” Then her voice rises. “Do I look like someone dumb enough to poke the lioness? You clearly don’t know her if you think she explains anything to anyone.”

“Right,” Rio mumbles. “Sorry.”

Jen lets out a dramatic sigh, “It was really good, by the way.”

“What?” 

“Pick up the pace, slowpoke. Did you dump all your tiny brain cells into that article? I read it this morning on my way to work. And I’ll admit, it was way better than I expected. Agatha made the right call running it. And somehow, you were the right one to write it.”

Rio doesn’t bother holding back her laugh, especially with how physically pained Jen sounds. 

“Thanks, Jen.” 

“Don’t get used to it. I’m still annoyed at you for turning my day, and probably the rest of my week, into hell on earth,” Jen complains, but there’s more exhaustion than bite in her voice. “Anyway, there are still some papers you need to sign here. I haven’t slotted you in yet, so I’ll just email the details. Agatha’s been in nonstop meetings, and I’m still trying to figure out where to fit you in.”

At the mention of Agatha, Rio perks up, already opening her mouth to ask, but stops when she hears Agatha’s voice in the background, paired with the familiar click-clack of her heels. God. It’s only been three days, and she already misses the sound.

“Oh, she’s here. I’ve got to go. Good luck with the vultures,” Jen says, filled with caustic joy.

Then the line goes dead before Rio can reply. She stares at her phone, sighs, and tosses it onto the bed before grabbing a towel and running it through her hair.

Not even a minute later, her phone starts ringing again. Then again. And again.

Different numbers each time, none of them saved, none of them familiar.

So, she lets them all go to voicemail.

Throwing on a hoodie and the first pair of shorts she can find, Rio heads out without brushing her hair.

She walks to the corner newsstand near her apartment, buys herself a copy of Nocturne, tries to act casual about it on the way home, and curls up in bed the second she gets back.

She flips through the magazine, each page gleaming with careful work. 

Her story, her words, appear almost surreal in print, wrapped in clean layouts and powerful photos that make it feel bigger than just her. 

Now more than ever, she can see how much Agatha, as the editor-in-chief, cared about this issue. It’s like a gift packaged in pretty paper, handed gently into her hands by Agatha herself.

She sighs, feeling a familiar wave of missing someone wash over her. It’s frustrating, this strange ache, the restless yearning, this stubborn longing. 

She knows she shouldn’t be feeling anything but happiness. She should be celebrating. This is a milestone, after all.

But how can she celebrate this when she hasn’t heard from the one person she really wants to share it with?

More days pass, and every time the phone rings, Rio hopes it’s Agatha. 

Between replying to a handful of job offers and turning down a few pushy interview requests from eager media outlets, Rio also keeps an eye out for an email from Nocturne. 

Jen did mention there are still papers she needs to sign, and Rio wouldn’t mind using that as an excuse to see Agatha again. But the messages never come. Nothing at all.

Not even when Rio sends Agatha a photo of a bus with their magazine’s cover on it, or another picture of a woman reading the issue in a subway.

Not even when she shares part of her text chain with Lilia, where Lilia says she loved the article, has decided to stay a little longer in America, and is throwing a party before heading back to Italy. One she invited Rio to attend, and by extension, Agatha too.

Rio spends most days playing phone tag with editors and magazines that want her on board. 

Some offers sound decent. Others, not so much. Other fashion magazines, as expected, reach out with their usual pitches. And then, out of nowhere, she even gets an email from Oxe. 

But does she really want to write for them? More fashion stories? When she even barely enjoyed it before? And the only thing that made it bearable was getting the chance to see Agatha around the office. And now, that’s gone.

One afternoon, Hela sends Rio a text about a freelance writing job for The Wall Street Journal, and maybe even The Washington Post if she’s interested. 

The work would be serious reporting: digging into financial trends, corporate scandals, and breaking down complex economic issues.

It’s the kind of hard-hitting journalism Rio’s been craving all her life. And freelancing for these outlets might be exactly what she needs right now.

But instead of jumping at the opportunity, Rio keeps herself busy with other mundane things like cleaning her room, scrubbing the kitchen, baking cookies, planting new greenery on their tiny balcony, and calling Lorna to ask for her recipe for pot roast and homemade bread.

Anything to keep her hands moving during these last few free days while her mind spins through the choices suddenly tossed her way.

It’s only when a package shows up at her doorstep that Rio is finally pulled out of her New York domestic bender.

Inside is a black, full-length, tuxedo-style coat, double-breasted with structured shoulders, clean white cuffs, and a metallic silver bow tie folded neatly on top. 

Tucked beside it is a long note in Lilia’s unmistakable scrawl: 

“Hope you don’t mind me dressing you up for my party, kid. My driver’s picking you up. And don’t even think about bailing. I want to flaunt the writer who told the world about my wildest adventures.” 

At the bottom of the paper, embroidered in shimmering gold, are the words: I Died in Paris, 1978.  

Rio can only assume that’s the theme.

The night of the party sneaks up faster than Rio expects. 

With Agatha still radio silent, she debates about backing out altogether. 

She looks at the tuxedo laid out on her bed and comes up with a hundred excuses to stay home: her stomach hurts, her foot’s acting weird, or Mercury’s probably in retrograde. 

She paces around her room, heart thrumming against her ribs like it’s trying to crawl out. 

But she owes Lilia at least a quick appearance. 

One hour, tops, she tells herself. Show up, say thanks, then head back home.

The venue is a renovated theater house downtown, dressed like a funeral’s dream. 

Black and white everywhere. Black roses in tall crystal vases. White candles that are so realistic they’re actually melting wax onto silver platters. 

As Rio’s come to expect, it smells like expensive champagne and too much perfume the moment she steps inside.

Somewhere in a far corner, a cello quartet plays a mournful version of what Rio’s pretty sure is The Phantom of the Opera. 

Jesus. This might just be the craziest, and somehow coolest, party she’s ever been to.

She weaves through the crowd, scanning the sea of black and white for Lilia, partly to thank her, mostly to anchor herself in this surreal scene. 

People weren’t kidding when they said Lilia throws the most lavish, over-the-top parties in fashion history.

Perhaps, this is her way of reminding New York’s fashionable elite exactly who she is, even if she purposely chooses to stay out of the spotlight.

Rio trades a few polite smiles. Some people nod back. Others just throw a look at her before moving on, probably wondering who she is.

Unlike the usual industry functions she’s been to, where she knows at least half the room, here almost every face is new. Just a few names she recognizes: editors, stylists, people who never miss a party.

She politely turns down champagne flutes offered by a handful of men in shiny suits and keeps walking. 

Right now, her only plan in mind is to find the elusive and legendary hostess, and perhaps cling to her for the rest of the night like a well-dressed barnacle.

Rio is halfway across the marble floor when the lights around her suddenly dim, and the music morphs into something slower, lusher, and less haunting: a swell of cello layered with a voice full of longing and velvet sadness. A ripple moves through the crowd as heads turn toward the center of the room, where the space clears like magic.

Then, from the high ceiling, long sheets of diaphanous silk — black, white, and ghost-gray — begin to float down, spinning gently like they have a mind of their own. 

They don’t fall so much as drift, slow and weightless, like spirits moving through the air in search of something long forgotten. 

The room pulses with strobe lights, casting everything in flashes of shadow and glow.

A figure in a floor-length white dress moves with the falling fabric, hidden beneath a wide-brimmed hat and veil, guiding the silk, indeed like spirits caught in her hands.

The room is silent, except for the music and a few soft gasps nearby. It’s beautiful, luminous, otherworldly, and Rio can’t look away.

She stops walking and somehow completely forgets what she came for. For a long suspended second, it’s just her and the performance in front of her. 

Then, as if she can feel her presence among the blur of people, her hazel eyes catch someone across the room, standing near one of the arched windows — looking as beautiful, as luminous, as otherworldly as the light allows.

Her face is tipped up toward the swirling silks. She’s dressed in a long, structured white coat-dress with a tailored, blazer-style top and soft lapels, while the bottom blooms into a full, sweeping skirt. It’s as if Rio is seeing her in a wedding gown that had fallen in love with a power suit.

Rio promptly goes still at the sight of the face she’d come to miss more than she realized, and it takes her a moment to believe what she’s seeing. Deep down, she had hoped to see her here. But only a small part of her truly believed she would.

When their eyes meet across the room, time doesn’t slow but stops altogether. Just for a breath. Just long enough to steal the air from Rio’s lungs. They move toward each other, meeting halfway between a marble pillar and a swan-shaped ice sculpture Rio couldn’t care less about.

“Hi,” Rio blurts, voice scratchy with things she’s not saying.

“Hi,” Agatha echoes, just as softly.

“You look…” Rio trails off, because what is she supposed to say? 

You look like everything I’ve been missing. And it’s only been a week, but I’ve come this close to hopping the subway and showing up at your door just to tell you how much I miss you.

“You clean up well yourself,” Agatha says instead, sensing Rio’s run out of words. “One of Lilia’s, I assume? I could tell by the cut,” she adds, gesturing to the sharp lines of the tux Rio is wearing.

Rio rubs the back of her neck. 

“She insisted.” Then, not wanting their conversation to end there, she adds what she should’ve said seconds ago. “You look really good, by the way. I mean, the color looks really good on you.”

Agatha smiles. “Oh, honey. Everything looks good on me.”

Rio blushes at the way she says it. God, she misses how Agatha’s voice can just drop like that, so natural and effortless. They stand there in silence for a beat before Rio blurts out, “I wasn’t sure you’d come.”

Something crosses Agatha’s face, and Rio is bold enough to assume it’s a bit of guilt. But Agatha shakes it off like she always does, brushing her curls back with a subtle shrug.

“I wasn’t entirely sure I’d come either. I’ve been in back-to-back meetings since the new issue dropped. But I also didn’t want to miss one of Lilia’s parties. It would’ve been a shame to miss the spectacle. And who knows how many more years we’ll have to wait before she decides to throw another one.” She looks around at the crowd surrounding them. 

Rio simply nods and looks at her. But there doesn’t seem to be a single coherent thought in her head while staring at Agatha, just one question repeating over and over: 

“Are you holding up okay?”

Agatha turns back to her, clearly surprised by the question. She doesn’t answer right away, and the silence stretches just enough to make Rio fill it. “I mean, how’s work? You said you’ve been in meetings nonstop. I was just wondering how you’ve been. I hope you’re taking care of yourself.”

Agatha meets the question with a small, unreadable smile. “Other people’s inefficiency and stupidity still follow me around, but I manage. This isn’t my first world exclusive, after all.” She pauses, then adds in a more businesslike tone, “You, on the other hand, how are you keeping up with all the attention? Have you decided which road you’re going to take, with all the publications lining up to get you under their wing?” 

Rio shrugs. “Not really.”

“Not really?”

“I mean, not yet.”

Agatha raises an eyebrow. “Why not?”

“There are a couple I’ve started talking to, but I haven’t really committed to any of them yet. I mean, I’m still thinking it through. Also, there are some freelancing offers that I, um, I might try first. They seem kind of promising and I’m—” 

“Rio.” The sound of her name from the other woman stops her mid-ramble. 

She then meets Agatha’s sapphire eyes again. 

“I know everything feels overwhelming right now, but don’t let any of it mess with your head, okay? Just because a lot of people are making offers doesn’t mean you have to say yes to something that doesn’t feel right. I mean, you’re doing great, taking your time, figuring it out. Choose what you really want, and build from there. You don’t have anything left to prove, do you understand? You’ve already done that. Now it’s about choosing what makes you happy.”

Rio lets Agatha’s words settle in. And damn it, she’s right. She always somehow is.

Like she knows the exact thing to say, even when Rio hasn’t fully figured out the feeling herself. It really is her choice now. Whatever road makes her feel like herself. Whatever makes her happy. 

But what if what truly makes Rio happy is for the woman standing right in front of her to finally realize that she has somehow, unexpectedly but inevitably, become Rio’s happiness?

Agatha seems to catch the look on Rio’s face and pauses. “What is it?”

Rio shakes her head, half-smiling. 

“Nothing. You’re just being oddly nice.” 

Agatha arches a brow. “Haven’t I always been?”

Rio huffs a soft laugh. “More than usual.”

“Well, I wouldn’t make a habit of expecting it.”

Before Rio can say something to keep the conversation going just a little longer, someone nearby calls Agatha’s name. She straightens almost instantly, slipping back into that polished, untouchable version of herself. “Looks like I’m needed elsewhere.” 

She takes a step, then glances over her shoulder. Rio expects her to say something, anything, that might quiet the storm in her head and the thudding ache beneath her ribs. 

But instead Agatha just says, “You might want to avoid the red punch, unless you feel like throwing up all night and waking up with a headache.”

That ends up being the last real conversation Rio has with Agatha all night, and she hates how ridiculously disappointed she feels because of it.

Eventually, she spots Lilia in the middle of a story, making a small group of guests laugh.

Lilia lights up when she sees her, pulling her in and introducing her like a proud grandma showing off her favorite granddaughter who just won something big.

They talk for a while, and Rio tries to stay present, but nothing seems to hold her attention. 

Not when Agatha is just a few feet away, smiling at people who aren’t Rio and making small talk with people who definitely aren’t Rio. And all Rio can do is watch from afar.

Is this how it’s going to be between them now? 

Just short, polite words at parties? Glimpses from across crowded rooms? Smiles that never quite reach the eyes? Like nothing ever almost happened between them? Like they hadn’t come so close to being something more? Like they never once looked at each other like the world had stopped spinning, just to make space for them, and them alone?

Lilia hands her a flute of champagne and a plate of delicate pastries Rio can’t even pronounce right — fancy little things that pull her out of her gloomy thoughts for a bit. 

But Lilia is the hostess, so it doesn’t take long before she’s swept away by more guests, more stories to tell, leaving Rio standing alone, lost in a crowd of suits and dresses. 

“And here I thought someone like you couldn’t possibly get any hotter.” 

Rio turns toward the voice, oddly relieved to see a familiar face. At least she won’t have to squeeze into a group and pretend she’s not quietly cringing at compliments from people who just found out who she is. 

“I have to say, fame suits you,” Hela adds. 

“This was all Lilia’s doing,” Rio nods to her tux, right as Hela swaps her empty glass for a full one.

“A million-dollar tux and a front-page exclusive. Talk about a winning streak,” Hela notes with a sly smile. “I’d wager every editor in New York is tripping over themselves to get you on staff. A bit exhausting, isn’t it? When the dream finally catches up, and suddenly you’re not sure if you can keep up?”

“I’m…getting used to it.”

Hela shoots her a look over the rim of her glass. “I hope you’re not having second thoughts about the pitch I laid out for you. A byline with us and the Post would make your resume practically bulletproof.”

Rio knows that. Her dad used to read these papers religiously. 

“I’d be lying if I said I didn’t want it. But I just need my first assignment to be something I can really sink my teeth into. If it is, then yeah, you’ll have my byline.”

“Oh, don’t worry. You’ll have more than enough to sink your teeth into. And trust me, it’s a smart move, career-wise,” Hela assures her. “Though, for a second there, I thought you’d crawl back to your old magazine and get buried in fashion again. A lot of people did, actually. Some even bet Agatha wouldn’t let you leave after that global exclusive.”

In a heartbeat, Rio’s eyes soften at the mention of Agatha’s name. “She didn’t think it would be fair to me if I stayed and kept writing about things she didn’t think I was as interested in.”

“Which definitely surprised a lot, just in case you haven’t heard the industry whispers.”

“I don’t think I’ve got enough connections yet to hear those.”

“Well, you’re about to.” Hela takes another slow sip of champagne. “Anyway, how are things going with the rotten apple of your eye? Now that you’re no longer with the magazine, I’m guessing HR’s not an issue anymore, which is lucky for you, ’cause you could kiss her stupid and no one would file a report.”

Rio nearly chokes on her own drink.

“I—what?”

“Aren’t you two already dating? I mean, if ‘dating’ is even a thing Agatha Harkness does.”

“Dating? No! Agatha and I are…we’re not—” Rio fumbles, eyes wide.

Hela chuckles and shakes her head. “Is that so? I could’ve sworn she’d have pounced on you by now.”

This time, Rio almost hacks up a lung. “Why would you even think that?”

“Because she clearly has feelings for you too.”

Rio’s jaw drops at Hela’s words. “No, she doesn’t. If anything, I think she’s just trying not to hate me.”

Even when they shared a kiss and perhaps a few more. 

Even when Agatha looked at her the way she always does when it’s just the two of them.

Even when there were little cracks that made Rio almost hope Hela was right. 

Even then, Rio tells herself it didn’t mean anything to Agatha.

Hela laughs, loud enough that a few people nearby glance over before turning back to their drinks. 

“I thought overnight fame would at least make you a little less clueless, but it seems nothing has changed. Then again, I can’t really blame you. That’s part of your faultless charm.”

When Rio just looks at her, Hela goes on, downing the rest of her champagne before swapping the empty flute for a fresh one from a passing tray. 

Rio wonders how someone can drink like that and still talk in full sentences.

“Agatha Harkness,” Hela states, slow and pointed, “is a power-hungry, terrifyingly well-dressed succubus whose entire life revolves around her magazine. And yet, she had in her hands a brand-new writer. Someone with barely a byline, who somehow became one of her best almost overnight. Someone she could’ve had wrapped around her finger without even trying. But instead of keeping her, as her reputation would suggest, she lets her go. Willingly. So that writer can chase her dreams. If that’s not screamingly obvious, Rio, I genuinely don’t know what is.”

Rio turns it over in her head. As absurd as it sounds, Hela’s words land somewhere stubborn in her chest and refuse to budge. And, like always, her mind circles back to the kiss.

Agatha kissed her back.

Not passively. Not indifferently. But longingly. 

But then why hasn’t either of them brought it up? Why has Agatha been acting like it never happened? 

Rio lets herself believe that perhaps it was just a moment, a strange, spontaneous blip brought on by adrenaline or gratitude. Perhaps kissing her back was Agatha’s twisted way of saying thank you for landing the exclusive.

Or perhaps it was merely pity.

Rio had been the one who leaned in first, after all. Perhaps Agatha didn’t want to embarrass her by pulling away. Or maybe it was simply something else entirely.

The truth is, Rio doesn’t know. And the more she tries to make sense of it, the less she understands.

Rio looks around and spots Agatha almost instantly, standing near the windows with a glass of wine in hand, half-listening to someone in a suit.

It had always been easy: finding her. Like Rio’s eyes had been trained to do it long ago.

She watches from a distance, and even across the room, nothing about Agatha slips past her. 

The way her eyes darken when she’s deep in thought. The faint scrunch of her nose when something fails to impress her.

And then there’s her smile. Rare, reluctant, as if it costs her something each time, yet still enough to make Rio feel as if the ground under her had moved.

Then she’s reminded of where they are, of how easily Agatha moves through this world. And Rio, by contrast, still feels like she’s fumbling her way through it. 

She shakes her head and turns back to Hela. “Even if she does, which I still don’t believe, I’m not the kind of person someone like her would want. We’re too different. And I’m just not worth the trouble.”

Hela lets out a long-suffering sigh and tilts her head back, like the ceiling might offer her more patience than Rio ever could.

She looks thoroughly exasperated, as if she’s speaking to the stupidest person in the room.

Rio pulls a face, wondering if Hela’s had one too many flutes of champagne before this. 

She’s about to make a comment about her alcohol intake when Hela cuts her off. 

“I haven’t the faintest idea where all this bullshit is coming from. But what I know is, you like her, and she likes you. Truly, why do we, as lesbians, always make things so needlessly more complicated than they need to be?”

With zero warning, Hela slips an arm around Rio’s waist, pulls her close, and presses a kiss to the corner of her mouth just as the lights drop for the next performance. 

Strobe lights burst across the room, camera flashes firing like fireworks. 

And out of the corner of her eye, Rio catches a glimpse of an image she wishes she hadn’t.

Agatha, still as a photograph, eyes locked on them while everyone else is looking the other way.

Before Rio can even have a heart attack, Hela pulls away with a wink, leaving her blinking like she just walked into a lamppost.

“What the hell was that for?”

“Just the starting pistol.” Rio wants to slap the grin right off the other woman's face as she says it, if she weren’t so thrown and still catching her breath. “We both know your woman likes to win. I just gave her a reason to realize what she’s about to lose if the two of you keep being this stubborn, slow, and stupid.”

Then she leans in, still grinning like a Cheshire cat, and Rio’s instinct is to take a small step back, but Hela is fast enough to cup her cheek.

“You’ll thank me later, darling.”

And with that, she strolls away like she didn’t just light a match and drop it into the dry kindling, with Rio standing right in the middle.

“It’s like the seventh circle of hell in here!” 

Rio winces and immediately yanks the phone away from her ear, stepping off the subway just in time to dodge someone who clearly never learned the basic courtesy of letting people exit before barging in.

“I don’t even know what set her off this time,” Jen tells her, then pants like she’s been running. Maybe she has, Rio thinks. “She came in looking like she hadn’t slept in a week and just started snapping at everyone. I think this might be a personal record for how many people she’s fired in a day. She even let go of three models before the shoot, two for being too tall and slender, and another just for having naturally warm blonde hair. Can you believe that?”

Rio perks up mid-step at the description. She knows someone tall, slender, and with naturally warm blonde hair. But she shoves the thought aside and keeps walking.

“Monica’s probably crying in the bathroom, Sue’s gone full statue in front of the mood boards, and we’re supposed to pull off eight looks with one model who looks two seconds away from bolting. I honestly don’t know how we’re getting through this shoot alive.”

There’s a loud clatter in the background, something falls, and Jen mutters a curse under her breath.

“Are you on your way? Please, please tell me you’re coming. And for the love of God, can you swing by Starbucks and grab her usual? Piping hot,” she says, then barrels on before Rio can even open her mouth. “I know you don’t technically work here anymore, but the assistant who replaced your replacement keeps messing up this one thing, and I cannot get thrown under the bus for it again. I’ve gone through four of them this month, and I am not about to train another full-grown toddler on training wheels.”

“But is now really the best time for me to show up there?” Rio manages to squeeze in a word as she heads up the stairs. “I mean, I can always come by and sign the rest of the papers another day.”

Rio might not admit it, but the way Jen’s describing things at Agatha’s office is starting to make her genuinely nervous.

And as much as she tries not to, she can’t help but wonder if this sudden rampage has anything to do with Hela kissing her last night.

“Oh god. She just snapped at Melina. Melina, Rio! That’s how bad it is here. I never even say please, but I’m begging you. Crawl, teleport, hitch a ride with a pigeon, I don’t care how you do it, just get your ass up here with her Starbucks. Or I’m faking a seizure and letting the paramedics carry me out.”

“Watch it!” someone snaps as Rio narrowly avoids bumping into them. 

She mutters an apology but hears Jen’s voice still crackling in her ear. 

“Five minutes, Rio! I need you here in five minutes.”

“But I—” Her protest quickly dies in her throat the second the call drops, just as she glances up and spots the familiar green logo staring directly at her across the street.

A few minutes later, Rio’s in the elevator, fidgeting with the coffee tray in her hands.

It oddly feels like the day after Pride all over again, her nerves fraying with every floor the metal box climbs.

And maybe she would’ve found the humor in it, if she hadn’t just nearly crashed into a crying, six-foot model wobbling in sky-high Louboutins.

“And here I thought you’d died. What took you so long?” Jen hisses the second she spots Rio approaching her desk. “Go. Just get in there. She genuinely looks like she’s about to breathe fire.”

Rio stops short, eyebrows shooting up. “Wait, why me? Shouldn’t you be the one giving this to her?” she asks, already halfway to shoving the coffee into Jen’s hands. But the latter quickly pulls them back.

“Because you’re ten minutes late when I told you I needed you here at five,” Jen snaps, all but shoving Rio toward the door. “If I walk in there with that cup, I’ll be walking out without a job. You, however, already got fired twice. So, consider yourself fireproof.”

Somehow, Rio miraculously manages to balance the coffee, even as Jen gives her a shove that nearly sends her stumbling into Agatha’s office.

And Jen hadn’t been exaggerating about Agatha’s mood when she walks in and sees the woman with her back towards her, standing by the glass window with her arms crossed, glaring down at the street like she’s about to crush every car and pedestrian beneath her.

“Hey,” Rio greets, a little too brightly, showing the gap in her front teeth like it might help. “I, uh, brought you coffee.” She walks over, sets it gently on the desk, then takes a careful step back.

Agatha barely throws her stormy eyes at her before dropping into her chair and dives straight into her laptop, fingers flying over the keys like she’s typing out a grudge letter by letter.

“You must’ve missed the joy of fetching lattes,” she comments, not bothering to look up. “Last I checked, you no longer work here, unless, of course, you’ve taken up delivering coffee as a charitable endeavor.” 

Rio feels the chill of her voice run down her spine, colder than the AC humming in the corner. 

“I was already on my way, so—” 

“I wasn’t really asking,” Agatha says dryly, and Rio slowly tucks her hands behind her back. 

Instead of saying more, Rio waits for Agatha to speak again, but the latter just picks up the coffee, takes a sip, and starts hammering away at her keyboard again.

Rio watches her, unsure if she’s actually typing something or if the screen’s just full of angry gibberish. Either way, her former boss is definitely pissed.

Growing a little uncomfortable with the silence and angry tapping of the keyboard, Rio opens her mouth to speak, only for Agatha to pull her hand from the keys and push a folder across the desk toward her, still without looking up. 

“These are the final documents you need to sign,” she begins, her tone more clipped than usual. “A standard post-publication release, confirming that the rights to your article remain with the publisher. Customary, especially for first-time contributors.”

Rio steps forward and grabs the folder, flipping it open to scan the first page.

“You’ll find the full payment breakdown enclosed,” Agatha continues. “Now that the issue’s out, the remainder of your fee is being processed. It should reach your account by the end of the week.”

Rio flips through the pages slowly, eyes skimming the fine print even though she already knows she’s going to sign it.

Her first instinct is to get it over with, but some stubborn part of her brain keeps telling her to take her time, to stay just a little longer.

“I don’t see anything about reader metrics or reach. Will I ever get those?”

“You’ll receive a performance report in sixty days. Circulation numbers, site analytics, demographic breakdowns. Everything you’d expect on that front. We just don’t release projections until after the second wave of press. I figured you knew that,” Agatha answers, still focused on her screen, or pretending to be, as Rio notices.

And sure, Rio does know that. But she’s not about to walk out without Agatha at least glancing her way.

She clears her throat, tossing out another question even though she already knows the answer. “Just to be clear, the exclusivity clause means only Nocturne gets to publish it, right? No syndication deals?”

Agatha furrows her brows at that, still not looking at Rio, seemingly unaware of what she’s trying to do. “It was a global exclusive. That means no reprints in other magazines, no overseas editions, and definitely no syndication. The embargo covered all of that, as you know full well.”

Rio nods and pretends to flip to the next page. She bites her lip, hesitating before voicing another seemingly stupid inquiry. “And the online version stays up indefinitely? Or is it pulled after a while?”

“It’ll remain in the digital archive, same as print. Standard policy for cover features.”
