“So that’s it, then? It’s out, done, and over with?” Rio asks again, hazel eyes still on Agatha, who seems hell-bent on avoiding eye contact for the entirety of their conversation.

“As far as the publisher is concerned, yes.” Agatha sips her coffee, still without looking at Rio.

Rio presses her tongue to the inside of her cheek, pausing again before saying anything. 

It might be her dumbest question yet, but it’s the only one left in her head, and the only one she thinks might finally get the woman in front of her to look up.

“Did I do something wrong?”

That causes Agatha to pause. Her fingers hover mid-air, frozen between keystrokes.

For a beat, she just stares at the screen, schooling her face into its usual inscrutable expression. Then, as if the question had not touched her at all, she resumes typing.

Rio lets out a long, tired sigh, suddenly feeling just bold enough, perhaps foolish enough, to steer the conversation toward her early hypothesis. “If this is about last night—”

“Don’t,” Agatha cuts in, cold and immediate. “I couldn’t care less about what you were up to last night.”

Rio pushes anyway. “I know you saw us.” She swallows hard, then adds, “But whatever you think that was, it wasn’t. She was just messing around. Trust me, it didn’t mean anything. Hela and I aren’t even—”

Agatha stills again, but this time, her hands drop to the desk. 

“I told you once that whatever you do outside these walls is none of my concern. And now that you’re no longer part of this company, that sentiment applies even more. I don’t care what alpaca you let suck on your tongue, and I certainly don’t care about you and your reckless, flighty, attention-seeking lips.”

“I didn’t—” Rio stands there, a little stunned, only just beginning to believe that Agatha’s rampage might actually be about her kiss with Hela. “I just thought you deserved to know that it wasn’t—”

“Rio.”

This time, Agatha finally looks up. Her storm-bitten blue eyes meet Rio’s, and lately, more than ever, Rio can’t tell what’s behind them. Only that something’s there, tucked too far back for her to reach.

“Let’s not pretend whatever happened between us mattered enough to owe each other explanations.” 

This is the first time Agatha has ever brought up their almost — the thing Rio had once been desperate to talk about, desperate for Agatha to acknowledge, but also the one that apparently didn’t matter enough. 

And now that it’s out in the open, all she wants is for Agatha to take it back.

“Now, if you’re done wasting my time with your questions, I believe you still owe me a signature,” Agatha presses on, nodding toward the papers.

Without a word, Rio picks up the pen, signs in angry loops, and sets it down, just short of slamming it. 

She then heads for the door, but stops once, her jaw clenched as she looks back.

“Well, for the record,” she snaps, fists curled tight at her sides, “you don’t get to call my lips attention-seeking when you used to look at them like…” She cuts herself off and shakes her head. “You know what, forget it. You’re Agatha fucking Harkness. The truth only matters when it serves you,” she scoffs, and storms out without another glance.

Rio is well aware she could’ve said all that a little less harshly. Then again, there’s only so much you can do when your better judgment gets drowned out by a pissed-off mouth.

Instead of going home and dumping whatever lousy, godawful energy she picked up after talking to Agatha on Alice, and probably Billy, Rio lets her feet take over. 

She spends the rest of her day drifting through the streets of New York, aimlessly kicking dented soda cans and nursing bitter thoughts, until she stumbles on a half-hidden speakeasy tucked behind a flower shop just off West 11th.

By the time her third sazerac is sweating in her hand, her phone lights up on the bar. Her brows knit together, and the drink suddenly tastes warm and bitter in her mouth.

Agatha’s name blares on the screen, the answer button practically daring Rio to do something stupid. 

But lucky for her, she’s not drunk enough for that kind of stupidity yet. 

So she ignores it, lets it ring out, and leaves it to go to voicemail.

It doesn’t even take three seconds before her phone lights up again. This time, it’s a text.

Agatha: You left one document unsigned. Could you return to the office to take care of it?

Rio scoffs and catches the time glowing at the top of her screen. It’s already past eight. She closes the app with a flick of her thumb and sets the phone face down.

But not even a full minute passes before the phone buzzes again, skittering slightly against the wood. 

Agatha: Legal needs this on their desk by morning.

Rio still doesn’t bother typing a reply and sets her phone back down on the bar.

If Agatha thinks Rio is going to march all the way back to the office at this hour over one unsigned page, and especially after everything that was said earlier, then she’s sorely mistaken. 

But then, because she knows exactly how relentless and annoyingly persistent her former boss can be, Rio sighs, picks the phone back up, turns off all notifications, and shoves it deep into her jacket pocket, just as the bartender slides a fresh drink toward her.

“Rough day?” he asks.

She taps a finger against the rim of her glass and drinks. “Something like that.”

Another hour passes, maybe two, maybe more, Rio can't really tell.

But the warmth in her limbs and the slow, lazy spin in her head tell her she’s definitely had more than enough to drink.

However, when she finally reaches for her wallet to settle the tab, her fingers meet nothing but empty fabric.

Her brows pull together in confusion.

She checks her other pocket. Then the other. Then again, just to be sure she didn’t miss it. Still nothing.

A simmering panic starts to bubble up as she pats herself down: jacket, pants, inner lining, back pockets. She even leans sideways to peek under the bar stool, just in case. But there’s no sign of it anywhere. 

Running a hand through her hair, she tries to retrace her steps in her mind, thinking hard about where she could have left it. 

Slowly, and to the utter horror of anyone who decides to drink alone on a whim, she comes to the conclusion that she must’ve dropped it somewhere earlier during her angry little walk through the city, when she wasn’t paying attention to anything else except her own thoughts.

“Shit,” she mutters under her breath. “You gotta be kidding me. Shit, shit.” 

She blows out a breath and digs into her pocket for her phone, fingers clumsy and slower than she wants them to be.

Her head’s swimming just enough to make everything feel a beat off. She then curses herself for having one drink too many. Then curses Agatha for this stupid chain reaction of a day. 

Easier to blame it on Agatha anyway, Rio thinks.

She flips to her recents, taps the first name she sees, and holds the phone to her ear, silently praying to whatever version of God might still be awake on a Friday night that Alice picks up.

The phone rings once, twice, three times, then, to Rio’s shaky relief, Alice finally picks up on the fourth.

“Hey, Al,” she says, then immediately hiccups. Great. Now Alice would know instantly just how far gone she is. The hiccups have always been a dead giveaway, always hitting when Rio is past tipsy and heading straight into should’ve stopped two drinks ago territory. 

Her ears are hot now, and she can feel the flush rising in her cheeks and up the back of her neck. She rubs it instinctively, as if that might somehow cool her down.

“I, uh, kinda lost my wallet,” she mutters, glancing around the bar like it might turn up if she just looks hard enough. “I’m at this bar. It’s behind a little flower shop, somewhere off Eleventh. It’s called the Burning Bush. I think. Or something like that.” A breathy laugh slips out of her. Jesus, she’s definitely drunk. “Can you come get me? Please? And before you ask why I’m here, I’ll explain. Later.”

Rio’s brows draw together when the other end stays quiet a little too long. “Hello?” she asks. “Alice? You still there?” She knows the call connected. Alice had definitely picked up. But just as she pulls the phone back to check if the line dropped or if Alice hung up on her, the phone dies in her hand.

“Fuck,” she hisses, then lets out a bitter little laugh as she thunks her forehead against the bar. 

This is definitely not her brightest night. 

She stays like that, forehead pressed to the wood, stewing in the realization that getting drunk alone without thinking it through was a very, very stupid idea. 

On a normal, sober night, she would’ve figured something out by now.

She’s usually good at that.

But she’s drunk, walletless, and completely cut off from the one person who might’ve helped.

Okay, maybe, on the bright side, if Rio keeps betting on the better parts of people, the universe might throw her a bone.

Maybe some kind stranger will spot her and offer help. Or maybe the bartender, out of sheer pity or mercy, will wave off the tab and call her a cab home. 

It’s not that far-fetched. New York isn’t completely heartless.

She isn’t sure how long she’s been sitting like this: forehead pressed to the bar, arms folded like a shield, when she senses someone step up beside her.

She hears the soft click of heels break through her haze, and registers a faint presence in her periphery.

Her head’s getting fuzzier, and she barely catches the sound of someone speaking beside her.

“I’ll take care of her tab.”

Rio lifts her head slowly, squinting through the strands of hair falling into her eyes. 

And even if every block of ice in the bar’s backroom freezer had been dumped over her, it still wouldn’t match the chill that shoots down her spine the moment she recognizes the face.

“What are you doing here?” she hisses, straining her already half-lidded eyes. Stupid lightweight genetics.

Her thoughts scatter, and all she can really register are those familiar blue eyes, staring right back at her.

They look calmer now, or maybe that’s just the lighting. But she still can’t tell if the storm from earlier has passed or if it’s just lying low.

Agatha’s lips are drawn in a tight, unreadable line. Is she still as angry as Rio is? Hard to tell. Rio’s drunken brain isn’t exactly the most reliable source right now.

“You called,” Agatha says, watching her while the bartender swipes her card.

Rio frowns. “No, I didn’t. Not to you, anyway.”

“Yes, you did,” Agatha says, just as the bartender returns and hands it over. “Though I’m guessing you meant to call Alice.”

Rio blinks, and her stomach drops as the pieces slowly start to come together. She hadn’t even looked at which name she tapped earlier. “Oh, shit,” she mutters, running a hand down her face.

Agatha slips her card back into her own purse. 

“I hate to interrupt whatever…party you’ve decided to throw for yourself, but it’s time to go.”

Rio snorts. “I’m not going anywhere with you.” 

It’s only then that she really notices how out of place Agatha looks in here, with her long jet black trench coat and blood-red pumps that have definitely never seen a sticky bar floor.

“Yes, you are. I just saved your ass, and I’d prefer not to waste the effort.”

Rio turns back to the bar. “Which, by the way, I clearly didn’t need you to do. I’ll pay you back tomorrow. Now, if you don’t mind, you can go. I can handle my own shit.”

“If you could, I wouldn’t be here. You’re drunk. Your phone is dead. You’re in a bar you can’t pay for. If this is you handling your shit, I’d hate to see the alternative.”

Before Rio can fire back, the bartender leans in and nods toward Agatha. 

“You should probably go with your girlfriend, sweetheart.”

“She’s not my girlfriend!” Rio whips her head toward him. “And I’m not your sweetheart.”

The bartender raises his hands in surrender, and Rio sighs. 

Great. Now she’s picking fights with bartenders. 

She presses her fingers to her temple, trying to will away the slow throb building behind her eyes, then turns back to Agatha. “I really don’t need a babysitter. You can go home.”

“Not when you’re acting like someone who clearly does.” And before Rio can even come up with a comeback strong enough to knock her off her pedestal, Agatha adds, “There’s a car parked outside. You can argue with me here, on the sidewalk, or in the passenger seat of a warm Mercedes. Your choice.”

“Again, I’m not going anywhere with you, Agatha.” 

Agatha exhales slowly, in a manner someone does when they’re trying very hard not to roll their eyes. 

“You know I could easily pay someone here to carry you to my car. It would take all of thirty seconds.” Then, softer, but still unbending. “But I’d rather not do that. So I’m giving you a choice. Walk out with me like a functioning adult, or be dragged out and cause a scene. Either way, we’re both leaving.”

Rio knows Agatha doesn’t bluff. She makes a threat, and follows through.

With a groggy sweep of her half-lidded eyes, Rio scans the bar. Just her luck: it’s full of guys who could probably lift her without breaking a sweat, even if she kicked and screamed the whole way.

She looks down at the empty glass in front of her. Then at the dead, useless rectangle that is her phone. Then, finally, back up at Agatha’s expectant, unmoved face. 

Rio groans and drops her head onto the counter again.

“I hate you.” Her voice is muffled but she knows Agatha heard it.

“Well, you wouldn’t be the first.”

There’s a pause. Then Rio stands and brushes past her, stumbling a little but ignoring the arm that reaches out to steady her.

Good thing Agatha doesn’t insist. She simply follows.

So this is what it feels like to walk ahead of her former formidable boss instead of behind. 

Too bad she’s too angry, and too goddamn drunk, to revel in it.

True to Agatha’s word, there’s a car parked out front. But this time, Rio immediately notices there’s no Javier waiting inside.

Did Agatha actually drive here herself?

“Where’s your driver?”

“Home with his family.” 

“And you didn’t call him to drive you?”

“I’m not a monster. And I figured you’d prefer I not ruin his night, too,” Agatha says, already opening the car door like it’s an order, not a suggestion. “Get in.”

Rio crosses her arms. “I’m not getting in that car.”

“I thought we already established that I’m the only adult in charge tonight. Get in the car, Rio.”

“I’d rather call a cab than get in that car with you.”

Rio had been cursing the alcohol ten minutes ago, but now she’s kind of grateful for it, because somehow, she’s managing to hold her ground against the unshakable Agatha Harkness. 

God bless liquid courage.

Agatha raises an eyebrow. 

“Your phone is dead. You don’t have your wallet. How do you plan to pay for that, exactly?”

Rio hiccups and immediately wants to disappear. If only said liquid courage came with a halfway functional brain to match. This is beyond embarrassing.

“Fine. Can I borrow ten bucks?” 

Not exactly the power move she was hoping for.

It doesn’t help that she catches the tiniest twitch at the corner of Agatha’s mouth.

Oh, Jesus. She’s finding this funny, isn’t she? The more she thinks about it, the more Rio wants to sink straight into the pavement and never come back up.

“Adorable, but no.” She schools her face into something more serious again. “Now stop wasting both our time and just get in.”

Rio stays planted, arms crossed, glaring and pouting like a kid refusing to get in the car after a bad day at school.

Agatha lets out an exhausted sigh. “Can we be done with the tantrum, please? I’d rather not be photographed here looking like I just dragged a college student out of a divebar.”

Another beat. Rio still doesn’t move. 

If she could tie herself to the doorframe, she would. 

Actually…that’s starting to sound like a solid plan.

But apparently, she’s pushed her luck far enough, because the next thing she knows, Agatha grabs her by the arm with all the calm of someone absolutely done.

“Alright, that’s it! I’ve had enough. In the car, now.”

“Ow,” Rio complains loudly, mostly for show. But Agatha’s already steering her toward the seat, one hand slipping behind her head so she doesn’t smack it on the way in.

She tells herself not to blush. Really, she tries. But a small, annoying part of her kind of wants to.

“Stay,” Agatha states, pointing at her. Their faces just inches apart as she clicks Rio’s seatbelt into place.

Rio fights the urge to swallow.

Agatha lingers for a second, then finally pulls away and heads for the driver’s seat.

“I can’t believe I’m doing this,” Rio hears her grumble just before the door shuts.

Rio doesn’t remember when she fell asleep, just that it was raining outside, the window glass was cold against her temple, and her head hurt like hell.

She only stirs when the car slows to a stop and the engine goes quiet. She blinks at the familiar townhouse outside.

“Why are we at your place?” she mumbles, still half-asleep.

“I couldn’t remember how to get to your apartment. Turns out having a driver for years kind of kills your sense of direction,” Agatha mutters, and Rio knows she’s right.

This is actually the first time she’s ever seen Agatha drive, and she’s not even sure if the woman has a license.

“You could’ve woken me up,” Rio grumbles, then winces. “God—my head.”

“Well, we’re here now, so unless you want to sleep in the car, stop complaining and come inside.”

Before Rio can even argue, Agatha grabs the umbrella from the backseat, circles around the car, and opens the door for her.

“Here, put your arm around me.” They squeeze under the same umbrella as they head up the stairs to Agatha’s front door and step inside the house.

They’re not soaked, but they’re not exactly dry either.

“Stay here. I’m getting a towel,” Agatha says, slipping off her trench coat, kicking off her heels, and leaving Rio on the couch as she heads upstairs.

It doesn’t take long before Agatha comes back to the living room.

She wraps the towel around Rio without saying a word, and Rio’s too out of it to even think about protesting. But even if she weren’t, she probably wouldn’t.

Because something about this: Agatha being gentle, quietly taking care of her, like they’re just two normal people, makes her want to stay right here.

Even with all the anger still buzzing under her skin, Rio can’t help it. 

She still wants this. Still wants her .

“Take off your shirt,” Agatha tells her, snapping Rio out of her daze momentarily. 

She blinks up at her, just as Agatha finishes towel-drying her short hair.

Realizing how that sounded, Agatha quickly adds, “I mean, your clothes are soaked. You need to change, or you’ll catch a cold. Here.” She holds out a soft, worn T-shirt. “It’s clean. Just…yeah.”

She turns away slightly, giving Rio her version of privacy.

Rio hesitates, then slowly peels off the damp shirt and pulls on the one Agatha gave her.

It’s soft, a little oversized, and smells devastatingly like Agatha and she has to physically stop herself from moaning like some kind of lovesick idiot. 

Once it’s over her head and settled on her shoulders, she clears her throat. “You can turn around now.” 

Agatha does. She looks like she’s about to say something, but stops. 

Instead, Rio picks up the towel and gently pats at Agatha’s damp hair, brushing it off her shoulders. When Agatha doesn’t pull away, she keeps going.

“You didn’t have to come get me,” Rio mumbles, mostly to herself. The alcohol’s making her drowsy again, but even through the haze, she can feel the silence between them sitting heavy in her chest.

“I know,” Agatha says honestly, her eyes never leaving Rio.

“Then why did you?”

Agatha doesn’t answer.

The scene from the office earlier flashes back in Rio’s mind. If everything that had happened didn’t mean anything to Agatha, then why did it still feel like it did? Like it still does.

In the way she speaks to her when she thinks Rio needs gentleness. In the way her hands linger when they touch. In the way her eyes seem to tell the truth her mouth refuses to.

They sit there, facing each other in silence, both waiting for the other to speak, while their eyes do all the talking.

Rain taps against the windows, and thunder starts to roll somewhere far off.

Rio’s voice cracks before she can stop it.

“Why don’t you want me?”

Agatha freezes, like she didn’t expect the words. “I…” Her mouth opens, then closes again. Her eyes drop to the floor. “I’ll just…get the guest room sorted.”

She stands and walks out before Rio can ask anything else.

Rio slumps against the arm of the couch, the towel still balled in her lap, and the sweet scent of Agatha’s shirt begins to cling stubbornly to her skin. She shuts her eyes.

When Rio wakes up for the second time that night, the house greets her with its usual silence.

It’s still raining outside and the thunder hasn’t let up either. 

People should probably be worried. New York’s weather is starting to screw around.

She shifts on the couch, a blanket now draped over her chest. Then her eyes dart to the big wall clock. It’s already three in the morning. 

Her head is still throbbing, but her gut tells her she needs to get out of here.

Rain or not, she doesn’t care, she’ll walk through it if she has to. She just doesn’t want to wake up and see Agatha’s face in the morning.

And Agatha probably feels the same way.

She slips on the shoes she kicked off earlier and heads down the hallway, moving slow and careful, even though she probably doesn’t need to, since Agatha’s likely asleep upstairs.

But just as she nears the door, a voice calls out from the kitchen.

“Rio? Is that you?”

She stops. Why the hell is Agatha still awake?

Rio doesn’t answer. For a second, she wonders if there’s someone else in the house. But the silence says otherwise. She shakes it off and keeps walking.

“It’s still raining,” Agatha calls out, her voice making it clear she hasn’t slept yet. “You’re not gonna find a cab outside at this hour. And walking nine miles in this weather isn’t exactly smart.” 

Rio sighs. She hates that Agatha has a point, a point she refuses to acknowledge.

“I’m not exactly aiming for smart,” she shouts back, not bothering to turn around.

From the kitchen, Agatha fires back without missing a beat. 

“And how’s that been working out for you so far?”

Rio spins halfway, ready to snap something equally biting. 

But before she can, Agatha’s voice cuts in again. “Will you just come in here?”

Rio rolls her eyes at the way Agatha makes it sound like a command, like she’s so sure Rio will listen.

She decides to ignore it, hand already on the doorknob, when Agatha adds, “Please, Rio.”

Rio fucking hates how all it takes to make her cave is Agatha Harkness saying please, with the added cruelty of tacking her name onto it. Like some magic spell that cracks straight through her defenses.

She groans under her breath, fists clenching like she might punch a wall, or herself. Then she sighs, mutters something unflattering, and pads toward the kitchen. 

As she rounds the corner, Rio finds Agatha at the kitchen counter, a half-full glass of red wine in hand, a book resting beside the open bottle. 

She’s in a matching set of soft olive pajama shirt and shorts, glasses perched on her nose, and soft waves of hair falling messily around her face in that unfairly perfect way that makes Rio maybe want to stare a little longer than she should.

Agatha doesn’t say anything when Rio sits down across from her. She just stands, grabs a clean glass, and fills it with water instead of wine. She then places it in front of her.

“I’m not thirsty,” Rio lies. Her throat feels like sandpaper.

Agatha doesn’t even look up. “Do I have to make you drink it like a five-year-old?”

Rio sighs, dragging the glass toward her. “Fine.” She drinks, and the second the water hits her tongue, it’s like her whole body remembers how much it needed it.

Like she’s just been dragged out of a goddamn desert somewhere in Arizona. She downs the whole thing in three seconds flat.

Agatha just hums, not even trying to hide the smugness. She sets the pitcher down in front of them without saying anything else. And Rio quietly pours herself another glass.

After a full second of Rio audibly gulping her water, Agatha says, “You’re probably starving too.”

“I’m fine,” Rio counters stubbornly, too fast and too defensive, praying her stomach doesn’t pull the same stunt it did last time Agatha asked her that. 

It’s bad enough she just drank like a dehydrated animal in front of her. She doesn’t need a repeat of Agatha hearing her stomach growling loud enough to be heard across the room.

She already feels like a stray cat getting adopted by a rich, elegant cat lady.

If the cat lady also happened to be terrifying, beautiful, and the exact kind of person who makes Rio feel confused, hurt, embarrassed, flustered, and just plain crazy.

Agatha raises an eyebrow but doesn’t argue. Instead, she takes another sip of wine, rests her elbows on the counter, and goes back to her book. 

Meanwhile, Rio shifts in her seat, suddenly too aware of how the oversized shirt keeps slipping off her shoulder.

She glances at Agatha, watching her for a moment too long before clearing her throat and turning toward the window, focusing on the soft patter of rain against the glass.

The silence stretches between them, almost peaceful and calm, until a low, deep rumble of thunder rolls in and breaks it.

Just as Rio predicted, Agatha flinches.

She shuts her eyes almost instantly, holds them shut for a bit, then opens them again and takes a small breath, which Rio wouldn’t have noticed if she hadn’t already been watching.

“Is this why you’re still awake?” Rio asks.

Agatha doesn’t look up. “One of a few reasons.”

Rio props her elbow on the counter, resting her cheek against her hand as she watches Agatha. 

She’s always wondered why the sound of thunder seemed to rattle someone usually so composed. 

The question has been sitting with her for a while, ever since that night at the hotel, but she’s never been brave enough to ask.

And she doesn’t want to push. Not now, especially, when the chances of Agatha actually opening up feel close to zero.

Then, to her surprise, Agatha speaks.

“When I was a kid, I used to love playing in the rain,” she starts, eyes still on her book. “But only when I was lucky enough to get the chance. Usually when my mother was away on a church retreat with her friends and my father was out on a business trip or working late. I’d sneak past the nannies and into Marmee’s backyard. Just run around out there for hours until I was soaked and covered in mud.”

A small smile slowly forms on Rio’s face as she pictures little Agatha, soaked and muddy, running around in the rain.

She and Alice used to do the same thing when they were kids. But the thought of Agatha not being able to do it freely the way a kid should, dulls the smile just as quickly. 

“I was nine when I told my mother I thought this new girl from church was pretty. With her pigtails and little blue dress,” Agatha goes on. “I didn’t even really understand what I was saying. I didn’t even know I liked girls yet. I just thought she was simply pretty.”

She still doesn’t look at Rio when she says it.

“That’s why I was so confused when my mother locked me in my room after that and made me fast for three days. Said I shouldn’t be entertaining ‘iniquitous’ thoughts.” She lets out a dry laugh. “I was a very smart kid, but even I didn’t know what the hell that word meant.”

Rio feels something twist in her gut. How could a mother do something like that to her own child?

“But that wasn’t the worst part,” Agatha continues, and she looks like she’s using every bit of courage just to say it out loud. Rio almost opens her mouth to tell her she doesn’t have to share it if she doesn’t want to, but Agatha pushes through anyway. 

“She ignored me for weeks. Then one night, there was a storm. Thunder so loud it shook the windows. She told me that if I was still thinking sinful thoughts…God would hear me clearer if I was outside.”

Rio’s chest stays still, bracing for what she already suspects comes next. Can a mother really be that cruel to her own flesh and blood?

“She dragged me into the yard. Barefoot. Still in my nightgown. Locked the door and left me there,” she carries on, still not looking at her. “I stood there for hours. Soaked, shivering, begging God to stop being mad at me, even though I didn’t understand what I’d done wrong. I prayed for the rain to stop. The storm. The thunder. Or whatever it was in me that made my own mother hate me so suddenly. But it didn’t. I just cried until I made myself sick.”

She turns toward the window, eyes following the rain as she slowly swirls the wine in her glass.

“I was nine,” she repeats, probably thinking the same question Rio is. 

How could anyone do that to a child?

Rio doesn’t say a word. Because really, what can you say to something like that? 

Now, all she can think about is every time she stood face to face with Evanora, and how stupid she was not to sock that woman straight in the jaw while she had the chance.

Agatha drains the last of her wine and sets the glass down. “Anyway. Now you know.” 

Agatha pours herself another glass, but Rio notices the way her shoulders have gone more rigid.

“What about your dad?” Rio finally asks, “Didn’t he find out?”

“There are a lot of things my father doesn’t know about me,” Agatha answers, with none of the warmth Rio usually has when she talks about her own parents. “Whether it’s because he really doesn’t, or simply because he just doesn’t care enough to.”

“And Marmee?”

“They weren’t home that night,” says Agatha. “And I never told them. I knew Marmee and Henry would’ve tried to stand up for me, but I also knew what my mother was capable of. So, I didn’t say anything.” She pauses, swirling her wine again. “But that was it. That was the worst thing my mother ever did to me as a child. After that, I slowly started making her life hell. So, I think I still got even.”

She gives Rio a faint, dry smile, but Rio can’t bring herself to return it. “I’m sorry,” she tells her. “I’m really sorry you had to go through that.”

Agatha doesn’t say anything. She just lifts her glass in acknowledgment, and drinks.

Nothing is said for a while, until Agatha sets her glass down again, the sound almost lost in the rain.

“I’m sorry,” she says, not quite looking at Rio. “For what I said earlier. At the office. I was wrong for saying things I knew would upset you.”

Rio doesn’t look at her either. “Yeah, you’ve made a habit of that lately. Saying the wrong things.” 

“Only because I never know how to say the right ones when it’s you.”

Rio doesn’t know how to respond to that. 

There are still parts of this conundrum in front of her — this impossible, infuriating, terrifying, beautiful, and deeply guarded woman — that she doesn’t fully understand. Agatha says one thing, means another, and holds the rest close to her chest. 

But for reasons Rio can’t always explain, she still wants to keep trying. Even when it’s confusing. Even when it’s hard.

Something in her keeps choosing to understand Agatha, over and over, again and again.

Then Agatha finally looks at her and closes her book. “Well,” she says, and Rio can already tell she’s about to change the subject. “Are you going to explain why that woman kissed you?”

Surprise jolts through Rio. “I—” Hela kissing her was the last thing she thought Agatha would bring up again. “I thought you said we didn’t owe each other explanations,” she answers, blinking at her.

“Wasn’t that also what my apology was for?” Agatha lifts one of her brows.

Rio tries not to visibly cheer at the fact that, in her own guarded and roundabout way, Agatha is taking back what she said.

That what happened between them matters enough for her to care that Rio’s lips were on someone else.

That seeing Rio with another woman got under her skin enough to need an explanation.

Which totally goes against what she said earlier that upset Rio in the first place.

“I mean, I already told you, it was nothing.”

“That doesn’t really tell me anything.”

“It tells you everything.” Rio meets her eyes, hoping Agatha can see how earnest she is.

“So, you’re not into her?”

“And why would I be? When all I’ve been thinking about is you?”

Rio feels her stomach twist in a way that’s hard to name. It’s the first time she’s laid her cards out so clearly in front of Agatha, and the woman just stares at her, inanimate and unmoving.

For a second, Rio wonders if Agatha can hear her heart pounding from across the counter.

Agatha clears her throat, sets her reading glasses down, and rises to her feet. 

“I’m going to bed,” she announces.

And Rio tries and fails to keep the disappointment off her face. 

Her eyes drop to Agatha’s abandoned wine glass, unsure now if she said too much.

But right before disappearing down the hall, Agatha stops and throws a glance over her shoulder.

“Well? Are you coming or not?”

Rio’s head snaps up in Agatha’s direction. It takes her a second to process what she just heard.

“I—what?” 

She crosses her arms, eyes locked on Rio the entire time. 

“To bed. Unless you’re feeling especially attached to that couch.”

Rio opens her mouth but then shuts it again, too stunned to come up with anything clever. Her heart’s pounding loud in her ears as she slowly stands, legs almost unsure beneath her. And she walks toward Agatha before her brain can even make sense of why.

“I’ll be fine on the couch. Really.” 

Rio wants to slap herself for that answer. Either she’s being delusional for reading too much into what Agatha just said, or she’s being dumb for pretending it didn’t sound exactly like an invitation. 

Either way, one of them is being vague on purpose, and Rio can’t tell if it’s Agatha, or just her own hopeful imagination getting ahead of her.

“Are you sure?” Rio can only nod as Agatha suddenly moves in front of her, close enough that her back nearly hits the wall. “I don’t think you are, honey,” Agatha adds, and she steps even closer.

She then leans her elbows on the counter, warming her hands on the cup before looking up. “I’ve got a piece coming out in the Journal in a few weeks,” she tells Agatha, and sees her perk up a little. “The Post too. Just waiting for them to throw me an assignment.”

“That’s good,” Agatha nods in response. “So you’re actually committing to freelancing, then?”

“Well,” Rio clears her throat, fiddling with the handle of her mug, “it just feels like the most doable thing for me right now.” She shrugs. “And it’s kind of nice, waking up and not having to answer to anyone.” She grins when she sees Agatha raise an eyebrow at that. “But I did also send out a bunch of resumes to other outlets too. Just to see.”

Agatha hums, her finger absently tracing the rim of her mug.

“That’s smart. Keeping your options open,” she says, glancing up at Rio. “Also sensible, since you’d be wasting your reach if you settled this early, especially when half the field is already circling and trying to get you on their byline.”

Rio gives a lopsided smile, but drops her eyes to her coffee, trying to hide the way her cheeks warm.

Agatha squints slightly. “What?”

“Nothing,” Rio mutters, still ducking her head. “I’m just...not really used to praise, I guess.”

Agatha quirks a brow. “Didn’t I just spend the better part of the night giving you plenty?”

Rio blushes so fast it’s almost comical. Jesus, this woman is going to be the death of her.

Agatha laughs, clearly pleased by the reaction. Then her laugh softens into a small, fond smile. “But all that aside...it’s just my way of saying I’m proud of you.”

Rio’s face somehow gets even redder, warmth spreading across her cheeks as she ducks her head, flustered beyond saving.

Agatha laughs again, clearly amused, and for a brief second the kitchen feels light and full in a way Rio doesn’t quite have words for. 

Oh, Rio could stay here, right here, for who knows how long and never want to leave. 

That thought dawns on her, and she must be making some weird, sappy face because Agatha’s laughter slows and her eyes settle on her. Suddenly, Rio wonders if she is thinking the same thing. 

Would Agatha want to stop time too, stay like this, be with Rio?

But before Rio can follow the thought too far, Agatha’s phone lights up and rings across the counter, snapping her out of it. The other woman picks it up with a frown. 

“Sorry. I need to take this. I’ll be right back.” 

Agatha stands and walks off, phone to her ear. “Ah, yes, Pepper, darling. Bright and early as always. What do I owe the pleasure this time?” Her voice slips into that overly polite, sweet-as-syrup tone she uses for people she’d rather not deal with but has to.

Rio can’t help but smile as she watches her disappear down the hall.

When Agatha returns several minutes later, Rio’s finished eating and is nursing the last of her coffee. 

Agatha sets her phone down with a sigh and takes the seat across from her again.

“My lunch with Tony’s condiment of a wife just got moved to brunch,” she says, rubbing her temple. “I have to head out in about twenty minutes. Do you mind staying here while I get ready?”

“Yeah, sure. I was thinking of heading out anyway.”

“You don’t have to,” Agatha says quickly, almost too quickly, which catches Rio off guard too. “I mean, if you’re not in a rush, I don’t see why you shouldn’t stay. It’s just a brief brunch. I’ll be out for a couple of hours and back before noon. After that, I’m entirely free.”

Rio stares and listens, trying to wrap her head around what Agatha’s actually offering.

“If you feel like freshening up or anything, the shower’s just upstairs, and there should be something in my closet you can wear. Whatever you’re comfortable in. And if you’ve got work to do today, my office is just there. You’re welcome to use the computer and any amenities you find useful.” She seems to catch herself then, noticing the way Rio’s just looking at her. “That is, if that arrangement works for you.”

Rio tilts her head, still trying to process. “Are you saying…I can stay the whole day?”

Agatha looks over, then immediately turns her attention to her now-empty mug.

“It’s actually more like, if you wanted to stay the weekend,” she continues, evidently unaccustomed to making such requests. “But only if you want to, of course. If you’ve got other plans or something lined up, I won’t hold you back. I just thought it’d be nice to come home later and see you still here.”

Rio is a little dumbfounded and completely speechless that Agatha actually wants her to stick around longer, but somehow, she finds her words.

“Yeah, sure. I mean, if you’re okay with it.”

“More than okay.” Agatha’s eyes soften with something close to a smile, and Rio feels her knees go a little weak. Ridiculous, really, considering she’s still sitting down. How she ended up here, wrapped in this unexpected kind of tenderness from Agatha Harkness of all people, she has no idea. “So you’ll stay?”

Rio can’t help the goofy, tooth-gap grin that spreads across her face. 

“Yeah. I’ll stay.”

And that’s how Rio finds herself spending the entire weekend at Agatha’s place.

They eat dinner barefoot in the kitchen, sharing bites straight from the same plate, stealing sips from the same glass of wine, then fuck, right up against the counter, with Rio’s back pressed against the cold Calacatta marble and Agatha’s hands tugging her shirt off like she’s starving.

At some point, they also end up in the shower, laughing when Agatha gets shampoo in Rio’s eye, but that doesn’t stop the latter from sliding her hand between the older woman’s thighs. They slip, grab, press into each other, too turned on to care about anything else.

They watch a mix of fashion shows and climate documentaries on Agatha’s insanely big TV, the two of them sprawled on the bed, legs tangled in the sheets.

But somewhere between runway models in Paris and melting ice caps in the Arctic, Agatha decides to dip her head down, her mouth warm and unrelenting against Rio’s throbbing cunt. 

Fortunately for Rio’s thriving career, she actually manages to get a bit of work done on Agatha’s ridiculously fancy desktop, before getting completely distracted and, yes, ending up having sex in Agatha’s home office too.

And somewhere on Monday, after all the orgasms, shared toothpaste, borrowed shirts, bottles of wine, and the stack of dishes left behind from the meals they’ve cooked and eaten together, and then stood side by side washing, Rio starts to realize they never once talked about what any of it is supposed to mean.

After a long week of chasing leads, digging through numbers, and piecing together quotes, Rio finally wraps up her draft and sends it in.

The article, her first non-fashion feature since the Nocturne exclusive, is set to go live on The Journal next week, so she’s meeting Hela at Fresco, per Hela’s insistence, to go over a few final notes and discuss placement.

As she sits in the backseat of her rideshare, Rio pulls out her phone and opens her messages. 

Somewhere between writing and rewriting, she somehow keeps finding herself texting Agatha, who occasionally responds when she isn’t occupied in meetings or yelling at some unfortunate intern (if Shuri’s updates are to be believed).

Shuri, ever the relentless oversharer, continues to text Rio on a daily basis, even though Rio no longer works at Nocturne, something Rio silently enjoys more than she admits.

Rio: How’s your day going?

She doesn’t expect a reply right away, but to her surprise, the message gets read almost instantly.

Agatha: Still dealing with the usual mediocrity and incompetence. Some intern ‘misplaced’ one of the pull quotes and now, instead of final proofs, I’m getting myself a headache.

Before Rio can even tap out a reply, another message lands.

Agatha: How’s your meeting with Helena? Have you made it clear to her that there would be no kissing you involved this time?

Rio shakes her head, grinning despite herself.

Rio: First of all, her name is Hela. And I’m still in the cab on the way there. Second, no one’s kissing me anytime soon, unless it’s someone with steely blue eyes, most likely frowning at her phone right now, with her eyebrows doing that judgy little arch.

A few seconds pass.

Agatha: You might know a lot of people with steely blue eyes and judgmental eyebrows.

Rio laughs under her breath, biting her lip when the driver glances at her in the mirror. 

She types back quickly.

Rio: I actually only know one.

And then, maybe just a little bolder than she intends, she sends another.

Rio: Will I be seeing you tonight? It’s been a while since…well, the weekend.

She hesitates after hitting send, staring at her screen while chewing the inside of her cheek. Then, to her relief, the typing bubbles appear, followed by Agatha’s reply.

Agatha: Well, my weekend has been miraculously cleared, so I wouldn’t mind if you stayed again. 

Rio’s smile blooms before she can stop it. Jesus, what is this woman doing to her?

Then another message comes in, one that makes her smile stretch even wider.

Agatha: Also, I seem to remember you mentioning those cookies you used to bake specifically for wooing. My kitchen’s yours, should you feel inspired to test their powers on someone more difficult to impress.

Rio: Is that a challenge? 

Agatha: Only if you’re brave enough to take it.

Rio chuckles, shaking her head before tucking her phone back into her pocket, still grinning as the car rolls to a stop in front of Fresco.

Inside, she spots an open table tucked in the corner and starts to reach for her phone to text Hela, only to stop when a familiar pair at a nearby table catches her eye.

“What the hell?” Rio mutters to herself, brows furrowing as her confused hazel eyes land on the woman with dark brown hair marked by unmistakable blonde streaks, currently deep in conversation with none other than Tony Stark.

A pit opens in her stomach, and she swears again under her breath.

Because why the actual fuck is Tony Stark having a friendly little sit-down with Valentina Allegra De Fontaine, the editor-in-chief of Nocturne’s oldest and most notoriously competitive rival?

A peculiar tightness coils in Rio’s chest. Not panic, exactly. 

But something that feels like a warning flaring just beneath her ribs. 

And her first thought, immediate and instinctive, is of Agatha.

Chapter 5

Chapter Summary

Funny thing is, this all started because Rio pretended to be sick and lied to Agatha (her former boss) just to skip work and go to fucking Pride.

Chapter Notes

even after the poll, i still debated cutting this into separate chapters again, but i couldn’t really decide, so here we are. all 28k and the whole fucking ride. might also be all over the place lmao. just remember to take little breaks in between, i guess. kicking my feet nervously as i post this. hoping the words reach you like light passing through a prism, splitting into a rainbow across the rain.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

Rio feels like she’s confined in a cage, stuck in her seat while the whole world keeps moving around her. 

It’s been more than fifteen minutes since Valentina De Fontaine and Tony Stark walked out of Fresco, leaving her restless in their wake. Hela had shown up not long after, sliding into the seat across from her. 

Rio barely notices the waiter sliding a plate between them as her eyes stay fixed on Hela and her mind drifts somewhere else entirely, the other woman’s moving lips and voice blurring into a low hum against her own tangled thoughts.

Something about what the editor thought of Rio’s article and what happens next, but not a single word makes it past the fog in her head.

“So, Stewart says yours is one of the strongest they’ve had all quarter. But don’t let it go to your head, because now you’re stuck competing with yourself.”

Hela takes a sip of her Aperol spritz, glances at Rio, then keeps going.

“They’ll wire half the payment this week, the rest after publication. But I’ll email you more details tonight so—” She cuts herself off, squinting at Rio. “All right, what is this? I feel like I’m talking to a wall here. Are you even listening to a word I’m saying?”

Rio finally blinks, like she’s just surfaced from underwater. 

“Uh, yeah, of course. I got it.”

Hela leans back, unimpressed.

“Really? Then tell me what I just said.” 

Rio stalls, fiddling with her fork just to keep her hands busy, but no words come. 

“Uh-huh. Just as I thought.” Hela sighs, setting her glass down with a clink. “So, what’s going on? And please don’t say nothing,” she adds, holding up a hand before Rio can even speak. “Whatever it is, it’s written all over your face.”

“It’s probably nothing,” Rio argues, “and maybe I’m just overthinking.”

“Overthinking what?” Hela asks. “If this is about your article, I literally just told you it’s great work.”

“No, it’s not the article.” 

“Then what is it?” 

Rio exhales slowly, eyes fixed on her plate as she absently taps her fork against the rim. 

“It’s just…I don’t know what to make of it. I saw Stark with Oxe’s editor right before you showed up, and they were having—” she hesitates, searching for the words, “I don’t know, a really friendly chat. Which makes no sense, right? Why would Stark be even talking to the editor-in-chief of a rival magazine?” 

She eventually looks up, catching the barely-there reaction that crosses Hela’s face. The balance between them suddenly tilts.

“You know something,” she concludes. “What are you not telling me, Hela?”

The other woman sidesteps Rio’s accusing eyes and takes another sip of her drink. 

“I only picked up on it recently, though it looks like it’s been going around for a while,” Hela admits. “But it’s just a bunch of rubbish, baseless rumours, and I think you shouldn’t really be worrying about it, not with you being—”

“What baseless rumors?” Rio interrupts, leaning forward slightly.

She can tell Hela already knows she’s not the type to let something simply drop once it’s on the table, but Hela still says, “Again, I really don’t think you need to concern yourself with this.”

“Hela,” Rio presses, her focus locked on the woman’s blue eyes, too much like another pair she’d rather be staring into right now, the very ones at the root of the dread slowly knotting her chest. “Tell me. What baseless rumors?”

Hela sighs. “Fine. If you really must know,” she says, lifting her glass for another sip before setting it down a little too firmly. “Word’s been going around that Tony Stark might be trying to bring Valentina into his company, most likely to take over Nocturne by the end of the month.”

Rio stares at her, as if she misheard. 

“Take over Nocturne?” The fork slips from her hand, clattering against the plate. Her stomach twists as the realization clicks into place. “You mean…no. No, you can’t be serious. That’s—Stark wouldn’t do that to Agatha. She’s been the backbone of that magazine for years. She practically built it. Why the hell would he even consider replacing her?”

“I don’t mean to sound harsh, but perhaps it’s because De Fontaine is a bit younger than Harkness—” 

“That’s bullshit.” 

“—and brings a fresher perspective,” Hela points out, rather regretfully. “Nocturne is one of the most expensive magazines in the business, and a lot of people have noted that Val can do the same work for much less. Tony Stark is a numbers guy, Rio. He’s a businessman through and through, and he always thinks about the ledger rather than loyalty. On top of that, I suspect Agatha’s recent stunt has probably pushed him even closer to making this decision.”

“Recent stunt?” Rio’s brows knit together.

“Your world-exclusive, darling,” Hela says, her eyes studying Rio’s reaction with intent. “It’s still the talk of the town. Partly for its sheer quality, but also for how Agatha managed to pull it off at the very last minute, directly against Stark’s explicit orders. And well, let’s just say it ruffled more than a few feathers.”

Rio blinks, disbelief written all over her face. 

“What? That doesn’t even make any sense. That issue brought in almost ten times the revenue. How can he be upset? He’s the one always harping about numbers! Is he seriously that much of an idiot?”

Hela leans back, folding her arms.

“Yes, I agree. Most men are like that, both in this business and out of it. But he’s also an idiot with an exceptionally fragile ego.”

Rio feels a pit open in her stomach. “Agatha’s going to be devastated. Her whole life is about that magazine. It’s all she’s worked for. Stark can’t just screw her over like this.” She presses her face into her hands for a moment, then looks up again. “Does she even know?”

Hela regards Rio for a bit, then shrugs, a hint of worry in her eyes. 

“I don’t know, but I like to think she’s aware of what’s going on. After all, this is Agatha Harkness we’re talking about. Hardly anything ever slips past her.”

Hela has a point. But Rio’s stomach twists further anyway.

“What do I do? I can’t just—I have to do something, right? I mean…it was my exclusive that set all this off. I should at least be doing something about this. Right?”

The blonde shakes her head. 

“And what, exactly, could you do? If these rumours hold any truth, Rio, you’re still a greenhorn, a mere speck in the eyes of everyone else. You’re only just starting to carve out your own name here. You don’t need to play Romeo in this, do you understand? Agatha has been in this business far longer than you. I’m sure she can handle this on her own. You certainly don’t need to get involved.”

But what Hela said back at the restaurant doesn’t make things any easier for Rio as she steps out of the cab in front of Agatha’s house in Scarsdale, a duffel bag slung over her shoulder.

She and Agatha had decided it was safer to spend the weekend here rather than at Agatha’s Upper East Side townhouse, which would easily be crawling with photographers. 

Yes, even on a fucking weekend. The vultures don’t rest, as they say. 

And it doesn’t look right for Rio to be spotted there, since she’s neither Agatha’s assistant anymore nor a writer at the magazine.

Last weekend, she’d slipped out in the dead of night with a hoodie pulled low, and though it went unnoticed, she’d rather not tempt fate.

The last thing she wants is to cause Agatha any more trouble.

She hesitates, rocking awkwardly on her toes before finally pressing the doorbell.

A moment later, there’s a shuffle inside, and then Agatha opens the door, one brow already arched. 

“The doorbell? Really?”

“What, you wanted me to climb in through the window?” Rio manages a sheepish grin, praying she doesn’t look as rattled as she feels. “Because I totally would. Might even be more romantic.”

“And borderline illegal,” Agatha retorts dryly, rolling her eyes but stepping aside. “I’m still buried in a few calls, but I’ll be free after. You can go upstairs, take a shower, whatever you need. Just make yourself at home,” she adds in a distracted ramble as she ushers Rio inside.

Rio trails after her, chewing over the thought of what she had seen earlier.

Part of her desperately wants to spill it right there in the hallway, but she swallows it back. She decides it’s better to bring it up later, when they’re both sitting down.

She does as Agatha suggested. She heads upstairs for a hot shower, then pulls on a pair of worn sweatpants and an old band tee before heading back down with her laptop in hand.

The living room is empty. So is the kitchen when she peeks in. 

Agatha must still be in her office.

So Rio sinks onto the couch, only to jolt when a pair of big brown canine eyes peer at her from behind.

“Jesus, buddy, you scared me.” Rio presses a hand to her chest, but the mastiff just trots right up and starts sniffing at her. Rio lets her, crouching down to scratch behind her ears when the dog circles around in front of her. The mastiff’s tail thumps happily against the floor. 

“You must be Fanny,” Rio greets her with a grin. The dog snuffles at her once more before licking her hand, and Rio’s smile brightens. “Well, aren’t you the cutest thing.” 

She gives her another good scratch, and Fanny tips her head back, clearly asking for more. Rio settles onto the rug and starts rubbing her belly.

“So what are you doing here, huh? Aren’t you supposed to be with Marmee? Did she drop you off because you’re on babysitting duty? Or are you here to make sure your other human doesn’t forget to eat?”

The mastiff huffs through her nose and rolls over, leaving Rio no choice but to keep scratching. 

Rio laughs under her breath. “Bet you’re better company than half the people she works with.”

“She’s more effective than half my staff, I’ll give her that.”

Startled, Rio lifts her head and finds Agatha standing in the doorway: arms crossed, glasses askew and hair just slightly out of place. She looks tired in a way only Rio would notice.

Fanny immediately abandons Rio’s hand to trot over to her other human. Agatha bends down, running a hand over the dog’s back before straightening again.

“Marmee’s out tonight,” she explains, adjusting her glasses. “One of her old friends is in the hospital, so she insisted on staying over to look after her.” She gives the dog another absentminded pat before glancing at Rio. “So it’s us and Fancakes tonight. Hope that’s not a problem.”

Rio pushes herself up from the rug, dusting off her sweatpants. 

“Are you kidding?” She looks at the dog, tail wagging like a metronome. “Other than Marmee, she’s the nicest welcome committee I’ve ever had at your place.” Fanny lets out a single bark, as if in agreement, and Rio snorts.

The dog eventually loses interest, padding off to roam the house and leaving the two of them alone. 

Rio’s fingers twitch at her side, the urge to finally say what she saw earlier tugging at her again. But before she can get a word out, Agatha glances at the clock and breaks the silence first.

“I’m starving, and I’m sure you are too. I was craving steak, so I had some delivered. It’s probably gone cold by now, but we can warm it up in the oven. Would you mind giving me a hand?”

Rio blinks, a little thrown by the domestic ease of it all, but nods. 

“Yeah, sure.”

Agatha is already moving toward the kitchen, slipping her glasses off and setting them on the counter as she opens one of the paper bags. 

The scent of seasoned meat wafts out, faint but still rich enough to make Rio’s stomach rumble. Her last meal had been hours ago, and she’d barely even touched it.

“Plates are in the top cabinet to your left,” Agatha says without looking up, distracted as she checks the containers. “Grab a couple, will you?”

Rio does as she’s told, watching her former boss slide their dinner into the oven. She debates again whether she should tell her right away. 

Maybe they should eat first. Standing almost side by side in Agatha’s kitchen, the soft domesticity of the moment feels too fragile and gentle to shatter with something so serious. 

Rio can wait a little longer. Surely telling Agatha can wait. 

So, she decides to hold off, savoring this brief reprieve before reality comes calling again. 

It’s only when Agatha is on her second pour of wine that she finally notices Rio’s restlessness, or perhaps she’s just grown tired of skirting around it. “All right, I can’t keep up this charade any longer. You’re here, but you don’t really seem present. Is everything okay?”

Rio opens her mouth, then closes it again, unsure how to start the conversation. Noticing her reluctance, Agatha sets her fork down and adds, “Is the steak not to your liking?”

“What? No, it’s perfect. I mean, the seasoning could be…a little different, maybe, but it’s perfect.” Rio rumbles. She’s always loved steak, a sucker for it, and she even cooks it well. She even wants to cook some for Agatha one day, and she could easily eat more of this, but tonight her appetite isn’t really in the right place.

“The wine, then?”

“No. The wine’s great too.”

Agatha narrows her eyes at her, clearly trying to figure out what Rio isn’t saying, then sighs in defeat. 

“Fine. So if it’s not the steak or the wine, then what is it? Do you have somewhere else you need to be? I could call Javier now to pick you up, have you go wherever you need.”

Rio sits up a little too quickly. 

“No, of course not! That’s not necessary. I really do want to be here.”

“Well, you don’t seem like it,” Agatha mutters to herself, though Rio still catches it. 

She pouts, frowning at Rio, and Rio can’t help but feel her chest soften at the sight, seeing the older woman look so adorably frustrated, like Rio is ruining their perfect little evening. 

Somehow, she really is.

Agatha sighs, letting herself calm. Well, mostly. That’s a recent development, Rio notes.

“If it’s not the steak, the wine, or the fact that you’re here, then what is it that’s been bothering you? Clearly, there’s something you’re not telling me, Rio.” 

Rio stares at her for a moment. Since when had Agatha been so good at noticing when something was troubling her? And, stupidly, Rio kind of liked this new little rhythm in their back-and-forth. 

But there’s a more pressing issue at hand, so she sighs and sets her utensils down as well.

“It’s about something I came across earlier, during my meeting with Hela. And it’s not exactly the kind of thing you’d be happy to hear,” Rio begins. Agatha looks a bit more impatient, but she doesn’t interrupt. “I saw Tony in a meeting with Val, Oxe’s editor, or at least it looked like some kind of a meeting. I’m not entirely sure, but it definitely gave me that impression.”

Rio’s suspicions, along with Hela’s earlier words about the rumors, seem to be true, judging by the sudden trace of something wary on Agatha’s face, only before she quickly masks it with a more neutral expression and returns to cutting her steak. 

“And that’s been bothering you because?” 

Rio should have expected it. Of course, Agatha would deflect. 

She shifts in her seat, fingertips grazing the edge of the counter. 

“I think you already know why.”

And once again, Rio knows she’s right, because she can almost see the familiar parabolic wall Agatha is putting up, piece by piece, between them. 

The latter lets the wine roll over her tongue before lowering the glass carefully. She cuts another piece of steak, chews slowly, and only then does she glance up at Rio. 

“Then trust me when I say it’s not something that concerns you,” she says at last. “Whatever you’ve convinced yourself is happening, it’s not yours to get tangled up in. Are we clear on that?”

Those words land more violently than Rio expects, hitting bone. 

She fires back before she can stop herself. “What do you mean it doesn’t concern me? You’re in this position because of me.” Her voice comes out guilty and frustrated, mirroring how she’s felt all day. “No, Agatha, please don’t deny it,” she adds the moment the other woman’s lips part. “Tony is replacing you because of that stupid exclusive—”

“No one is replacing me. And that wasn’t some stupid exclusive,” Agatha cuts her off. “Do you really want to devalue what Lilia trusted us with?”

“No. That’s not what I meant.” Rio shakes her head hard. “I’m not talking about Lilia here. I’m talking about me. If we hadn’t run the piece I wrote, Tony wouldn’t even be thinking about doing this to you.”

Agatha exhales through her nose, setting her utensils down again like a punctuation mark. 

“If we hadn’t published it, the numbers would have stayed disappointing. Tony would’ve still found a reason to screw me over.” She finally lifts her eyes to Rio. “Believe me, he was already making his choice long before your words ever hit print.” 

That’s all the confirmation Rio needs: the rumors are true, and Agatha has known it for a while. 

And somehow, even though Agatha makes it sound otherwise, Rio can’t shake the feeling that her fingerprints are still all over it too. 

And she couldn’t deny the disappointment gnawing at her, because it feels like she and Agatha had been building some kind of trust.

Agatha had already shared so many truths with her, and yet this, something that clearly involved her, Agatha had chosen to keep her in the dark.

“Why didn’t you tell me?” Rio asks more calmly, though even she herself can hear the hurt in her voice.

It takes Agatha a few seconds before she replies. 

“Because you didn’t need to know,” she reiterates, almost protectively. “I ran that article because I knew it was what the magazine needed. It was entirely my call. I didn’t do it just for you.” Rio doesn’t have a word to throw back, so Agatha continues, “Try not to let this bother you, do you understand? I’m more than capable of dealing with this on my own.”

The one thing Rio can’t stand about herself is the feeling of helplessness, especially when she knows she could at least do something about it.

She remembers being a kid, sitting frozen in class while a classmate was unfairly scolded for talking, even though Rio knew it was someone else who had whispered first. 

Or when the class hamster got sick and everyone just accepted it, but Rio stayed up late flipping through her dad’s old encyclopedia, trying to figure out how to help the poor thing, furious that no one else cared enough to even try. 

Or the time her mom came home late, eyes tired and shoulders sagging, and Rio sat at the kitchen table with her homework, too young to lighten the load, but old enough to feel its weight.

Even then, she had always hated the idea that circumstances beyond her control could decide outcomes for her. 

People had often called her stubborn, a complaint wrapped in exasperation, as if her refusal to bend was a flaw. 

But like her dad, she believed stubbornness wasn’t weakness. It’s simply courage in disguise. As he once said, “Stubborn people are often the ones who carve their own roads when the world insists on walls.” She had always liked to think of herself as one of them.

She turns her head toward Agatha, naked under the sheets and curled up peacefully on her side of the bed. Rio had dreamed of this: waking up to see Agatha like this, to simply watch her sleep. 

Even the strongest souls have a way of appearing fragile and serene when they surrender to rest, and Agatha is no exception. She looks so vulnerable and delicate, so entirely unaware of Rio’s eyes on her, that it makes Rio’s chest ache.

There’s no way Rio is going to let this woman face something alone when she’s right here to help. 

She stands carefully, making sure the sudden shift of the mattress doesn’t wake Agatha.

Grabbing the boxers tossed on the floor and a loose white shirt from her overnight bag, she slips into them quietly.

Laptop in hand, she pads downstairs and finds Fanny already waiting at the bottom, her tail wagging. The dog must have sensed a human was awake, but thankfully, she doesn’t bark.

“Hey, buddy. Sorry to wake you,” Rio murmurs, scratching behind Fanny’s ears before moving into the living room and sinking onto the couch. Fanny seems to understand, curling up at her feet and soon drifting back to sleep.

Rio opens her laptop and types in a name, along with a few keywords she hopes will lead her to a way to help Agatha. She shakes her head while doing so. 

If her dad could see her right now, he’d just roll his eyes. Not at what she was doing, but at the fact that she was doing it at all, stubborn as ever, just like him, right against Agatha’s insistence. 

Some things, it seemed, ran deep in the family.

And Rio is doing this for the woman she…well, she hasn’t really put a name to it yet, but that doesn’t matter right now. 

What matters is whether there’s dirt to find on this so-called billionaire, philanthropist, playboy Tony Stark. Her gut screams that there’s something there, and Rio is determined to dig it up.

Hours had passed, and Rio hadn’t even realized how long she’d been scrolling, reading, and bookmarking articles before she dozed off on the couch.

It’s the sunlight streaming through Agatha’s big windows and Fanny’s tongue on her arm that drags her out of sleep. 

Panic shoots through her immediately, but thank goodness her laptop had auto-locked, so there’s no way anyone could have seen her open tabs.

“You certainly have a strong attachment to that couch,” Agatha quips from the threshold, arms crossed over her emerald satin robe. Rio quickly notices she doesn’t look thrilled to have woken up alone without Rio by her side. “What are you doing down here?”

Scratching the back of her neck, she tries to sound casual and convincing. “Sorry, I didn’t want to wake you. I couldn’t sleep, had a bit of work to catch up on, and thought Fanny might like the company.”

“So you’d rather have Fanny’s company than mine?”

Rio shakes her head with a sheepish grin.

“Am I imagining things, or is Agatha Harkness suddenly jealous of a dog?”

The older woman rolls her eyes. 

“Oh, definitely the first one. I never get jealous.” She leans down slightly, letting her hand glide over Fanny’s fur, and the dog leans into her touch with a soft whine. “But enjoy Fanny’s company if you must. Truthfully, I’d also pick hers over yours anyway.”

“Why don’t you just get over here?” Rio pats her lap, and Agatha instantly raises an eyebrow. Rio laughs, knowing full well Agatha never willingly takes orders from anyone. Then, for the first time, she tries giving her puppy-dog eyes, something she’s sure Agatha can’t resist. “Please?”

Agatha sighs, though there’s no real protest in it, and slowly walks over. 

Rio reaches up and guides her down, so she ends up straddling her lap. 

Their eyes meet, pale ocean-blue against warm hazel, and suddenly their worlds feel a little closer as Rio says, “Good morning.”

Agatha smirks. “Shouldn’t a proper greeting come before any conversation?” But she still mirrors Rio’s knowing stare and snakes her hands around her neck. “Morning.”

Maybe it’s Rio trying to make up for the microscopical distance that lingered after their conversation in the kitchen last night, even through what came after in bed. 

Or maybe it’s just seeing Agatha so domestic and unguarded that it swallows her whole. Her hands settle on Agatha’s waist as she leans in for a kiss, and Agatha meets her without hesitation.

When had they decided to be this sappy? When had Agatha let Rio get this close, let her touch her like gravity pulling a comet, let her kiss her like two stars caught in orbit, circling each other endlessly and burning bright? 

But before Rio can get lost in the thought, Fanny barks at the door, and Marmee’s cheerful voice rings out from the hallway.

With this, Agatha quickly scrambles upright out of Rio’s lap and fusses with her robe, and Rio fights the urge to laugh at how she looks exactly like a kid caught misbehaving.

“Well, hello there, sweetpea! Have you been a good girl?” They hear Fanny’s barking stop abruptly, and Rio guesses Marmee is giving her a happy scratch behind the ears. Not a second later, Marmee shuffles into view, smiling at them both. “Would you look at that, you two are up early.”

“Marmee,” Agatha greets. “I thought you said you’d be back before noon.” Her cheeks are still a little pink from…well, almost getting caught with Rio in a near-makeout.

And really, who would want their second mom walking in on that? And yes, Rio knows exactly how Agatha feels about Marmee, even if she’d never say it out loud. It’s the same way Rio feels about Lorna.

“Oh, I couldn’t possibly leave Fanny with you two and ruin both your weekends any more than I already have,” Marmee declares, making her way toward the kitchen with a playful sway. “Hi, Rio, dear.”

With the way Marmee greets her, Rio can’t help but assume she has no problem with her being here with Agatha, as if she’s already on board with whatever it is they’re starting to be. 

Still, all Rio manages is to awkwardly raise a hand in greeting.

Then she notices her carrying a few paper bags, the content of which she still can’t figure out. Rio hurries to catch up, offering to help Marmee with some of the load, while Agatha trails behind them.

“Fanny’s not as much of a handful as you think she is,” Agatha argues. The dog wags her tail like she knows she’s being talked about, trotting at their heels as they step into the kitchen. “And we really love having her here. Right, Rio?”

Rio’s stomach does a little unexpected flip at the “we,” mostly because of how easily Agatha says it. 

The casual intimacy in her voice. 

As if they’ve already become a unit overnight. As if that’s just what they are now. 

Rio nods, though her thoughts scatter like startled birds. 

Are they really already a unit? Have they even talked about being a unit? Or is Rio supposed to just assume it too?

“Oh, I know you do,” Marmee says, unloading the bags onto the counter. She raises an eyebrow at them. “But you couldn’t possibly have Fanny running around here while the two of you bake. Trust me, this girl is dangerous near an oven.” She snorts and sets down the eggs, flour, sugar, and everything else. Agatha must’ve asked her for a favor to gather it all. “I assume this will be enough?” Marmee turns to Rio, who’s only just now piecing it all together.

“Uh, yeah, I think that’s more than enough. Thank you, Marmee,” Rio replies softly, then glances at Agatha and leans closer to whisper, “We’re really baking?”

Agatha crosses her arms. “Yes. Unless, of course, you’re thinking of backing out of my challenge.”

Rio grins, leaning in just a little more, recalling their text exchange from yesterday. 

“Not a chance. I’m dead set on impressing you with pastries today, Miss Harkness.”

They hold each other’s eyes for a beat, and Rio swears her heart stumbles into a faster rhythm. 

She wonders if Agatha feels the same. 

Then Marmee claps her hands together, snapping them both out of it. 

Wait, did they really just lean in for a kiss? Right here? In front of someone? Rio can’t even tell. All she knows is she’s pulled to Agatha so strongly she doesn’t even have the time to figure out how much.

“Well now, it looks like you’ve got everything you need,” Marmee says kindly. “I even tucked a few extra things in the cupboard the other day, just in case. You never know when a bit of extra sugar might come in handy.” She chuckles to herself. “Now, dears, Fanny and I will go on our morning walk. You two enjoy the rest of your weekend, and do try not to burn the house down while you’re at it.”

She pats her knees, and Fanny springs up, tail wagging as she trots after her.

Rio lifts a hand in farewell, Agatha murmurs a polite thanks, and Marmee’s warm, crackling laughter trails down the hall as she finally shuffles out the door.

Rio glances at Agatha, then at the neatly lined-up ingredients on the counter. 

“So…we’re actually doing this? Baking?”

“More like you’ll do the baking, I’ll do the supervising,” Agatha says, raising an eyebrow.

“Oh no, you don’t.” Rio reaches out, letting her fingers brush Agatha’s. “You’re not getting out of this that easily. Today, you’re my charming assistant. We’re doing this together.”

Agatha folds her arms, giving Rio a cool, mock glare. “Very well. But you should know, much like Fanny, I’m a walking hazard near an oven. In fact, anything electrical in this kitchen would be wise to fear me.”

Rio bursts out laughing, already picturing the disaster coming. 

And sure enough, Agatha hadn’t been exaggerating because when they start baking more than an hour later, the batter flies the second she takes the hand mixer from Rio, streaking across the wall and splattering the counter, while a few chunks even land on her own cheek. 

Rio laughs even harder as she grabs a towel to wipe off said chunks from Agatha’s face.

By the time the clock nudges past one, the kitchen looks like it’s been through a type of war. 

Flour dusts the counters, smudges the floor, and a thin trail of sugar sparkles wherever the sunlight hits. Agatha, to Rio’s surprise, hasn’t abandoned the ship.

Instead, she’s taken her role as critic-in-chief and assistant seriously, perched in one of Rio’s oversized shirts with an apron tied over it. 

She had insisted her own clothes were too precious for the battlefield of baking.

Though Rio doesn’t let her handle any more moving tools, Agatha keeps busy passing ingredients and rinsing out bowls and measuring cups.

Every so often, Rio slips in close, hands finding her waist, lips brushing her temple or cheek, stealing kisses whenever she can.

Soon enough, with boygenius blasting through the speakers at Rio’s insistence, Agatha’s counters aren’t just crowded with one and a half dozen of chocolate chip cookies, but also a pan of salted caramel brownies and a whole glossy chocolate ganache cake — the kind so rich it has Agatha making noises so sinful Rio swears she could float straight off the floor.

“If you weren’t so dead set on becoming a journalist, have you ever thought about opening a bakery?” Agatha asks, lifting a forkful of ganache cake with her usual mechanical elegance. She takes her time with the bite before turning to Rio. “Where did you even learn to do all this?”

Rio wipes her flour-dusted hands on her apron. 

“My mami and Lorna used to swap pastries all the time when Alice and I were kids. Sometimes they’d come over, and Lorna and my mom would bake for the neighbors while Alice and I hung around the kitchen, sneaking bites and pretending to help. Most of what I know comes from my mami, but the recipes? Most of these are Lorna’s.”

Agatha acknowledges her answer with a soft smile, but lets out another little groan around her bite. 

“I think I could easily finish all of this on my own. This is just so good.”

Rio tries not to smile so hard her face might crack. Something about Agatha not even trying to hide how much she loves Rio’s baking makes her heart flutter. 

“You should leave some for Marmee, though,” she quips.

“Oh, you’re right.” Agatha sets her fork down with a small huff of disappointment, and Rio can’t help snorting. Agatha swivels toward her, narrowing her eyes. “What?” she asks.

Rio tilts her head, tongue poking at her cheek. All this sweetness will probably give her a sugar rush. 

“You’ve got a little something…” She doesn’t bother finishing the sentence and just wipes her thumb across the corner of Agatha’s mouth, smearing a streak of chocolate. She licks it off her finger, and Agatha’s cheeks flush bright red before she hides it behind a smirk. “There. All gone.” 

“Well, you’ve got something too,” she echoes, and Rio’s brows furrow.

“I do?”

“Uh-huh,” Agatha replies, hopping off the stool and leaning in before Rio has a chance to think. Their lips meet in a deep, teasing kiss, tongues brushing, and Rio swears she can taste the chocolate on Agatha’s. Oh, she really did a good job with that cake. Pulling back, Agatha taps her cheek, the smug grin on her face ebbing. “There. All gone.”

Rio’s face heats up like a tomato popped in a microwave. She can never win against Agatha in this little game, no matter how hard she tries. “I-It does taste good,” she stammers, “—the cake, I mean.” 

Agatha chuckles, sits back up on the stool with her wine, and nibbles a cookie this time, watching Rio with a soft, satisfied smile. Then Rio attempts to recover her cool by saying, “So, does impressing you with my baking skills earn me any points?”

“Who says you’ve got me impressed?” Agatha teases.

Rio just shakes her head. “You’ve been literally moaning at every bite. That says a lot, actually.”

Agatha rolls her eyes but doesn’t argue. “We should really take some of these to Marmee,” she parries, opening a drawer to grab some containers. 

But as soon as her fingers close around one, her phone rings  and vibrates on the counter. 

Before Rio can even see the caller ID, Agatha lets out a disappointed sigh and picks up the phone, giving the woman across from her an apologetic look.

“Afraid I have to take this. Mind if I leave you here for a minute?”

“It’s fine. Go ahead. I got this. I’ll get these goodies packed up.”

Agatha regards her briefly before nodding. “It’ll be just a quick call. I’ll be right back,” she says, brushing off her hands and sneaking one last bite of cookie. She hurries toward the entryway, and Rio begins arranging the pastries into the containers.

She smiles, imagining how much Marmee would love a few of these treats. And since Agatha mentioned that Marmee bakes, maybe she could even teach Rio some of the pastries she used to make for Agatha. 

Rio shakes her head as she keeps at her task. 

College Rio would have laughed at her. She once swore she’d stop baking after a fling called it too sappy and not really a useful skill, and for a while, she believed it. 

But now, if she’s being honest, Rio could spend the whole weekend in this kitchen, as long as it means having Agatha close, flirting and laughing freely, without caring about anyone else. Just the two of them. 

Ten minutes later, Agatha returns to the kitchen without her phone. A small detail Rio notices right away, forcing herself to stop grinning like an idiot because it’s obvious that after taking that call, Agatha doesn’t plan on letting anyone disturb them for the rest of the day.

“Shall we?” she says, and Rio follows, carrying their baked goodies across the street to Marmee’s house.

As soon as Rio steps inside, the house wraps around her like a warm hug. 

Marmee's home feels lived-in, welcoming, and completely unlike the cold perfection of Agatha’s estate the first time she ever set foot there.

But somehow, on this second visit, Rio notices that Agatha’s place has grown warmer, softer, and more alive — and she finds herself wishing it could always stay that way.

After all, Agatha deserves that kind of warmth more than anyone else.
