The afternoon stretches lazily in a slow, honeyed haze as the three of them lounge in Marmee’s backyard, teacups warm in their hands. Marmee had insisted, claiming, “These pastries are far too good not to be enjoyed with a proper cup of tea, dears.”

Every so often, Rio breaks away to toss a ball for Fanny, laughing as the dog barrels after it and skids across the grass, tongue lolling and tail wagging like a flag in the breeze. Marmee had chuckled more than once at the sight, noting how quickly Fanny had decided Rio was her new favorite person.

Though Fanny had always been a friendly dog, she usually needed a little patience, a few treats, and some gentle coaxing before she truly warmed up to anyone. But Rio had managed it effortlessly, at which Agatha commented offhand, “Rio has that effect on people. She’s just disarming without even trying.”

Thankfully, Fanny bounces over and licks Rio’s face just as Agatha says it, sparing her from having to respond at all, and, more importantly, keeping Agatha from noticing the warmth creeping up her cheeks.

After a few hours of being spoiled in the backyard, Marmee had insisted they both stay for dinner. It had been a while since she’d shared a table with anyone besides Agatha, and Rio was far too charmed to even think of declining.

She had slipped into the kitchen, sleeves rolled up and insisting on helping, while Agatha had been planted firmly on the living room couch, a book in hand to keep her occupied after Marmee and Rio had unanimously agreed she couldn’t be trusted anywhere near the stove.

“As I recall, I was a perfectly decent baking assistant earlier, and this is the thanks I get? Come on, buddy, no one here seems to know how to show genuine gratitude,” Agatha had said with mock outrage, patting her thigh for Fanny to follow as the two of them swept dramatically out of the kitchen. Rio could only laugh while she chopped vegetables for Marmee’s beloved beef stroganoff.

After more than an hour of dinner chatter, with Marmee doing almost all the talking and recounting how little Agatha made her husband Henry wear a tutu to help her practice a dance recital, or how she once tried to bake cookies with her only to end up covered in flour from head to toe, the three of them naturally move into the living room. 

Marmee uncorks a bottle of white wine while Rio crouches by the shelves, carefully flipping through a stack of vinyls.

Every so often, Rio sneaks a glance at Agatha, curled up on the couch with yet another book. Fanny’s head rests on her lap, and she absentmindedly strokes the dog’s fur, completely absorbed in her reading.

It’s only when she finally takes in the full collection of vinyls that she gapes, her eyes briefly moving away from Agatha.

“This is quite the stash you’ve got here, Marmee,” holding one of the sleeves up to the light. “I think you and Alice would really get along. I don’t know much about music myself, but she’s got an impressive collection too, though she leans more toward eighties rock than anything else.”

Marmee’s eyes warm as they fall on the stack. “They’re not mine, actually. These are all Henry’s. They were his pride and joy. He treated them better than the furniture, if I’m honest.” She chuckles, her gaze lingering awhile on the stack, tracing the edges of the sleeves as if she can feel him there, then looks back at Rio with a small smile. “Go on. Play one.”

Rio glances at Agatha, who looks up briefly from her book, then back at Marmee. 

“Are you sure? I mean, I don’t think I—”

Marmee shakes her head gently. “Dear, I hardly play them these days. My husband would’ve loved knowing they’re still being listened to, and not just sitting there gathering dust,” she says this as she finally settles back onto the other couch.

Rio regards Marmee one more time, then nods and turns back to the shelves. She runs her fingers slowly along the spines, pausing here and there, as if she can feel the weight of memory pressed into each one. 

Finally, she pulls out a record: something she thinks Marmee, maybe even Agatha, will like.

She slips the vinyl carefully from its sleeve, sets it on the turntable, and lowers the needle. After a soft crackle, Sam Cooke’s Nothing Can Change This Love fills the room, almost at the same time Marmee presses the wine glass close to her chest, a soft, tender smile touching her lips.

“Henry and I used to dance to this,” she says, the memory clear in her voice. “He would always pull me out here in the living room, from the kitchen or the garden, spinning me around until our knees gave out, both of us laughing. This was one of his favorites.”

Rio, always quick on her feet, steps forward, and offers her hand. “I’d hate to let a beautiful song go to waste.” Her grin spreads, that signature tooth gap catching the light as she looks at Marmee, and she dips into a playful half-bow. “May I have the honor of stealing the loveliest lady here for a dance?”

“Oh, aren’t you a gentleman,” the old woman giggles, setting her glass aside as she lets Rio lead her to the middle of the living room. Rio slides her other hand around Marmee’s waist, and they begin to sway, slow and easy, to the music playing on the turntable.

From the couch, Agatha watches them wordlessly, her book forgotten now, lips curling into a sweet, affectionate smile. And Rio can’t tear her eyes away, tracing the line of her jaw, the gentle slope of her nose, the loose fall of her hair, and the faint smattering of freckles across her cheeks.

Her eyes, however, are what keep her rooted. Blue like winter yielding to spring, frozen one minute, alive with warmth the next. Impossible to look at without losing herself.

Rio wonders, half in hope and half in longing, if Agatha is feeling the same pull, the same silent aching in her chest, as the song wraps around them like honeyed light, thick and languid, while everything beyond their little space slowly recedes into obscurity.

Marmee chuckles lightly midway through the song, jolting Rio out of her reverie. 

“Oh, I think that’s enough for me. I’m old, and my knees aren’t what they used to be. I think I’ll sit down.” She eases herself back onto the couch, still smiling as she catches her breath. Then she gestures between the two women. “Why don’t you two finish it for me?”

Agatha’s brows shoot up. “Marmee…you know I don’t dance.”

“Oh, nonsense. You could at least try,” the latter argues, waving a hand.

“Yeah, Agatha, you could at least try,” Rio adds with a grin, her hand already hovering.

“No.” Agatha crosses her arms “I know exactly what you’re doing. And I’m not dancing.”

Rio can’t help but grin wider. Marmee joins in, pretending dismay. “Well, my dear Henry would be so heartbroken if this song didn’t get danced all the way through.”

Rio can’t help but chuckle, grateful that even though Marmee knows nothing of the bet between her and Agatha, she’s unwittingly helping her case.

Agatha lets out a long sigh but straightens her shoulders.

“Okay, fine. For you…and Henry.” 

She glances at Marmee, who claps joyfully, then looks at Rio. With a reluctant but amused shake of her head, Agatha accepts the hand Rio is offering, letting herself be led to the center of the room.

Eventually, Rio places her hand around Agatha’s waist, holding her gently but securely, while Agatha rests hers lightly on Rio’s shoulders.

They sway together to the song, the room slowly shrinking around them until it feels like everything exists only for the two of them.

At first, Agatha hesitates, her eyes darting away, unsure or perhaps a little bit scared, to meet Rio’s big, embracing amber eyes.

But when she finally looks up, their eyes lock, and a shiver runs through Rio as Agatha’s other hand slides from her shoulder to rest over her chest, directly above her beating heart.

And Rio wishes nothing more than that she could stop time, press her palm against the heartbeat of this moment, and never let it go. She wishes she could hold the sway of Agatha in her arms, the warmth of the room, Agatha’s stare, and bottle it all up: bright, endless, and infinite.

“This is cheating, by the way,” Agatha quips. Rio chuckles, utterly pleased that she also remembered their little deal and the consequences, conveniently, in Rio’s favor.

“What part of this is cheating?” Rio teases. “I think I convinced you, fair and square.”

“Technically, Marmee did all the convincing. Not you,” Agatha shoots back, but with an obvious smile tugging at her lips. Proof that she, too, is secretly pleased about this. 

“Well, if we’re sticking to technicalities,” Rio says, leaning a little closer, “our bet was really about me seeing you dance. And by the letter of that bet…this counts. So technically, I win.”

Agatha rolls her eyes, and Rio can’t help but laugh even louder. She feels like someone who somehow got the prettiest girl in school to say yes to prom, her heart racing, completely certain that nothing could ever feel this perfect again. 

“Now you owe me ten bucks and an ice cream date,” she adds. “Though if I’m being honest, the ten bucks can go. I’m good if it’s only the ice cream part, and that little place on the way here will do just fine.”

Agatha squints at her, mock stern, though the corners of her mouth are still smiling. “Alright,” she drags the word. “An ice cream date…or whatever you want to call it. Next weekend.”

Rio’s smile spreads effortlessly as she takes Agatha’s hand in hers.

She pulls her closer, letting their bodies move together with the music.

The sides of their faces press softly against each other, warm and tender, saying everything words cannot.

However, the smile drains from Rio’s face as soon as she thinks about this weekend ending and what awaits her.

Come Monday, she’ll be back to digging through articles and probably interviewing people about Tony Stark and the messes he’s been involved in. 

Something she almost forgets entirely, lost in all this domestic bliss.

Had Agatha been deliberately distracting her? Or was she merely distracting herself? 

Either way, Rio couldn’t bring herself to complain.

If this is the kind of distraction she’s being offered, she’ll take it gladly and relish every second.

On the last night of their weekend together, Rio had lost count of how many times Agatha moaned, gasped, and trembled under her touch, each second hanging on the edge as if it might never come again. 

And maybe, with what Rio was planning in the next few days, something Agatha might not like, it truly wouldn’t. 

So she spends the remaining hours lying awake, her eyes fixed on Agatha, who is half-asleep beside her.

She doesn’t mind that Agatha sometimes prefers curling up on her own side of the bed instead of snuggling close.

In fact, there’s something quietly liberating about being able to watch her like this without worrying about waking her.

Rio thinks she could never tire of this view: a dream made real.

But this time, Agatha seems to sense Rio staring, stirring slightly, her eyes still closed. 

“What are you thinking?” she murmurs in a groggy, half-lidded voice, shifting closer so Rio can trap her in her arms. Okay, on second thought, Rio likes this even better.

She smiles at the familiar question. “Thinking you should go back to sleep,” she answers, pressing a soft kiss to Agatha’s forehead.

The latter doesn’t seem to notice the churn of thoughts in Rio as she drifts deeper into slumber, letting out even, gentle snores that Rio can’t help but listen to.

She regards Agatha for a minute longer, her mind racing over the plan she’s about to set in motion. 

To many, Agatha often comes across as imposing and unyielding, even a little ruthless. Yet these very traits, which might push others away, only draw Rio in, making her admire Agatha all the more.

Because beneath it all, there is fire and passion, and an untamed heart that makes her who she is. 

The side Rio has seen since the very first day she started working for her. That power, that intensity…it’s the heart of Agatha Harkness, and the magazine is a huge part of that.

And nothing, not even something stronger than Rio’s own will, could stop her from doing whatever it takes to protect it.

Perhaps Agatha would understand. Perhaps she wouldn’t resent her. Perhaps she’d see it for what it truly is: a promise from Rio to stand by her. That she will no longer have to face her trials alone, because Rio will be by her side through it all.

And now, seeing Agatha so peacefully asleep, Rio can only hope.

Rio’s gut had never steered her wrong, even when it led her to places she wouldn’t touch with a ten-foot pole. After four grueling days of digging through financial records, interviews, and insider tips, her efforts finally pay off. 

She uncovers that Tony Stark has been systematically slashing the salaries of lower-level employees across all his businesses (including Nocturne) funneling the money into his extravagant yacht-and-private-island lifestyle, all while financing a string of high-profile extramarital affairs.

Poor Tony’s wife, Rio had thought to herself.

For a man who prides himself on being a devoted family man and a philanthropic genius, this revelation is devastating, harming the very image that forms the backbone of his carefully curated empire.

And Rio isn’t the least bit afraid to drag it into the light.

“I have a story to pitch,” she announces, practically storming into Hela’s office on Sixth Avenue. “And trust me, you’ll want to hear this one.” The sudden intrusion makes the blonde woman startle, nearly spilling her coffee across the polished mahogany desk.

Rio had spent the entire night holed up in her room, pounding out the article, so much so that even Alice had started to worry. She’d shrugged it off as “work stuff.” And technically, it was work stuff. Just the kind that exposes the man threatening to jeopardize Agatha’s life’s work.

“Has spending too much time with your girlfriend completely robbed you of your manners?” Hela jests, though her humor quickly fades as she watches Rio drop the files. Her eyes widen, snapping up to meet hers. “What is this—Rio, you can’t be serious. Didn’t I explicitly tell you to stay out of this?”

Rio stays standing, clears her throat, feeling a flutter of nerves in her chest, but she’s already made up her mind. “I actually almost didn’t bring this to you,” she admits, “because I knew exactly how you’d react. But I did it anyway, because I already think of you as a friend, Hela. So here’s the deal: you help me run this story, or I take it somewhere else. Though honestly, I’m really hoping it’s the first option.”

Hela slowly sets her coffee cup down, lets out a long exhale, and begins to skim the article Rio has written.

As her eyes light up ever so slightly and the corner of her mouth twitches, Rio is sure she thinks it’s a solid piece. Something any journalist would be proud to put their name on, and most of all, something that could rattle the business streets of New York. 

This is real journalism. Rio knows it.

Any half-decent publication wouldn’t dare let a piece like this slip through their fingers.

Hela lets out another long exhale as she sets the paper down. 

“I’ve got to admit, as a journalist, I respect the guts it takes to pull this off. I’ve only read a few words, but there’s no doubt, this is going to make waves. Hell, this could very well be the end of Stark. But as the friend you claim I am, my honest opinion is that you’re being reckless, and you might very well regret this.” She glares at Rio, then a trace of concern crosses her face. “Does Agatha even know?”

Rio reluctantly shakes her head. 

“She doesn’t. And I intend to keep it that way, at least until this piece is published.”

Hela looks at her for another beat, then nods gravely before lifting the pages again.

“I’m going to run this past the higher-ups,” she continues, shifting to business. “You need to understand that publishing something of this magnitude comes with a lot of conditions. They’ll require thorough fact-checking, airtight sourcing, and the authority to tweak phrasing to manage any legal risk. You have to be ready to stand by everything you’ve written, before and after publication. That includes taking whatever fallout comes your way, work or personal. Once this goes live, there’s no taking it back. Think you can handle that?”

If it means Stark gets ousted and Agatha keeps Nocturne, then Rio can handle it.

”Yes.”

Hela shoots her a wary look and sets the papers down again.

“I just hope you really know what you’re getting yourself into.” 

Rio knows she is doing the right thing, especially for the people being screwed over by Stark. What she isn’t sure about is whether it is the right thing between her and Agatha. 

But like Hela, she hopes. She hopes Agatha will understand.

It had taken less than four days for the Journal to splash her story across the front page. 

The lead photo had shown Tony Stark slipping out of the St. Regis New York late at night, while a set of blurred, censored shots had revealed high-profile wives and celebrities sneaking out the back. 

The headline had blared in bold: Luxury at Labor’s Expense: How Stark Funds His Affairs on Workers’ Wages. 

Rio’s name had stared back at her from the byline. But unlike the first time it had appeared in Nocturne, she had felt a strange juxtaposition of exhilaration and apprehension and didn’t know what to make of it.

As Hela had warned her, the story had blown up within seconds of hitting the internet.

Every major news site had shared her article, and people had already begun debating the fate of Stark’s business empire, and who might take over the companies that now needed leadership without a questionable reputation.

Some had speculated it would be Ross, given he held the second-largest share.

Rio’s phone had been buzzing nonstop once again. Messages from friends and former colleagues congratulating her on yet another career break, news outlets asking if she had Stark’s list of high-profile mistresses, and editors from big-name magazines offering assignments she’d never even imagined.

Yet through all the noise of the past week, one silence cut deeper than the rest.

Agatha still hadn’t said a word.

And all the hope Rio had held onto slowly dropped like autumn leaves with each day that passed without hearing from her.

Had Rio underestimated the weight of the situation and left Agatha deeply upset? Or had she grown so sure of her feelings that she assumed Agatha would understand? 

“Still nothing?” Alice asks, peeking in and leaning on the doorframe while Rio stays half-distracted by the countless emails and tabs open on her laptop.

Rio slumps deeper into her chair. She should’ve expected this, right? Agatha’s anger was inevitable after she’d gone behind her back. 

But even if Rio had seen it coming, would it have hurt any less? She tells herself Agatha just needs time, that eventually she’ll understand why Rio did it and that it isn’t something to be gravely worried about.

“You don’t actually think she’s that mad at you just because of the article, do you?” Alice presses. Rio stays silent. “Okay, say she is. But probably only because you kept it from her and still went ahead after she told you not to get involved. Still, that doesn’t change the fact you did it for her. I’m sure part of her knows that, and maybe even appreciates the guts it took.”

“Then she would’ve called back, wouldn’t she?” Rio hates how hopeless she sounds.

Alice flops onto the bed with a groan. “You and your woman are starting to give me gray hair.” She props herself on her elbows. Then her voice gentles. “But for what it’s worth, getting that article out was brave, Rio. I know Agatha was the start, but you fought for it, for the people being treated unfairly. She might be upset you didn’t tell her, but I bet she understands why you did it. That’s still a good thing, no matter what. And I’m proud of you, and I’m pretty sure your mom and dad would have been proud too.”

Rio looks up from her laptop and gives her a small, genuine smile. “Thanks, Al.” 

She hadn’t even realized how much she needed to hear that.

Alice gives her shoulder a nudge. “Now how about we celebrate? You sit tight while I go buy us some beers. No buts, you and I are having drinks tonight. You know you’ve earned it, at least. I mean, it’s not every day you write something that actually takes down a literal billionaire.”

Rio just rolls her eyes but lets Alice have her way. And yeah, she could definitely use a drink.

Alice is halfway out of the room when a knock at the front door beats her to it, and she and Rio exchange a confused look.

Who could be knocking this late? Surely it can’t be Billy. That kid never bothers to knock.

“I’ll get it,” her best friend offers, completely slipping out of Rio’s room.

Rio barely pays attention, until she hears the front door open.

Then Alice’s surprised voice carries down the hall:

“Agatha.” 

And just like that, Rio freezes, her whole body sinking as if plunged into the icy waters of the North Atlantic. Then comes the familiar voice she hasn’t heard in days, slipping in like a ghost:

“Hi…Alice. Is Rio here?”

But before Rio can think better of it, her feet are already carrying her into the hallway.

And there’s Agatha Harkness, standing by the door of their shoebox apartment, looking like she just walked out of a meeting: classic black blazer over a crisp blouse, tailored pants, and her signature Jimmy Choos.

“I, uh, guess I’d better leave you two. I forgot Billy needs help with his calculus homework,” Alice mumbles (Billy doesn’t even take calculus) before edging past the unexpected visitor and into the hall. “Nice seeing you again, by the way.” But not before giving her best friend a look that clearly says she expects every single detail of whatever is about to happen.

Rio just stares, uselessly mute, as Agatha lingers at the threshold. They both look uncertain, maybe even a little nervous, but nothing compares to how Rio feels, especially with Agatha’s tight-lipped expression. She pushes the worry down.

There’s nothing serious to be concerned about, she tells herself, as if saying it enough could stop her from combusting under the tangle of emotions inside her.

“Can I come in?” the latter asks, the unexpected coldness of her voice cutting through Rio’s thoughts.

“Yeah, of course,” Rio stammers, blinking as she walks toward the door. “Sorry, it’s just…the place is a bit of a mess.” She steps aside and shuts the door behind them, shaking her head at herself. There’s nothing to be seriously worried about, she reminds herself yet again.

They’re halfway to the living room when Rio suddenly realizes she hasn’t brushed her hair or changed out of her plaid pajamas and Charlie Brown shirt since that morning.

A whole week without seeing each other, and this is how Agatha gets to see her. Rio is about to die of mortification.

“Can I get you something to drink?” she asks, fumbling for some sense of normalcy as Agatha’s eyes scan the room. “Alice has some of her mom’s special green tea tucked away in the kitchen. I could make you some if you’d like—”

Agatha waves her off without looking. 

“No need. I’m not planning to stay long.”

“Oh,” Rio says, trying and failing to hide the disappointment in her voice, as well as the gnawing dread that, based on Agatha’s cutting coldness, this conversation isn’t going to go well.

And that gnawing dread wells up as Agatha slowly turns to her, and it’s nothing like the calm face she had shown Alice just minutes ago. Now alone with Rio, her expression is a storm barely held in and ready to break.

But then her attention drifts, her eyes sliding past Rio and into the open room, landing on the laptop and scattered papers on the desk.

“Am I catching you in the middle of work?”

She follows Agatha’s stare and feels her throat go dry. She hadn’t expected that the pale green walls, the crooked Polaroids, the jungle of potted plants on the windowsill, and the books stacked sideways on the shelves would be enough for Agatha to quickly realize she was looking into Rio’s room.

Did Agatha really know her that well? 

And for some reason, that fact felt almost more intimate than a touch. 

A touch she had embarrassingly been starving for since last week.

“No, just catching up on some emails,” Rio says, edging toward the kitchen. She can’t let herself freeze there, her knees might give out if she does. “Are you sure you don’t want anything to drink?”

Agatha’s demeanor changes again, from stormy to distant, and now she looks at Rio with a grimness heavier than when she arrived, as if she’s just snapped out of something herself. 

“No, I’m only here to—” She doesn’t finish the sentence, as if forcing herself to say it, but eventually lets herself settle on, “Javier is waiting for me downstairs.”

Rio stops mid-step and looks at her. 

“I’ve been trying to call you, but you weren’t—”

“I’ve been busy. Damage control.”

Rio feels her throat tighten. Of course, Agatha also had to deal with the fallout from Stark’s mess, one way or another. She wants to skirt around the truth, but she’s not sure it would make a difference, since she already knows why Agatha is here. 

“I’m sorry I didn’t tell you about—”

“You don’t have to apologize,” Agatha cuts in, as if she’s also holding herself together. “What you wrote was necessary, and brilliantly done. Exactly what anyone would expect from you.” She exhales and turns slightly, and Rio can feel the disappointment radiating off her almost immediately. “Though I would have really appreciated it if you’d at least given me a heads-up.”

“Agatha,” Rio starts to say, but the words catch in her throat and die before they leave her mouth.

Agatha doesn’t say another word until she’s standing in the middle of the room. Now there’s no mistaking it, she had been far more upset than Rio had allowed herself to believe. So much for hoping otherwise.

“Thanks to your article, Pepper Stark, well, Potts soon enough, will assume control of Stark Publishing,” she tells Rio, not beating around the bush any longer. “Most of his businesses, in fact, along with some estates and a few key investments. All part of what she’s getting from their spectacularly public divorce.”

She slowly lets herself sink onto the couch, legs crossed, eyes roving around the room as if she doesn’t even notice Rio staring.

“But contrary to whoever fed you some of their little stories, she’s known about her husband’s indiscretions for quite some time. And somehow, even with the way we see things so differently, she trusted me enough to let me know what was going on.” 

Rio doesn’t dare speak or even move to sit. 

That explains why Agatha had been seeing Pepper more often than usual.

“She had her own plans to expose him, but your article beat her to it,” she says, finally locking eyes with Rio. “Turns out she’s a lot more than just the picture-perfect housewife everyone assumes she is.”

She rises again and walks over to the shelf, fingers brushing over the frames until they settle on one of Rio’s college photos. Rio beams from the picture, a medal gleaming against her chest, hands gripping a framed award that proudly reads: Best Investigative Journalist.

“What you wrote was fearless and uncompromising. I get why you went for it, even after I told you not to get involved. You’re simply relentless when you go after something, and you don’t stop until you see it through. I suppose that’s just who you are. You’ve never been the type to shy away from the truth, and I’ve always admired that about you.” Agatha exhales, setting the frame down, and Rio catches the feeble crack in her voice. “But that’s also why we couldn’t see each other anymore.”

“What?” Rio’s heart immediately drops.

“Going behind my back despite your best intentions, was reckless,” Agatha tells her, calm but cutting. “Again, Rio. Every time it’s because of me. You’re reckless when it comes to me, and I won’t let it keep happening. Being associated with me could cost you more than you realize, and I won’t allow it.”

“And what’s so wrong with that?” Rio blinks, incredulous. “I’ve done other things for people before, what’s so different about doing them for you?”

Agatha lets out a sigh, as if Rio’s words are nothing more than fairy tales.

“Don’t you see? Once people figure out why you wrote that article, there’ll be speculations about you, assumptions about how you got where you are now. That I’ve been doing you favors, that I’ve been clearing the road. We both know that’s not true, but unfortunately, that’s the story most people will choose to believe. And I won’t let your brilliance, your hard-earned success, be overshadowed by it. I can’t let anyone think it’s anything less than yours because of me.”

The stillness after Agatha speaks suddenly feels too loud for both of them. And Rio can’t even look at her now, even if she wants to. The truth is there, burning and relentless in her chest, but saying it out loud feels like handing them both a loaded gun. 

She swallows, her throat raw. 

“I—I didn’t mean to…to make things worse. I just…”

Agatha’s eyes finally meet hers again, the storm behind them terrifyingly clear. This scenario feels eerily familiar, and Rio feels her heart drop lower than it ever has.

“I know,” she says, reaching out but stopping herself, her hands curling at her sides. “But I can’t let this keep going. We can’t. If we went on like this, we’d just continue becoming each other’s problem. And I won’t let your choices, no matter how well-intentioned, mess up everything you’ve worked for yourself because of me. I can’t. And I won’t. I’m really sorry, Rio.”

When Rio was a child, her parents always said that an apology for one’s transgressions could undoubtedly mend a wounded heart. But why does the sound of Agatha saying such words feel like it’s only tearing hers apart?

The apology barely leaves Agatha’s lips before she’s gone, the door slamming behind her and leaving Rio alone, frozen, rooted to the spot.

Only the faint rumble of a car engine outside the open living room window harshly drags her out of her haze.

Rio feels enclosed in a glass tank, the world outside distorted and distant, every sound both magnified and muffled at the same time. She presses her hands against the invisible walls, but they won’t budge.

Her thoughts float like tiny, panicked fish, darting in every direction, colliding with each other, unable to find a clear path.

The water feels both protective and suffocating, holding her in place as the world continues on outside, leaving her suspended, fragile, and utterly exposed.

Then, as if that world suddenly rearranges around her, one of the fish turns and speaks in a clear, recognizable, unmistakably human voice. It rushes through the water like sunlight breaking the surface, and everything stops for a brief while.

“Rio…” the fish says.

Rio blinks. 

“Rio…” it says again.

What the hell?

Now why does the fish sound like Hela?

“You know,” she adds, the human Hela finally cutting through Rio’s near-impenetrable haze, the scene painfully familiar. How on earth did Rio even get here? “We should really stop meeting like this when you’re clearly not even hearing a word I’m saying.”

Rio blinks, suddenly realizing she’s been staring at the bread basket. “I—I’m sorry,” she clears her throat. “I’m listening.” At the same time, the clatter of dishes and low chatter returns to her consciousness.

Hela exhales, regarding Rio like a four-eyed fish gasping at the surface for air. Rio feels the same, suddenly parched, as if the water around her has thinned.

Then, with careful patience, she hears Hela say, “You know, we don’t have to talk about work if you’re not up for it.”

“No, I’m good.” Rio shakes her head. 

What else would they even talk about? 

She definitely doesn’t want to dredge up what happened last week. 

The whole thing is almost laughable if she thinks about it. The absurdity of it. How does that even happen? How does someone end something that never really even started? 

And yet…Agatha did. 

She cut it off before Rio could even voice what she felt. What a tragedy.

Definitely not the kind of topic someone wants over a nice morning brunch.

Hela leans back, letting out a slow sigh. Though unconvinced, she drags out her words as she continues.

“Well, maybe this will help. Your first international assignment, if you’re interested.” She slides a file across the table. “Three months in Queensland, looking at how climate and other environmental changes are affecting life on the islands. It’s supposed to be mine, but I’d rather my family, especially my brothers, didn’t know I’m in Australia. It’s yours if you want it. I figured you might be better suited for it. Plus, a change of scenery could do you some good.”

Rio picks up the file and flips through it. 

The assignment is detailed: a deep dive into coastal communities grappling with rising sea levels, gathering firsthand accounts from the locals and its leaders. She’s never done anything like this before, but she’s always wanted to.

“And when would I be leaving?” she asks, running her eyes over the notes.

“That depends on your schedule. But the team over there has already been informed someone could head out anytime this week.”

Great, Rio thinks, still staring at the file.

“And if I say I want to go tomorrow, could the publication arrange the trip?”

Hela blinks, disbelief written across her face. “You want to leave tomorrow?”

“Yes,” Rio replies, sure of herself. Then, more seriously, she adds, “I’d rather be out there, actually doing something, than spend another day cooped up in my apartment.”

Hela studies her for a long stretch. “I mean, Peggy could have everything arranged by tomorrow morning. But you could at least give it another day. Three months is still a long time to be away from here.”

Rio considers it. Three months. That’s basically a year in dog years. Why she even thinks about dog years, she has no clue. Probably the hangover. She definitely spent a significant amount drinking last night.

Unsolicited breakups do that to people.

But she does need to get away. An international assignment is exactly the kind of opportunity that looks great on a resume, and she could even treat it like a mini-vacation. Might as well take it.

Pressing her lips together, Rio says, “I’m sure. Have them fly me out tomorrow. The sooner I start the assignment, the sooner the story hits print.” 

And the sooner she can get away from Agatha.

Rio pushes open the restroom door and checks the time on her phone. Saying yes to Hela only minutes ago means she’s got barely a day to pack for a three-month trip. 

She also still needs to give Alice and Lorna a heads-up. It will be only a quick call but Lorna will definitely have questions. 

Luckily, Rio can frame it as work, because technically it is. An international assignment is an international assignment, even if it’s really just an excuse to disappear for a while and breathe.

But she barely looks up from her phone, tapping out a quick message to Alice about needing to talk when she gets home, before she accidentally bumps into someone.

“Good heavens! Do mind where you’re walking!”

“I—sorry,” Rio mutters, but the apology immediately dies the second she meets the woman’s baleful glare. 

Whatever mess of feelings she still carries for Agatha sharpens into a sudden, hot burn when she recognizes Agatha’s mother. 

Seriously, is the universe testing her now?

Evanora’s eyes narrow in instant recognition, her lips curling as if the sight of Rio offends her. 

“I remember you.” Her voice drips with condescension, wrapped in a patrician drawl. “The assistant my daughter speaks of so fondly. How is she these days? I heard about that Stark business her little magazine got dragged into. I’ve always said those sorts of frivolous ventures of hers would never last. But, of course, she never listens, and look where that’s gotten her.”

Rio debates whether to give Evanora the satisfaction of a reply or just walk away, but the jab at Agatha is too much to let slide, even with Agatha being the last person she wants to think about right now.

And it doesn’t help that the memory of everything this woman put her daughter through flares in Rio’s chest like a lit match.

“Not that it’s any of your business, Mrs. Harkness, but I don’t work for your daughter anymore.” Her hands curl lightly at her sides, knuckles white, as she forces a controlled inhale. “However, I can assure you, her so-called ‘frivolous venture’ is doing just fine.”

She’s about to walk away when she hears Evanora’s loud and dismissive scoff. 

“All that effort to dig up dirt on her own mother, and she still eventually got rid of you?” She lets out a cold, mocking chuckle. “Truly, evil never seems to be satisfied, does it?”

Rio feels a rush of heat pulse through her veins, but it’s the words before the insult that catches her attention.

“What did you just say?”

“I don’t repeat myself, child.”

Rio stiffens, staring in disbelief at the recognizable words. She can’t, for the life of her, wrap her head around the idea that someone like Agatha could have come from this woman.

“Why would your own daughter dig up dirt on you?” Rio asks, pressing despite herself. 

Her mind goes back to the heated argument between Evanora and Agatha at the office the first time Agatha had fired her.

But it takes Evanora a few seconds of coldly scrutinizing Rio before she finally opens her mouth.

“What is it about you that makes my selfish, heartless, ingrate daughter go to such lengths? All because of one idle threat I made, that I could ruin your prospects and see to it that you couldn’t work wherever you pleased?”

Rio can’t believe what she’s hearing. 

She remembers how Agatha had gone out of her way to keep her away from her mother. And now it all makes sense: why Agatha fired her and then brought her back, why she’d always been so careful with her career.

All this time, Agatha had been looking out for her just as much as she had been looking out for Agatha.

And for the first time, she realizes that everything she’s done, every risk she’s taken, has been because she loves Agatha. 

And if Agatha has been doing the same for her, maybe, just maybe, Agatha has been feeling the same all along.

She almost forgets Evanora is still there until the rest of her words hit her ears.

“That poor child will end up alone, just as I’ve always told her. She’s nothing but a storm who leaves ruin in her wake. Nobody in their right mind, or anyone with God-fearing morals, would want to put up with that.”

Rio has had enough. She jabs a finger at the older woman, her patience finally snapping. Evanora should be thanking heaven they’re in a public place (and only partially out of sight from the rest of the restaurant) because if they weren’t, Rio would have no qualms about punching her in the face.

“It’s a shame you don’t see how lucky you are to have Agatha as a daughter, especially since she’s the strongest person I know, having survived you as a mother. You may think poorly of me, but I’ll make damn sure she’s never touched by your cruelty again.”

Evanora seems taken aback by Rio’s unexpected boldness, and it only gives the latter more courage to speak her mind.

“And you’re dead wrong. She will never, ever end up alone, because I know there are people who actually care about your daughter, in ways your narrow-minded faith and self-righteous bullshit could never understand. So stay the hell away from her, or you’ll have me to deal with.”

Rio jabs her finger once more before turning and walking out, leaving the older woman stunned and speechless.

Perhaps it’s the adrenaline still thrumming in her veins from verbally taking down a pompous white woman by the restroom of a crowded restaurant, and actually getting away with it.

Or perhaps it’s something else entirely. 

Whatever it is, Rio finds herself sliding into a cab on a bustling afternoon, the city blurring past the windows, headed for an address she knows better than her own.

Being back in Nocturne is something she never thought would happen after the fallout with Agatha, yet the familiar walls immediately wrap her in a strange kind of comfort.

She had actually been thinking about this for a week. Bursting into Agatha’s office or showing up at her door, even briefly flirting with the idea of doing it drunk so she could at least blame her honesty on the booze.

But hearing those things straight from Evanora just hours ago made Rio realize she couldn’t let another day go by without Agatha knowing how she feels.

If things go south again, so be it. 

She’s out of here tomorrow anyway. Australia’s big enough to let her heal in peace.

“Rio? W-what are you doing here?” Jen’s voice cracks with surprise and a hint of intrigue as she jumps up from her desk. 

Rio doesn’t even look at her. “Where is she?” 

The other assistant across the room, whom Rio barely registers, looks just as puzzled.

“She’s inside, but she’s on a very important call, so—hey! Where do you think you’re going? You can’t just barge in like that—Rio!”

Jen’s voice fizzles with irritation, like a mosquito meeting its pop on a bug zapper, the second Rio slips into Agatha’s office and slams the door behind her, locking it for good measure.

The woman inside startles, her tired eyes widening just a fraction as Rio freezes a few feet away.

“Rio?” Agatha says, the name slipping out before she can stop it. But the phone currently pressed to her ear crackles. “No, not you, Jacqueline. That’s—it seems I’ll have to call you later. Oui, je te rappellerai,” she adds, her voice clipped in French before she sets the phone down, her eyes fixing on Rio.

The silence between them drags on a beat too long, as if the world itself decided to pause just to watch and listen. Agatha finally cuts through it again. “What are you doing here?”

Rio paces in place, her feet mirroring the restlessness she feels in her chest. 

Her heart drums like it’s trying to punch its way out of her ribs.

She had perhaps imagined this moment once or twice before, telling Agatha how she felt, but never like this.

She thought she would take it slow, wait until she was sure the other woman would not just bolt. But the timing now leaves no room for tiptoeing around it.

“You said I’m reckless,” she starts, chest rising and falling too fast, but she forces her voice to stay steady. “That I have a tendency to be, when it comes to you. And yeah, maybe I do. But that doesn’t mean I can’t handle my own shit.” Agatha doesn’t say anything, so she keeps going. “I’m not some fragile, incapable person you think I am. Yes, I’m younger. Yes, I’m new to this business. But that doesn’t make me any less capable of standing on my own, or of protecting myself from the consequences of my choices.” 

Agatha could only stare at her, and Rio takes a deep breath. 

The last time they’d had a conversation like this, it had ended with her getting fired, storming out of this very office, or Agatha leaving her apartment.

And now, this might just end the same way.

But she realizes this might be the only chance she’ll ever get to say what she truly feels. 

Why she does the things she does for Agatha, why she can’t look away when Agatha tells her to, why she keeps getting herself into the problems Agatha wants to keep her out of.

Every unspoken word, every risk she’s ever taken, it all comes down to this. And even though she’s terrified of whatever comes next, she can’t let this pass without telling Agatha the whole truth.

“I’ve said it already, and I’ll say it again. I’ve done things for other people before, but for you I’d do them differently.” Rio takes a beat to breathe. “Do you know why Agatha?”

Agatha just looks at her intently, as if she, too, is holding herself together between breaths.

Agatha somehow managed to become Rio’s anchor, even if everyone else might think she’s the current pulling her under. But Rio knows, deep down, that Agatha is the one keeping her afloat, the one who keeps pushing her back to shore. 

And even if it were the other way around, like everyone else thinks, Rio wouldn’t mind drowning.

Not when she can stare long and unflinching into Agatha’s eyes, seeing both the storm and the calm all at once.

In that moment, she admits to herself that she was never meant to withstand eyes like hers. She was made to sink completely, to let herself drift, piece by piece, at Agatha’s feet. 

“The reason I do the things I do for you is because…” She falters, then forces herself to meet Agatha’s eyes. “It’s because I love you,” she finally admits, biting her lip and shaking her head. “No…you know what? That doesn’t even begin to cover it. Even saying ‘love’ feels too fucking small to describe this.” She presses a hand to her chest, over her heart. “But then I can’t call it anything else. And yes, I know that’s the kind of word you’d run from the second someone says it. But that’s exactly how I feel. That’s why I can’t help how I am around you. Everything I do, I do because I love you. I’m hopelessly, irreversibly, entirely in love with you, Agatha.”

Agatha blinks, clearly caught off guard, her blue eyes widening briefly before softening into that familiar, almost fragile look Rio knows better than anyone. 

“You’ve told me over and over that you trust me. Now let that trust be enough to tell me what’s really going through your head when you look at me like that.”

But all that comes in reply is a faint, almost whispered, “Rio.”

Rio shakes her head, determined to hear everything. “Just this once, Agatha. Please, the whole truth.” Her knees even threaten to buckle. “What are you thinking?”

Every nerve in Rio’s body seizes, and a sudden wave of nausea twists through her throat, made worse by Agatha, who is just staring at her.

If only she could read Agatha’s mind in this moment, then perhaps this whole conundrum would be easier to solve.

But she can’t. So now she’s stuck, eye to eye with the woman she loves, waiting for even a single word.

“I—” Agatha opens her mouth, then closes it again.

Rio only notices her own tears sliding down her cheeks when she sees Agatha struggling to hold back hers. Her blue eyes are faintly rimmed with red, glassier than Rio has ever seen. 

Now, the stretching silence makes Rio almost wish Agatha would just blow her to pieces.

It might have hurt less than this dagger twisting between her ribs. Because now she feels the feeblest glimmer of hope, and hope is the most dangerous thing Agatha could ever give her.

Say it. Please, just say it.

Rio wills the words silently, letting her hazel eyes plead with the woman in front of her, hoping she can, in some way, feel them without hearing them. And by whatever god is listening, Agatha does feel the words behind Rio’s eyes, and finally, she speaks:

“I think you should leave.” 

Frantic packing after a night of crying and drowning in the kind of cheap beer only a 24-hour convenience store can offer is not recommended if someone plans to survive an almost 24-hour flight halfway across the world.

Perhaps that should be Rio’s next article when she comes back: Love, Loss, and Layovers: How Lesbians Handle Heartbreak at 30,000 Feet.

And if she were to write it, rule number one would be simple: never, ever fall in love with a stone-cold succubus of a woman whose full-time job is making other people miserable by being a stone-cold succubus. 

More importantly, never lie at work to attend Pride, especially when the boss is likely to be there. That alone could save anyone a whole lot of heartbreak.

She stuffs the shirt she wore to last Pride into the back of her dresser. Unfortunately, digging through clothes while packing all day dredged it back up. She’d thought about burning it, but why waste perfectly good fabric, and poison the planet in the process?

Yesterday, she had told Agatha that she loves her. And it might have hurt less if, deep down, she knew Agatha didn’t feel the same. Because knowing her love answers in kind, and Agatha not choosing to say it back, makes it fucking worse. Fucking tragic, even.

Her tragedy might as well be shared by the heavens, because it’s been raining nonstop since morning.

Thankfully, there’s no warning of her evening flight being canceled. She doesn’t think she could survive another night of wallowing in her room.

She gives it one last once-over, making sure she hasn’t left her passport on the bedside table or anything else important for her three-month trip, then closes the door.

She pads to the kitchen and scribbles a note for Alice, who’d reluctantly left almost an hour ago for work.

Alice had insisted on driving her to the airport, and Rio appreciated it, really.

But she didn’t want her best friend hovering over her, feeling sorry for her, or quietly questioning this whole trip.

She sticks the note on the fridge, promising to call once she lands in Cairns.

She also warns Alice to keep Billy away from her plants while she’s gone, saying the kid couldn’t nurture a cactus if his life depended on it. He’s like a reverse Midas, turning every leaf he touches into instant death.

The same trait the woman who broke her heart yesterday had, just before Rio taught her how to.

But Rio quickly shakes the thought off. If she wants to survive this grueling, almost 24-hour flight to the land down under, it has to start with not letting herself cry again at the mere thought of the said woman.

She’s about to dump the coffee mugs she’s been drinking from all day into the sink when a frantic knocking rattles the front door.

Rio wonders who it could be, then remembers that Billy had texted her this morning, saying he’d try to leave his boyfriend’s place early to stop by before she left. It must be the teen coming to say goodbye.

She grabs her oversized rucksack from the couch, snatches her keys, and heads for the door. 

It’s only when she opens it that she wishes she hadn’t.

“What the hell are you doing here?” She clamps down on the urge to slam the door shut.

She stares at the figure in front of her, silently hoping the disdain in her eyes comes through louder than the surprise. Because standing on her front door is Agatha. 

Dressed in a dark blue velvet gown with long sleeves, the side panel a deep, dark fuchsia — a dress clearly meant for some gala or charity event, yet now drenched from the relentless rain outside. Her long, dark hair is plastered to her face and shoulders, droplets tracing the curve of her jaw, and a fob dangles loosely from her fingers.

“Where are you going?” Agatha retorts, eyeing the rucksack on Rio’s shoulder instead of answering her question. Her chest heaves, and she’s visibly shivering from the cold.

It takes everything in Rio not to look at her worriedly. Jesus. Did she really drive all the way here by herself? She shoves the thought down, and clears her throat.

“None of your business.”

Agatha frowns at her. “I’m asking you a question, Rio. Where are you going?”

Still, Rio doesn’t answer and just starts a staring contest. 

Why give Agatha the satisfaction of a response? She could just slam the door in her face, right? Agatha at the very least deserves that. But seeing her like this, shivering, drenched, clearly exhausted, makes it harder for Rio to go through with it.

“Why do you even care? And I asked you first. What are you doing here?”

“No. I am asking you. Where on earth are you going?”

Rio scoffs at Agatha’s audacity but answers anyway. Might as well get this over with. “I’m heading to the airport. There. Now you know. Satisfied?” she snaps. “Now, if you’ll excuse me, you’re blocking my door.”

“And why would you be heading to the airport?”

Rio tugs her bag strap tighter. “Because I have a flight to catch. Why else?” 

Agatha doesn’t back down. “Flight to where exactly?”

Rio exhales and crosses her arms. “You’re not going to let me leave until I answer, are you?”

“You do know me well.”

“Oh, do I really?” Rio hisses, arching an eyebrow, her tone dripping with sarcasm and frustration. It’s only when she catches the obvious hurt in Agatha’s eyes that she’s forced to relent just enough. “I’m covering another feature for the Journal. They’re sending me to Queensland to—”

“Queensland?” Agatha’s usual mask of practiced indifference slips just enough for Rio to notice. Rio nods, and Agatha follows with, “And you’re leaving right now?”

“I wouldn’t be standing at this door, about to leave, if I wasn’t.”

Agatha only stares at her, then nods, as if silently conceding she deserves the tone Rio is using. 

Rio catches the subtle swallow. 

“And how long are they sending you out there for?” 

“About three months.”

“Three months?” Her blue eyes give her away. “And you didn’t even think twice about it?”

Truth is, Rio had thought twice about it because of Agatha. But it’s also Agatha who actually pushed her to do it anyway. But that’s not something Agatha needs to hear.

Rio lets out a small scoff, clicking her tongue against her cheek. “Why would I pass up a perfect opportunity for an international assignment? Now, please, step aside. I’m really running late.”

That’s a lie. She has nearly five hours to spare.

“Can we just talk for a minute?”

“No. We had plenty of that yesterday and the other night. I don’t have time for another now, so just get out of my way, Agatha.”

But Agatha bars the doorway with one arm.

“I’m not letting you leave unless we talk.”

Rio fights the urge to jump out a nearby window and hail a cab.

“As far as I remember, there’s nothing left to talk about. I got your message loud and clear, and I’ve already said everything I need to say. If you’re worried I’m upset, trust me, I’m doing my best not to be. Now, unless you want that to change, please move out of my way.”

Rio reaches to move Agatha’s arm, but Agatha plants her palm against her sternum and pushes back, harder than Rio expects from someone balanced on dagger-heeled Jimmy Choos.

“What the hell?” she glares, stumbling as her backpack drops with a dull smack. “Did you just shove me? For real?”

“I mean it, Rio. You’re not going anywhere until we talk.”

Rio steps back and checks her watch. 

She still has a couple of hours to spare, but she’d rather kill time at the airport than spend another minute trapped in the agonizing presence of Agatha Harkness. 

One more rejection from this woman is the last thing she needs before she leaves. 

“Agatha, I really can’t do this right now,” she says, trying for authority, though her voice wavers more than she wants. “What’s left to talk about? I already said what I said. We’re not on the same page, I get it. What else do you want? For me to admit I’m an idiot for even saying it?” She bites her lip, refusing to repeat yesterday’s words. “Fine then. I’m an idiot. Now forget it, okay? We’re done here.”

“No. You don’t get to decide when this is over. I do,” Agatha snaps, jabbing a finger at Rio, who recoils. “And yes, you are, undeniably, an idiot. Dropping all that on me yesterday and now running off? Impeccable timing, Rio. Truly impeccable.”

Rio just stares for a beat, caught between shock and awe at the sudden ferocity in Agatha’s voice. “Seriously? You’re the one who’s angry right now?” She gives a short, bitter laugh. “Yeah, okay. Sure.”

Agatha tries to breathe, still visibly shaking from the cold, but Rio is too mad to offer even a hint of sympathy. She notices the quick rise and fall of Agatha’s chest as she struggles for composure, and, against her will, Rio feels her own anger beginning to thaw.

“Sorry. I shouldn’t have—” Agatha glances down at her drenched gown. “Just listen to me. Please, Rio?”

Rio hesitates, letting the silence stretch like a drawn-out chord. Then, with a reluctant tilt of her head, she sighs. “Fine. Just make it quick before I change my mind.”

Agatha perks up, and nothing could have prepared Rio for seeing her on the verge of tears just because Rio agreed to listen. Rio catches her own breath and forces her face into a neutral expression.

Agatha clears her throat. “I…uh, I’ve always prided myself on staying in control, on always knowing what comes next. I think you know that by now. That’s how I’ve built my life, and my career along with it. I plan, I anticipate, I stay one step ahead of everyone else. And I make sure nothing ever pushes me out of it.” 

Silence stretches between them a bit until Agatha lets out a slow breath.

“And I’ve been doing that, keeping everything under control just fine — until you showed up. Suddenly, I’m chasing myself…and losing. And that’s impossible, because the Agatha Harkness I know doesn’t lose. But with you, it’s like there’s a version of me I’m trying to reach, and then you’re right there in the way, and I completely forget where I am, or what it is I’m even reaching for.”

Rio hates that her heart is racing. 

She’s supposed to be mad, but her anger feels like it’s shrinking as she watches Agatha pause, visibly struggling to get the words out. She’s confessing that Rio unsettles her, that Rio has thrown her off balance, and Rio doesn’t know whether to step forward or step back.

“You asked me what I was thinking after you said all that yesterday,” Agatha begins again. “Well, the truth is, it’s the same thing I’ve been thinking long before you even said any of it.” She doesn’t break eye contact, even as Rio struggles to hold hers. “I mean, how could I not? How could I not, when you made it far too easy? That’s what runs through my head every time I look at you. Every thought I have of you starts there, and it never really ends.”

The command in Agatha’s tone wavers as she exhales again slowly. 

And for the first time, her voice doesn’t even sound like it belongs to Agatha Harkness.

“When you make me laugh until I forget why I was angry. When you ramble about the dumbest little things and I forget why I was scared. When you sometimes say my name in your sleep. When your scent gets stuck on my clothes and I catch myself smiling like some lovesick schoolgirl.” Agatha pauses, then, with burning frustration, “I’m a grown woman, and the editor of the country’s most cutting-edge fashion magazine, for heaven’s sake! I shouldn’t be catching myself smiling like some stupid schoolgirl.”

Her eyes don’t cower, not even for a second. And that alone makes Rio hold her own breath.

“But what’s worse is realizing that I don’t even mind it anymore. And every time you stumble over your words, every time that ridiculous smile spreads across your face, I just want to kiss you like some stupid schoolgirl.” She draws another shaky breath. “Being with you makes it feel like I’m finally able to breathe. Because I know there’s no hiding when I’m with you. You see me. All of me. You see through me, and even though it fucking terrifies me, I’d still fucking let you. I’d still let you, because every part of me just can’t get enough of you, Rio. So tell me, how could I ever not love you?”

Rio doesn’t move. Not a word, not even a breath escapes her. 

She just stands there, willing her legs not to give out.

Agatha, on the other hand, looks like she’s just stepped off a ledge. 

Her composure, poise, and every piece of carefully crafted armor have utterly slipped. The hand that had been pointed at Rio only minutes ago drops uselessly to her side.

“But I’m afraid that I might fail at this. What can I even bring to a relationship? I don’t even know how to be in a normal one. You, of all people, know firsthand that I’ve miserably failed in that department. And I’m terrified that it could be you now, because what I can give you isn’t the full, perfect version of the love you deserve, and that scares the hell out of me because you’re—”

“Agatha,” Rio quickly grabs her hands, her own tears falling down her cheeks. “Baby, there’s no such thing as a full, perfect version of love. At least, not at the start. Love isn’t a finished manuscript. You don’t hand over the final draft the first time you write. You revise, you fix, you send it out. Love’s the same way, and that’s okay. That’s how it grows.” 

Another beat passes, just the two of them staring into each other’s tear-filled eyes.

“Do you ever wonder why you see me in the middle, when you said you were trying to reach this other, perfect version of yourself? The one who never loses? Maybe it’s because I don’t need that perfect version, Agatha. I’m in the middle because I simply want to meet you where you are. I’m here because I want this you, the one you are right now. The one who’s trying, the one who’s scared, the one who’s still learning. Even if it’s a grown woman who feels like a lovesick schoolgirl when she’s with me,” Rio says, letting out a soft chuckle they both share. “I’d still want you, even if it’s not the ideal version you think you should be. Just the version that makes you…whole enough to be with me.”

The ride to the airport passes in near silence, broken only by the sound of passing cars, the light patter of rain, and the boygenius album playing softly through Agatha’s speakers.

Neither of them has spoken much since their conversation at Rio’s apartment. Even though Rio keeps thinking of things she could say, the words just won’t come.

And Agatha, if anything, has said even less, right up until they reach the airport.

Still, the ride has at least given them a little more time together before she leaves.

And it seems Agatha wants to stretch that borrowed time a bit longer, too. Already changed into one of Rio’s hoodies, she pulls the hood up and tucks all her hair beneath it. Only after a quick phone call to a certain someone and a short talk about an escort pass do they finally step out of the car.

Now they sit side by side on the hard airport chairs, the hood of Rio’s hoodie pulled so low over Agatha’s head, sunglasses hiding her from any prying eyes even though it’s dark outside.

They wordlessly sip one awful airport coffee after another as they wait, and not once does Rio hear her complain.

Two hours pass slowly before Rio’s plane is finally called, and it’s time to go. They both stand almost at the same time, and Rio hesitates for a second before pulling Agatha into a long, tight hug.

She holds on longer than she intends, breathing in the familiar lavender scent, feeling the warmth of Agatha’s body pressed against her own. Agatha squeezes back just as firmly, a small sigh slipping against Rio’s ear, before they slowly step apart. 

Rio gives her a small smile, and Agatha returns it just as softly.

“When I get back, you better have that ice cream date planned,” Rio teases, trying to lighten the mood without giving Agatha a chance to overthink anything else.

The latter just rolls her eyes. “As if you’d ever let me forget it.”

Rio chuckles, and they share a look, both exhaling at the same time.

After a brief glance around the nearly empty lounge, Agatha lets out another breath, slips off her sunglasses, and grabs Rio by the strap of her backpack, pulling her in without hesitation.

The kiss is searing and unrestrained, and Rio answers by pressing herself tight against Agatha, her hands curling around her waist as if bracing against gravity itself.

What has Rio done? Is it too late to back out now? How on earth could she possibly get through the next three months without this woman?

A tiny, frustrated sigh escapes Agatha as she pulls away, her cheeks flushed.

“That better carry you through your whole trip,” she quips, cradling her face with both hands, and can’t resist giving Rio another quick peck on the lips.

Rio smiles against her, the warmth of her body settling into her as she looks around. Can’t believe they just did that out here. Well, kissing in an airport is common enough not to draw much attention anyway.

Then she looks back at Agatha, and smiles again as she studies her.

Wearing Rio’s oversized hoodie, long hair tucked inside the hood, Rio’s faded jogging trousers, and scuffed white sneakers, Agatha looks nothing like the editor-in-chief of New York’s top fashion magazine. It’s far from her customary high-fashion standards, yet Rio can’t help but find it irresistibly endearing.

“I know what you’re thinking, and don’t even dare mention this to anyone. This doesn’t do my reputation any favors,” Agatha warns, aware of how she looks.

Rio chuckles and shakes her head, though inside she’s really thinking, I can’t believe I get to love you like this. Instead, she smiles a little and says, “Don’t worry, I intend to keep this particular picture of Agatha Harkness just to myself.” She tucks a strand of hair from Agatha’s forehead. “Try not to miss me too much.”

Agatha hums, then mutters, “I think I’ll survive.”

But the way her eyes look at Rio tells her everything she needs to know. They hold each other’s gaze a little longer, an intimate understanding passing between them, before Rio leans in for one final hug. 

She feels Agatha close her eyes, pressing closer as she tightens her hold. 

Yeah. There’s no doubt, they’ll miss each other terribly.

It had only taken about five and a half days before Rio had started receiving lengthy emails from Agatha, rather than their usual string of quick, back-and-forth texts.

Mostly reminders and gentle nagging to reapply sunscreen every two hours because the Australian sun is brutal at this time of year, not to forget drinking enough water or risk passing out on some beach, warnings that it’s still stinger season and how dangerously venomous the jellyfish can be, and never to neglect wearing a life vest whenever hopping from one island to the next.

From time to time, their correspondence had included updates about what had been happening in New York, particularly at work, and occasionally Agatha had vented a little about the prosaic catastrophe (as she likes to call it) unfolding at Nocturne headquarters.

Agatha’s emails had become her ritual at the end of each week, arriving whenever she returned to her small, rustic inn on one of the main islands, where she could get online before moving to another island that might, or might not, have reliable internet.

She opens her laptop, and clicks on Agatha’s email first among the dozens waiting in her inbox.

Dear Rio,

I trust you’re actually taking my warnings seriously. Sunburn is not a joke. The jellyfish are not a joke either. And if you get stung by one of those tiny nightmares, I swear I will personally file a lawsuit against whoever thought it was a good idea to send you into harm’s way.

Did you know jellyfish stingers burn out once they hit something? I read it in an article. They’re designed for plankton, not journalists with zero sense of danger. 

So please, for the love of the ecosystem, don’t go screwing up the food chain while you’re at it.

I imagine the Australians will have vinegar bottles lined up along the beach in case you, or someone equally reckless, wanders into a tentacle. You’ll probably think it’s quaint. I, on the other hand, see it as proof of how often people ignore the signs.

That said, I still expect you to have fun down there. Just keep yourself out of trouble. And, of course, think of me waiting here when you inevitably ignore that advice. 

—Agatha

Rio shakes her head slightly, a wide grin spreading across her face as she thought about how Agatha had actually gone and researched Australia’s marine life all for her.

She takes a sip of the bitter, lukewarm coffee from the inn’s chipped mug before starting to type her reply.

My dearest Agatha, 

Don’t worry, your warnings have been duly noted, though I can’t promise my grin will ever be any smaller when I think of them.

The sunburn situation is under control (thankfully I remember to reapply every two hours, just like you said), and you also don’t have to worry about me messing up the ecosystem with a jellyfish sting. I’m accompanied by a few very capable local guides who make sure I stay well out of trouble. 

You’d be proud, though. They even showed me how to safely hold a tiny reef fish without startling it and taught me which shells are safe to touch.

Work going okay? Hope all the hubbub with the ownership change isn’t driving you crazy. A little bird tells me you haven’t been firing anyone, so I guess that’s a good sign. But please, don’t forget to eat. Even someone like you, who can handle anything, needs real food. I’d hate to hear you’re surviving on just coffee and whatever random snacks you grab on the go.

As for me…well, attached is a little proof that I’m somehow managing to follow your advice and have fun at the same time. It took a while to earn the locals’ trust since they’re very protective of their home, and I couldn’t blame them. It had only been two weeks, but the beauty of the islands had already captured my heart. It truly is a place that deserves protecting.

Luckily, I’ve made a few friends by helping them gather crabs, catch baitfish, and even learning to weave palm fronds into little nets. Now they’re showing me hidden swimming spots and pointing out all the tiny creatures I’d otherwise overlook. I’m learning more from them in a single day than I ever could from a textbook, and it’s been absolutely incredible.

Missing you more than I thought possible.

Yours,
Rio

Before hitting send, Rio attaches a photo of herself swimming with the local kids, wearing her forest green bikini top and shorts and a wide, sun-soaked grin.

A few days later, she opens Agatha’s reply, and it is every bit as pointed and prissy as she had anticipated.

Dear Rio, 

I’m happy to see that you’re actually enjoying yourself. I can practically hear your laughter through this photo. Though I couldn’t help but notice that the shot includes a small crowd looking at you with more admiration than is strictly necessary. Do they know someone is waiting for you here when you return? If not, perhaps it’s time to enlighten them, don’t you think?

Work has been interesting, to say the least. And your little bird, whoever that may be (rest assured, I will somehow find out), is correct. No one has been fired lately. 

I can only assume it’s either because I’ve been too preoccupied or, miraculously, people have finally started doing their jobs properly instead of being complete imbeciles. 

Remarkably, Pepper has been handling things far better than Stark ever did. It’s almost unsettling how competent she’s being.

I’ll be attending a gala next month, and I’m still struggling to decide what to wear. Monica and Sue have been excruciatingly slow at preparing options.

And while you are finding the pleasure in all your little adventures, I’m still reminding you to keep your mischief within tolerable limits. I would like your fingers still intact when you get back.

Also, I admit, things here would be far more interesting if you were around.

—Agatha

It’s late at night, just before she drifts off to sleep, that Rio finally sends a reply of her own.

My dearest Agatha,

I’m happy you can hear my laughter through the photo, though I swear most of it comes from trying not to fall off the rocks while diving with the kids. 

And don’t worry, my admirers know full well that someone very important is waiting for me back home. 

I might have also mentioned, casually, that this someone is as possessive as a mantis shrimp when it comes to what’s hers, so they won’t be trying anything. I left absolutely no room for confusion.

As for my little insider, don’t even think about hunting them down. Let me have eyes there. It keeps me connected to you in a way and calms my thoughts while I’m here. I promise I’m only letting them report on the important stuff.

About your gala. Might I suggest darker colors? They’ll make those piercing eyes of yours stand out even more. Though I’m sure you’ll look breathtaking as always, no matter what Monica and Sue manage.

While I’m finding adventure in every corner, exploring hidden inlets, and making spectacularly clumsy attempts at fishing, I’m keeping your warnings in mind. Don’t worry, fingers intact, promise.

Also, I watched a breathtaking sunset today, and for a moment, it felt like you were right here with me. Even surrounded by all this beauty and adventure, I can’t help but miss you even more.

Yours,
Rio

Rio smiles as she reads Agatha’s reply a few nights later.

Dear Rio, 

It’s been a maelstrom here, though a productive one. I’ve been neck-deep in managing the latest issue, and, surprisingly, Pepper hasn’t raised a single concern about the budget. In fact, I think we’re aligning better than I ever expected. Almost makes me wonder if I’ve been too quick to doubt her.

Marmee and Fanny are staying at my townhouse for the weekend. Marmee just signed up for a two-day bonsai and flower-arranging workshop at the New York Botanical Garden. Apparently it’s the “latest craze” in her social circle.

And she’s been insisting on feeding me practically nonstop. So don’t worry, I’m well-fed, though I can’t help but wonder if I’ll still fit into the gala outfit I chose after Marmee’s enthusiastic ministrations. 

I followed your advice, by the way. Going with a darker color, and I admit, it’s a perfect contrast to make my eyes stand out. When did you become such a fashion expert, I wonder?

—Agatha

Unfortunately, it had taken longer than Rio had expected before she’s able to reply.

My dearest Agatha, 

I’m sorry I hadn’t replied sooner. We ended up stuck on a tiny, remote island longer than planned. The boat broke down, and we had to wait three extra days. But everything’s fine now. The locals there were kind enough to welcome me into their home and even taught me how to make these cute seashell bracelets. I promised them I’d bring you one.

I’m certainly still not an expert in fashion. Perhaps I’ve just grown to become an expert in you. :) 

I’m happy to hear Marmee is taking on a new hobby and keeping you well-fed. And of course, Fanny must be loving all the extra attention.

The other islands here are even more beautiful than I imagined, but the beauty doesn’t exactly hide the struggle. I’ve watched fishermen dragging in nearly empty nets, kids carrying loads that are too heavy for their age, parents patching together a living however they can. It’s hard, exhausting work, and it humbles me every day. Though I’m grateful I get to tell their story, I just wish I could do more.

The time on that island gave me a lot of space to think. Mostly about you. Even more so after I met an old woman who waits on the shore every day for her husband to return from fishing. I asked her why she still does it after all these years. She just smiled and said, “The sea may not always be kind, but it always gives me back the man I love. So I wait at the shore, to remind the sea he has someone to return to.”

I haven’t been able to shake that. And it made me realize I don’t ever want to stop waiting for you either.

I love you, my dearest Agatha. Being here, so far from you, only makes me feel it more deeply. Because even surrounded by all this beauty, it’s still really you I’m thinking of.

Until I can tell you all of this in person, 
Rio

-

My Rio, 

I was worried sick when I didn’t hear from you for a few days. My mind spun through every possible scenario, each one worse than the last. If I’m being honest, I was this close to booking a flight on impulse, tossing aside every rational thought, just to make sure you were safe. And embarrassingly enough, I even caught myself picturing storming every island there if I didn’t hear from you soon.

I realize now just how unbearable the thought of anything happening to you truly is. Even from halfway across the world, you occupy more space in my mind than anyone or anything else. 

It’s infuriating, this hold you have over me. What on earth have you done? And why, despite all better judgment, do I find myself unwilling to be free of it?

Anyway, I have no doubt you’ll be writing a compelling piece, because that’s what you do. You have this rare gift of making people feel like they’ve been there themselves, like they’re seeing it all through your eyes. I can already imagine you’ll make their stories matter, simply because they mattered to you.

Also, how strict is that three-month timeline your editor gave you? Do you think there’s any chance you’ll be back the first week? I might need someone to make the other dreadfully boring guests at that gala I mentioned a bit more tolerable. But no pressure if you can’t, of course. 

I’ve already started counting the days until you’re back, and somehow every second without you stretches into a year. I hate admitting it, especially as someone who prides herself on staying busy, but it feels like my whole world is on pause until you’re here again.

Yours,
Agatha

Rio tumbles off the plane like a storm-drenched rag doll, each step heavy with a backpack that feels even heavier than when she left. 

Her short hair is wild and frizzy from nearly three months of sun, salt, and humidity. She didn’t have time to freshen up on the plane, hiding her tired eyes behind aviators. 

Pushing through the throng of travelers, she rolls her backpack across the cracked tile, eyes scanning for the taxi line like a survivor finally spotting solid ground after months at sea.

“No need to hunt for a cab,” someone says, close enough to feel the words brush her ear.

Rio spins toward the voice, eyes wide. 

“Jen? What—what are you doing here?” Seeing a familiar face after so much time away brings Rio an almost instant sense of comfort, even though it’s someone she didn’t really expect. “Wait, did Agatha send you? I very specifically said not to.”

Jen’s expression doesn’t change, though Rio can tell she’s clearly annoyed. A look she’s seen countless times during their shared past at Nocturne, one that hints at impatience and exasperation.

“No. She didn’t. I came on my own. Now get your ass moving. I had to park over there, and the last thing I need now is a parking ticket.”

“Really?” Rio asks, scratching her neck like a confused goldfish, but she still follows her former colleague toward the parked car. How did she even know Rio was coming home?

Rio wants to ask more questions, but seeing Jen look like someone’s holding a gun to her head, she decides not to pry and lets the heavy, awkward silence of the car ride speak for itself.

It’s also a bit of a relief, if she’s being honest. Nearly twenty-four hours trapped on planes have left her drained, and she can barely form a coherent thought anyway. 

Ever since the plane had landed, her mind has been completely consumed with how badly she can’t wait to see Agatha again.

So, after a few perfunctory exchanges with her unexpected company, she sinks into her seat, closes her eyes, and lets herself welcome a brief reprieve.

Almost an hour later, Rio’s eyes crack open again, and she groggily takes in her surroundings. 

They’re definitely far from the airport, she realizes, scanning the passing buildings. Still, she’s not so out of it to miss that this isn’t the way to her apartment. Where the hell is Jen taking her?

“I hate to complain, since I’m basically getting a free ride, but this doesn’t exactly look like the right way to my place. Are you sure you’re following the route I sent?”

“Who said we were going there?”

“We’re not? But…didn’t you ask for my address?”

“You gave it to me, dummy. I never actually asked.”

Right, it had been Rio who sent the link herself before dozing off.

“Okay,” Rio drags the word. “So, where exactly are we going? I don’t mean to freak out, but I’ve only got a few hours to get ready for that gala Agatha invited me to, and I haven’t even figured out what to wear. Not to mention, I haven’t showered since the flight, and my hair…well, let’s just say it’s not looking its best.” She also sniffs it cautiously. “Or smelling its best, either.”

“Can you stop whining? Your voice is frying my ears. And sit your butt down, we’re nearly there.”
