“Nearly where?”

Shortly after, the car stops in front of a row of two-story brownstones. They’re not the flashy, over-the-top kind from the ritzy parts of town, but they look very decent and well-kept. 

Still, Rio is as confused as a black cat in a dog park. What the hell are they even doing here?

Rio asks again, “Where on earth are we?”

“My place,” Jen answers dryly, reaching for her purse in the backseat.

The storm last night had pushed her into building it, and yes, despite Agatha insisting they should have just stayed on the bed, they had spent the entire night christening the fort in ways that still leave her cheeks flushed just thinking about it.

Well, at least the rain had finally stopped, just in time and perfectly in favor of what is about to go down in the streets today. Really, if the world hates the gays, then why the hell do the gays keep winning?

She carefully turns her head and finds Agatha still fast asleep, half-curled on top of her, palm pressed against her sternum, one leg draped over hers, effectively trapping Rio like a sun-warmed cat that refuses to move.

Some of her muscles, ones she didn’t even know she had, are starting to complain, and her arm is numb under her girlfriend’s neck, but she doesn’t care. There is no other way she would rather wake up than wrapped around Agatha, exactly like this.

Looking at Agatha, Rio can’t help but marvel at how the hell they ended up here, how quickly time has slipped by since that single turning point.

One harmless lie, one unexpected encounter at Pride, and somehow every road since has curved toward this sweet piece of their life that still feels so unreal.

Most days the house smelled of garlic and rosemary. Rio at the stove or the oven, Agatha leaning against the counter with a spoon in hand, tasting, learning, stubbornly trying to match Rio’s skill so she could cook when Rio disappeared into her writing. 

It hadn’t taken long for their days to settle into an easy rhythm — Agatha taking calls while Rio typed on her laptop, both pausing now and then for quick kisses over steaming coffee. 

Sunny Saturdays had often meant Marmee’s backyard, Fanny trotting after them through the garden.

Rainy Sundays had stayed slow and soft, the two of them wrapped in blankets, each with a different book until one had started to read aloud, or until the books had slipped aside and the rest of the day had been spent with Rio’s head buried between Agatha’s thighs or Agatha’s fingers coaxing moans from Rio, leaving them both craving more even hours later.

Career-wise, Rio can say they’re both thriving. 

Well, Agatha always had, but now she’s reaching even greater heights as a new shareholder at Stark Publishing while still running Nocturne, with record-breaking numbers climbing each day. 

Rio, meanwhile, has collected several awards for her writing and has just submitted another piece to her dream publication, set to be published this month, for those curious.

But no matter how high their careers had soared, Rio always loved coming home to Agatha’s townhouse, now overflowing with her own scattered plants, notebooks, and half finished coffee mugs. 

The house, which they both now simply called theirs, had grown alongside them: more greenery than ever, photographs tucked into frames on every surface, each one a small fragment of their life together. 

Rio’s favorite showed her sprawled on a sunbed with a book, Agatha curled on top of her, asleep — a snapshot from their week in Sicily, courtesy of Lilia. 

While Agatha’s favorite captured Rio grinning from ear to ear, with Agatha holding a horrendous-looking but somehow delicious cake in front of her, Marmee and Lorna on either side, while the photo was snapped by Alice, who had also introduced Jen to her mom that same day.

And now, after nearly two years of keeping their love mostly to themselves, they were finally going to Pride openly, side by side for the world to see. 

Just days earlier, Agatha had stood on the steps of the MET, facing the glare of cameras during a red carpet interview, and let everyone know she is in a devoted, loving relationship with a fearless, award-winning journalist (now a celebrated writer for Times Magazine) named Rio Vidal.

Rio still could hardly believe it, because now the world had finally caught up to what she had always known in her heart.

When Rio eventually makes a move to get up, Agatha presses her leg down harder and immediately slides her hand from the center of Rio’s chest to her waist, effectively pinning her in place. 

“No,” she says, her voice still rough with sleep. “Stay right here.”

Rio tucks a stray lock behind Agatha’s ear. 

“Baby, I was only getting up to make us coffee.”

“I don’t need it.” Agatha tightens her hold without opening her eyes.

Rio laughs under her breath.

“Says the woman who downs at least three cups before noon.”

Agatha only nuzzles closer to her neck.

“I don’t know who that woman is. All I know is that five more minutes of this beats a whole pot of coffee.”

Rio smiles even though Agatha’s eyes stay shut. 

“Alright, my love, victory is yours, as always.”

“I do like it when you say that.” Agatha idly traces circles along Rio’s side, her voice still muffled against her neck. “Why are you even up so early? I thought we still had—” her eyes stay shut “—how many hours do we have, my love?”

Rio peeks out from their pillow fort at the clock. 

“About four and a half.”

“Which clearly proves my point,” Agatha replies, snuggling even closer.

Rio trails a hand down her girlfriend’s spine. “But we still need to get the guest room ready. Billy and Eddie are coming over, remember? You promised them they could crash here tonight after the parade.”

“I did?” Agatha lets out a low grumble. “And why exactly did I agree to that again?”

“Because you, my love, also told them we’d pick them up from that Pride party they’re dying to go to with their friends. And that all started with you—” Rio presses a kiss to Agatha’s shoulder “—being a total pushover who melted at Billy’s sob story about never having been to a fancy party in this part of town.” 

Agatha nuzzles deeper into Rio’s neck. “No, I didn’t fall for his sob story. I simply assumed they’d end up at the party anyway. Better he spends the night here than passed out on some random curb.”

Rio smiles, knowing Agatha has come to care for Billy just like she and Alice have. “Just admit it, that kid got to you too. Though I don’t blame you. I don’t know how he does it, but he does have a way of getting through even the meanest of lesbians.”

Agatha hums. “Well, I suppose the teen’s got a certain charm—” Then, catching the other words Rio said, she finally opens her eyes and raises her head to meet her girlfriend. “—wait, did you just call me the meanest of lesbians?”

Rio laughs and can’t help but reach for her girlfriend’s furrowed brows. 

“No, no, my love. I said prettiest. I believe you’re far too beautiful to be the meanest.”

“I know that,” Agatha huffs, burying her head back in Rio’s neck. “And you smell the sweetest, it’s distracting.”

“Well, as much as I’d love to stay here and keep you distracted,” Rio says, nuzzling Agatha’s hair, “we really should start on the guest room.” That earns a muffled, irritated grumble. “And my back is starting to kill me,” Rio adds, adjusting herself atop the blanket pile sprawled across the hardwood floor.

“I thought someone your age was meant to have sturdier muscles,” Agatha teases, shifting her leg slightly to put less weight on Rio. “And I did suggest we move back to the bed last night. But no, you insisted we stay here. I don’t get what it is with you and hardwood floors.”

Rio laughs again, pressing their bodies closer. “I don’t have a thing with hardwood floors. I wanted us to stay here because the fort only keeps the storm out if we’re actually inside it. That’s literally why it’s called a fort, my love.”

“Well, I never needed a fort,” Agatha whispers, lifting her head to meet Rio’s eyes. “Because I know no storm could touch me with you here. You’re more than everything I need.”

Rio can’t stop smiling. “You really mean that?”

“With all my heart, my love.” 

Rio blushes but doesn’t hide it. “Wow, you must really be in love with me or something.”

Agatha shrugs. “I guess I am…doesn’t exactly do my reputation any favors, though.”

Rio chuckles, and Agatha mirrors it with a much more meaningful smile, those luminous blue eyes just locked on her.

Then, more seriously, Rio repeats, “You really are in love with me, aren’t you?”

Aligning herself along Rio’s body, Agatha cups her cheek and presses a gentle kiss to Rio’s nose. 

“Yes, my dearest darling Rio. I’m hopelessly, ridiculously in love with you.” She then places a much more heartfelt kiss on her lips, her eyes glistening almost immediately. “I mean, how could I not be? I simply fucking love you.”

Later, walking hand in hand through the streets of New York, the city alive with color and music, Agatha repeats the same words amid a sea of cheering faces and smiling strangers around them.

The world might have seen them publicly for the first time, but Rio had always known.

Every cheer, every colorful flag, every shout of love from the crowd felt as if it were meant just for them, a perfect reflection of the life they had built, now celebrated by everyone else.

And everything began with one simple heartbeat.

She Stands Taller Than the World and I Fell for Every Inch

By Rio Vidal / Times Magazine

The first time I met Agatha Harkness, she regarded me like an intruder who had unwittingly wandered into her impenetrable fortress. And in many ways, I had. I had shown up in a wrinkled thrift-store blazer, ripped denim, a faded graphic tee, and the unearned confidence that only comes from wanting a job at a renowned magazine I barely understood. One I’d been told a million other girls would kill for. 

Agatha, by contrast, carried herself with an authority that felt innate, a woman with steel in her spine and command in her presence. It was only natural that she would look at me and question how I had managed to slip past her gates.

On paper, she is the editor-in-chief who transformed a middling publication into a cultural barometer in a matter of years. In practice, she is more complex than her reputation suggests, more exacting than her rivals give her credit for, and, though she would deny it, infinitely more human than most assume.

Because behind the glass walls of her office, beneath the mythology that has grown around her, Agatha Harkness is something else entirely. 

To write about her is to confront a conundrum. 

She has been called intimidating, brilliant, difficult, visionary. And she is all of these things. Yet the other truth is that she is also vulnerable in ways the world is too impatient to notice. 

To appreciate her work is to embrace her contradictions: a ruthlessness tempered by aching tenderness, a need for control that conceals a deep vulnerability. It would be easy to mistake her armor for her entirety, but that would be like calling a cathedral simply a building.

This is where the article should end in professionalism. But it is said that objectivity fractures in the face of honesty, and I have always believed that a great profile is built on revelation. Mine is simple: Agatha Harkness carries a devastating softness she will never ever admit. 

She has the most disarming smile when, at last, she lets her guard down. She also cares in ways she would never acknowledge—the way she tucks your hair behind your ear when your hands are full, drapes a blanket over your shoulders while you’re writing late at night, or presses a coffee into your hand, knowing you haven’t slept for hours. 

Sometimes, I catch her on her tallest tiptoes, in the way she rises to meet the demands of the world. And yet, even at her peak, there’s a fragility beneath the reach. A reminder that the highest of heights often demand the most courage. Watching her there, I understand why she seems untouchable, and why anyone who truly sees her is inescapably, irrevocably moved.

It fills me with pride to share this side of her with all of you, especially in a time like this, when we celebrate who we love and who we are. But I also know I’m breaking one of her cardinal rules, “Don’t romanticize me,” she once said before she agreed to this feature. 

However, this isn’t romanticizing. This is simply me showing the world what I see. Especially after I’ve watched her wrestle with her own heart in silence, isolated in the in-between, haunted by the fear of wanting love in a world that has punished her for who she chooses to love.

I’ve seen her strength and vulnerability coexist in ways few ever get to witness, and I feel compelled to make that visible, to let people understand that behind the armor is a woman who deserves to be seen, understood, and adored exactly as she is.

Agatha would tell me to cut most of this section. She would remind me that a magazine feature is not the place for confession. Surely, she would hate this piece, accuse me of overindulging, of smuggling sentiment where objectivity should be. 

And perhaps she’s right. But then again, journalism, at its best, is about truth. 

And the truth is this:

I have never loved anyone the way I love Agatha.

And perhaps that is the most important story I’ll ever write…

Chapter End Notes

like any of the other work under this pseudo, i didn’t expect this to get so much love, and wow…i didn’t think it would take me this long to finish either lmao. what started as a silly premise somehow turned into a complete rollercoaster of a story, with THIS agatha and rio taking up way too much space in my brain for the past four months. i poured every word i had into this, battled imposter syndrome the whole way, and now my brain is officially fried. but please know, im really grateful to everyone who sent love, shared their thoughts, and stuck with me all the way through this. i fucking love you all :))
